Repeating Bequests: Sixth Then Third or Sixth Then Sixth
Rules for successive bequests of fractions to the same person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for interpreting successive bequests of definite fractions to the same person and apply it to determine the legatee's total share.

Core Idea
When a testator repeats a definite fraction bequest, Hanafi law gives only one share; when a larger fraction follows a smaller, the larger includes the smaller.

In this passage, al-Haskafi (the commentator) explains two key scenarios from Al-Hidayah about consecutive bequests to the same person. The linguistic principle that a repeated definite noun refers to the same entity is applied to fractions. Understanding this helps us correctly allocate the estate when a testator makes multiple statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two explicit scenarios
The text presents two cases: (a) testator says 'one-sixth … then one-third'; (b) testator says 'one-sixth … then one-sixth'. Both bequests are to the same person.
The first case involves different fractions; the second involves identical ones.
2
Apply the linguistic rule of repeated definites
In Arabic, when a definite noun (e.g., 'the sixth') is repeated as definite (again 'the sixth'), the second refers to the same entity as the first. This is derived from the Quranic verse 'Indeed, with hardship [will be] ease. Indeed, with hardship [will be] ease' – two 'eases' refer to the same ease.
This rule is used by Hanafis unless there is evidence of a separate intended bequest.
3
Determine the share in the sixth-then-third case
The later one-third includes the earlier one-sixth because one-third is a larger fraction that encompasses one-sixth. The legatee receives only one-third total, not one-sixth plus one-third.
This is because the testator's intent is understood to be cumulative but not exceeding the larger.
4
Determine the share in the sixth-then-sixth case
Since the same definite 'the sixth' is repeated, the second refers to the same sixth. The legatee receives only one-sixth, not two-sixths (one-third).
This holds whether the testator spoke in one session or two.
5
Analyze the ambiguous third-then-sixth case from Al-Hidayah
If testator says 'one-third … then one-sixth', the sixth may be an addition or just a repetition. The certain amount is one-third (since the third could include the sixth). Hanafis give the certain third.
Some later scholars argued that the third is certain from both probabilities, so the bequest is for one-third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (قال) سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال ثلث مالي له له ثلث ماله لأن الثلث متضمن للسدس فيدخل فيه فلا يتناول أكثر من الثلث . قال رحمه الله : (وإن قال سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال سدس مالي له له السدس) يعني واحداً سواء قال ذلك في مجلس واحد أو في مجلسين لأن السدس ذكر معرفاً بالإضافة إلى المال والمعرف إذا أعيد معرفاً كان الثاني عين الأول وهكذا قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما في قوله تعالى فإن مع العسر يسرا إن مع العسر يسرا [الشرح: ٥-٦] لن يغلب عسر يسرين وفي الهداية ولو قال ثلث مالي لفلان وسدس مالي له وأجازت الورثة فله ثلث المال ويدخل السدس فيه لأن الكلام الثاني يحتمل أنه أراد به زيادة الثلث على الأول حتى يتم السدس، ويحتمل أنه أراد به إيجاب ثلث على السدس حتى يصير المجموع نصفاً الاحتمال لا يثبت له إلا القدر المتيقن فيجعل السدس داخلاً في السدس حملاً لكلامه على المتيقن ؛ هذا هو المذكور في الشروح. قال بعض المتأخرين بعد ذكر الدليل على هذا المنوال : هكذا قالوا وهذا كما ترى حمل الكلام على أحد محتمليه ولك أن تقول : لما كان الكلام محتملاً للمعنيين وكان القدر الثابت به يتعين على الاحتمالين الثلث قلنا ما يثبت به من الوصية لأن المتيقن ثبوت الثلث بمجموع الاحتمالين لا بأولهما ؛ إلى هنا كلامه.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (He said: one-sixth of my property to so-and-so, then he said: one-third of my property to him, so he gets one-third of his property) because one-third encompasses one-sixth, so it enters into it and it does not take more than one-third. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he said: one-sixth of my property to so-and-so, then he said: one-sixth of my property to him, so he gets one-sixth) meaning one, whether he said that in one sitting or in two sittings, because one-sixth is mentioned as definite by addition to property, and when a definite is repeated as definite, the second is the same as the first. Thus Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, said regarding the verse of Allah: 'For indeed, with hardship [will be] ease. Indeed, with hardship [will be] ease' (94:5-6): one hardship will not overcome two eases. And in al-Hidayah: if he said: one-third of my property to so-and-so and one-sixth of my property to him, and the heirs allowed, then he gets one-third of the property and the sixth enters into it, because the second statement could mean he intended to increase the third over the first until the sixth is completed, or it could mean he intended to add a third to the sixth so that the total becomes half. Probability does not establish for him except the certain amount, so the sixth is made part of the third, based on interpreting his speech according to the certain. This is what is mentioned in the commentaries. Some later scholars said after mentioning the proof in this manner: thus they said, and this is, as you see, interpreting the speech according to one of its probabilities. But you could say: since the speech is probable for the two meanings, and the amount established by it is definitively the third according to both probabilities, we say that what is established of the bequest is the third, because the certain is the establishment of the third by the sum of the two probabilities, not by the first alone. Up to here his words.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage addresses when a testator makes two successive bequests to the same person. The first case: he says 'one-sixth' then later 'one-third'. The later bequest (one-third) includes the earlier (one-sixth) because one-third encompasses one-sixth, so the legatee gets one-third total. The second case: he says 'one-sixth' twice. Since the same definite noun is repeated with the same definition, it refers to the same one-sixth, so only one-sixth is given. The commentary then discusses a variation: if he says 'one-third' then 'one-sixth', the sixth is included in the third because of uncertainty—the testator might have meant to add a sixth to the third (making half) or to include it. The certain amount is one-third, so the sixth is taken as part of it. A later scholar notes that the certain amount is one-third under both interpretations, so the bequest is for one-third.

Key Terms
المعرف (al-mu'arraf): A definite noun (like 'the sixth of my property'); when repeated as definite, it refers to the same entity.
المتيقن (al-mutayaqqan): The certain amount that is established from ambiguous speech; here one-third is certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One-sixth.
B) One-third.
C) One-half.
D) One-ninth.

Key Takeaway
When a definite fraction is repeated identically, Hanafi law treats it as the same share; when a larger definite fraction follows a smaller one, the larger includes the smaller, giving only the larger.

Repeating the Same Bequest: Only One Sixth
Clarifying that repeating a bequest of the same fraction grants only one share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeated bequests of the same fraction and apply the linguistic principle that a repeated definite noun refers to the same entity.

Core Idea
Repeating a definite bequest of the same fraction does not create a second share.

When a testator makes a bequest and then repeats the same fraction for the same beneficiary, does the beneficiary receive the amount twice? The Hanafi school answers no: the second utterance is legally redundant. This lesson unpacks the linguistic principle behind this ruling and explores a related case where the fractions differ, introducing an internal scholarly debate on how to interpret ambiguous language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific legal act: a testator says 'One sixth of my wealth is for X' and then later repeats 'One sixth of my wealth is for X.' The ruling is that X receives only one sixth.
The ruling applies whether the two statements are in one gathering or separate gatherings.
2
Locate the linguistic principle (dalil)
The proof is the principle that when a definite noun (mu'arraf) is repeated as definite, the second occurrence refers to the same entity as the first. This is supported by Ibn Abbas's interpretation of Quran 94:5-6: the repetition of 'ease' does not create two eases.
The principle is grammatical and has legal consequences in testamentary interpretation.
3
Examine the Hidayah case: third and sixth
Consider the variant where the testator says 'One third for X and one sixth for X.' Here the second statement is ambiguous: it could be an addition to the first or a separate bequest. The certain amount is one third, so the sixth is included in the third.
This shows the operation of the 'certain amount' principle (muta'ayyin) when ambiguity exists.
4
Analyze the later scholar's critique
A later Hanafi scholar argues that in the third-and-sixth case, the certain amount from both possibilities is actually one third, not the inclusion of the sixth into the third. This critique highlights the tension between probability and certainty in interpreting the testator's words.
The original ruling remains the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), but the critique is noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن قال سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال سدس مالي له له السدس) يعني واحداً سواء قال ذلك في مجلس واحد أو في مجلسين لأن السدس ذكر معرفاً بالإضافة إلى المال والمعرف إذا أعيد معرفاً كان الثاني عين الأول وهكذا قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما في قوله تعالى فإن مع العسر يسرا إن مع العسر يسرا لن يغلب عسر يسرين وفي الهداية ولو قال ثلث مالي لفلان وسدس مالي له وأجازت الورثة فله ثلث المال ويدخل السدس فيه لأن الكلام الثاني يحتمل أنه أراد به زيادة الثلث على الأول حتى يتم السدس، ويحتمل أنه أراد به إيجاب ثلث على السدس حتى يصير المجموع نصفاً الاحتمال لا يثبت له إلا القدر المتيقن فيجعل السدس داخلاً في السدس حملاً لكلامه على المتيقن ؛ هذا هو المذكور في الشروح. قال بعض المتأخرين بعد ذكر الدليل على هذا المنوال : هكذا قالوا وهذا كما ترى حمل الكلام على أحد محتمليه ولك أن تقول : لما كان الكلام محتملاً للمعنيين وكان القدر الثابت به يتعين على الاحتمالين الثلث قلنا ما يثبت به من الوصية لأن المتيقن ثبوت الثلث بمجموع الاحتمالين لا بأولهما ؛ إلى هنا كلامه.
He said: (And if he said: 'One sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then said: 'One sixth of my wealth is for him,' then he has one sixth.) Meaning one, whether he said that in one gathering or in two, because 'the sixth' is mentioned definite by addition to wealth, and when a definite is repeated as definite, the second is the same as the first. Thus Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said regarding the Almighty's saying: 'For indeed with hardship there is ease. Indeed, with hardship there is ease' – hardship will not be overcome by two eases. And in al-Hidayah: If he said: 'One third of my wealth for so-and-so and one sixth of my wealth for him,' and the heirs consented, then he gets one third of the wealth and the sixth is included in it, because the second statement possibly means that he intended to add the third to the first until the sixth is completed, and possibly means that he intended to make a third over the sixth so that the total becomes half. Probability does not establish anything except the certain amount, so the sixth is included in the third, carrying his speech to the certain; this is what is mentioned in the commentaries. Some later scholars said after mentioning the proof in this manner: Thus they said, and this, as you see, is carrying the speech to one of its possibilities. But you could say: Since the speech is possible for both meanings, and the amount established by it is determined for both possibilities as one third, we say that what is established by it from the bequest is because the certain establishment of one third by the sum of the two possibilities, not by the first of them; up to here his speech.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Hidayah, explained in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author addresses the case where a testator repeats a bequest of the same fraction, here one sixth. The key principle is that when a definite noun (المعرف) is repeated as definite, the second occurrence refers to the same entity as the first, not to a new one. This is a grammatical principle with legal effect. The author supports this with an analogy from Ibn Abbas's interpretation of Quran 94:5-6: the repetition of 'ease' does not create two eases; hardship remains one. Similarly, repeating 'one sixth' does not create two sixths. The passage then notes an alternative case from al-Hidayah: if the testator says 'one third for X and one sixth for X', the second is ambiguous – it could be an addition or a separate bequest. Since only the certain amount (the third) is taken, the sixth is considered included in the third unless the heirs consent to more. A later scholar critiques this by arguing that the certain amount is actually one third from both interpretations, so the bequest should be one third, not the sixth included. This is a subtle point about probability and certainty in interpreting a testator's words.

Key Terms
السدس (al-sudus): One sixth of the estate, a fractional share in bequests.
معرف (mu'arraf): A definite noun, here defined by addition (الإضافة) to wealth.

Bequest of One Third of a Specific Type When Two Thirds Perish: Abu Hanifa vs Zafar
Ruling on a bequest of one third of a specific type when two thirds perish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of priority in bequests to determine the legatee's share when a specific type of bequest is partially destroyed, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and Zafar's positions.

Core Idea
In a restricted bequest, the legatee's priority over inheritance means perished property is charged to the heirs, not shared proportionally.

When a testator bequeaths one third of a specific type of property (e.g., his dirhams or sheep) and then two thirds of that type perish before distribution, a dispute arises: does the legatee take all that remains of that type, or only one third of what remains? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling and the intra-school disagreement with Zafar, focusing on the principles of priority and the analogy to fixed-item bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the Case
Identify the facts: a testator bequeaths one third of a specific type of property (e.g., dirhams or sheep). Two thirds of that type perish before the bequest is executed. The question is what the legatee receives.
2
Identify the Hanafi Position (Abu Hanifa)
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa), the legatee takes all that remains of that type, provided it does not exceed one third of the total remaining estate. The loss is borne by the heirs.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Recognize Zafar's Opposing View
Zafar argues that the legatee should receive only one third of what remains of that type, treating the relationship as a partnership where loss is shared proportionally.
Zafar is a prominent Hanafi scholar, so this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
The Hanafi response relies on two arguments: (1) the legatee's right is prioritized over inheritance (Quran 4:12), so destruction is attributed to the later right (heirs), not the earlier right (legatee). (2) Analogy to bequests of a fixed number of items (e.g., ten dirhams): if the specified items survive, the legatee takes them entirely. Loss is not shared when rights are not equal.
5
Determine the Practical Difference
Compute the difference: if the original property had 300 sheep, 200 perish, 100 remain. Under Abu Hanifa, the legatee takes all 100 (subject to the one-third limit of total estate). Under Zafar, he takes one third of 100 ≈ 33. (The one-third limit may further reduce both.)
This thamarah al-khilaf is the concrete outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أوصى بثلث دراهمه أو غنمه وهلك ثلثاه له ما بقي أي إذا وصى بثلث دراهمه أو بثلث غنمه وهلك ثلثا ذلك ثلثه وبقي وهو يخرج من ثلث ما بقي من ماله فله جميع ما بقي من الدراهم والغنم . وقال زفر : له ثلث ما بقي من ذلك النوع لأن كل واحد منهما شركة بينهما والمال المشترك يهلك ما هلك منه على الشركة ويبقى الباقي كذلك فصار كما إذا أوصى به أجناساً مختلفة. ولنا أن حق بعضهم يمكن جمعه في البعض الباقي فصار كما إذا أوصى بدرهم أو بعشرة دراهم أو بعشرة رؤوس من الغنم فهلك ذلك الجنس كله إلا القدر المسمى فإنه يأخذه إذا كان يخرج من ثلث بقية ماله بخلاف الأجناس المختلفة فإنه لا يمكن الجمع فيها جبراً فكذا تقديما، والمال المشترك إنما يهلك الهالك منه على الشركة أن لو استوى الحقان، أما إذا كان أحدهما مقدماً على الآخر فالهالك يصرف إلى المؤخر كما إذا كان في التركة ديون ووصايا وورثة ثم هلك بعض التركة فإن الهالك يصرف إلى المؤخر وهو الوصية والإرث لأن الدين مقدم عليهما، وهنا الوصية مقدمة على الإرث لقوله تعالى من بعد وصية يوصى بها أو دين [النساء : ١٢] فيصرف الهلاك إلى الإرث تقديماً للوصية على وجه لا ينقص حق الورثة على الثلثين مع جميع التركة لأنه لا يسلم للموصى له شيء حتى يسلم للورثة ضعف ذلك. وكذا إذا هلك البعض في المضاربة يصرف الهلاك للربح لأن رأس المال مقدم على ما عرف في موضعه الأصل في هذا الباب أن يحتاج إلى معرفة الوصية المقيدة والمطلقة والعين والدين كما سبكه المؤلف وأنواع الوصية بهما وأحكامها.
And if he bequeaths one third of his dirhams or his sheep and two thirds of that perish, then he gets what remains. That is, if he bequeaths one third of his dirhams or one third of his sheep and two thirds of that perish, one third remains, and it comes out of one third of what remains of his wealth, so he gets all that remains of the dirhams and sheep. Zafar said: He gets one third of what remains of that type, because each one of them is a partnership between them, and joint property: what perishes perishes according to the partnership, and what remains remains likewise, so it becomes like if he bequeathed different types. Our evidence is that the right of one of them can be collected in the remaining part, so it becomes like when he bequeaths a dirham or ten dirhams or ten heads of sheep and that whole type perishes except the specified amount; then he takes it if it comes out of one third of the rest of his wealth, unlike different types where collection is not possible by force, so too in priority. Joint property only perishes according to partnership if the two rights are equal; but if one is prioritized over the other, then the perished is attributed to the delayed one, as when the estate contains debts, bequests, and heirs, then some of the estate perishes: the perished is attributed to the delayed one, namely the bequest and inheritance, because the debt is prioritized over both. Here, the bequest is prioritized over inheritance by the Almighty's saying: 'After a bequest which he bequeaths or a debt' (4:12). So the perished is attributed to the inheritance, giving priority to the bequest in a way that does not reduce the heirs' right to two thirds of the entire estate, because nothing is delivered to the legatee until the heirs receive double of it. Similarly, if something perishes in a mudarabah, the perished is attributed to the profit because capital is prioritized, as is known in its place. The principle in this chapter is that one needs knowledge of restricted and unrestricted bequests, of 'ayn and dayn, as the author has laid out, and the types of bequests with them and their rulings.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa's view (as transmitted by the author) and Zafar's opinion. The case: a testator bequeaths one third of a specific type of property (e.g., his dirhams or his sheep), but two thirds of that type perish before the bequest is executed. According to Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi position in al-Hidayah, the legatee takes all that remains of that type (i.e., the surviving third), provided it does not exceed one third of the total remaining estate. The loss is borne by the heirs, not the legatee, because the legatee's right is prioritized over inheritance. Zafar argues that the legatee should only get one third of what remains, treating the relationship as a partnership where loss is shared proportionally. The Hanafi response uses qiyas: when the legatee's right is limited to a specific type, his right can be 'collected' in the surviving part, similar to bequeathing a fixed number of items (e.g., ten dirhams) where the legatee takes those specific items if they still exist. The priority of bequest over inheritance is supported by Quran 4:12, so destruction is attributed to the heirs (the later right). This principle is analogous to debt being prioritized over bequests and inheritance in case of loss.

Key Terms
الوصية المقيدة (al-wasiyyah al-muqayyadah): A bequest restricted to a specific type of property, as opposed to a general share of the entire estate.
الشركة (al-shirkah): Partnership; here used in the context of sharing loss proportionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths one third of his sheep, but two thirds of the sheep die before the bequest is executed. The remaining estate (other property) is sufficient to cover one third of the total. How many sheep does the legatee take?
A) All remaining sheep
B) One third of the remaining sheep
C) Two thirds of the remaining sheep
D) None, because the bequest fails

Key Takeaway
In a restricted bequest, the legatee's priority over inheritance shifts the burden of destruction to the heirs, so the legatee takes all remaining of the specified type, subject to the one-third limit of the total estate.

Definition of 'Ayn and 'Urud in Wills
Defining the legal terms 'ayn and 'urud for wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'ayn (specie) and 'urud (goods) as used in Hanafi law of wills, and classify property accordingly.

Core Idea
'Ayn means only minted gold and silver coins; all else is 'urud.

In Hanafi law, the terms 'ayn and 'urud have specific technical meanings that affect the interpretation of a will. A bequest limited to 'ayn gives only minted gold and silver coins, while everything else—including unminted precious metals, jewellery, clothing, and debts—falls under 'urud. This distinction ensures certainty in the testator's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definitions
Read the text to find how 'ayn and 'urud are explicitly defined. Note that 'ayn is confined to minted gold/silver coins, and 'urud includes all other movable property.
The text lists items like gold nuggets, jewellery, and goods as 'urud.
2
Contrast with common usage
Recognize that in everyday language, 'ayn might refer to any physical asset, but legally it is restricted. Understand the rationale: to avoid ambiguity in bequests.
3
Apply to a classification exercise
Given a list of assets, determine which are 'ayn and which are 'urud based on the definition. Check for minted status.
Minted coins (gold or silver) are 'ayn; everything else is 'urud, even if made of precious metal.
4
Understand the legal effect
If a testator bequeaths 'ayn, only minted coins are transferred. If the testator used the term ambiguously, the will may fail.
The definition prevents disputes over the testator's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دون التبر والحلي والعروض والثياب الدين كل شيء يكون واجباً في الذمة من ذهب أو فضة أو حنطة ونحو ذلك لأن العين عند الإطلاق ينصرف للذهب والفضة المضروبين : وأما غيرهما فيسمى في اللغة عروضاً وسلعة وحلياً وصياغة .
Excluding gold nuggets, jewellery, goods, and clothes, debts: everything that is a liability in the dhimma (financial obligation) from gold, silver, wheat and the like, because the term 'ayn (specie) when unqualified refers specifically to minted gold and silver. As for other than these, they are called in the language 'goods' (urud), 'commodities' (silah), 'jewellery' (huli) and 'manufactured items' (siyaghah).
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the legal distinction between 'ayn (specie) and 'urud (goods) in the context of wills. The author clarifies that when the term 'ayn is used absolutely in a will, it refers only to minted gold and silver coins (nuqud). This is important because a will can be made specifically to a type of property. Other items like clothing, livestock, jewellery, and even gold in an unminted state are classified as 'urud. The term 'dayn' (debt) is also excluded from 'ayn, as it is a liability. This classification affects the ruling of a will restricted (muqayyada) to a specific type.

Key Terms
العين (al-‘ayn): In this text, refers specifically to minted gold and silver coins when used absolutely in a will.
العروض (al-‘urūḍ): Everything other than coined gold and silver, including goods, clothes, livestock, jewellery, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All forms of gold and silver, including nuggets and jewellery
B) Only minted gold and silver coins
C) Any property that is physically present
D) Debts owed to the deceased

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law of wills, 'ayn is strictly minted gold and silver coins; all other property is 'urud.

Types of Wills: Mursalah and Muqayyadah
Defining mursalah and muqayyadah with legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a restricted (muqayyadah) and unrestricted (mursalah) will, and state the legal consequences of each regarding loss and precedence over heirs.

Core Idea
A restricted will ties the legatee's right to specific property, giving priority over heirs; an unrestricted will shares gains and losses proportionally.

When a person makes a will, the way they phrase it determines how the bequest interacts with the rest of the estate. The Hanafi school classifies wills into two types: unrestricted (mursalah), which gives a common share of the entire estate, and restricted (muqayyadah), which specifies a particular type of property. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper estate distribution, especially when losses occur before division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the first part of the passage where the author defines mursalah (unrestricted) as bequeathing a common share like 'one-third of my wealth', and muqayyadah (restricted) as bequeathing a share of specific property like 'one-third of my dirhams'.
Note the Arabic terms used: جز شائع (common share) for mursalah, and بجزء من مال بعينه (part of specific property) for muqayyadah.
2
Understand the legal effect of restricted will
The passage states that the restricted legatee's right is 'muqaddam' (advanced/precedential) over heirs and unrestricted legatees. If the specified property is lost before division, the loss falls on the heirs, not the legatee. The basis is Quran 4:12 'after any bequest...' which prioritizes bequests.
The text says: 'لو هلك شيء منها قبل القسمة يصرف الهلاك إلى الورثة لا إلى الموصى له' (if something of it is lost before division, the loss is attributed to the heirs, not the legatee).
3
Understand the legal effect of unrestricted will
The unrestricted legatee is treated like an heir (بمنزلة واحد من الورثة). His right is established as a common share in all the estate, so he shares proportionally in gains and losses. The estate becomes joint ownership between him and the heirs.
The text says: 'فصارت التركة كالمشتركة بينه وبين الورثة' (the estate becomes jointly owned between him and the heirs).
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario, determine which type of will is in effect and how loss is allocated. For example, if a testator bequeaths 'one-third of my camels' (restricted) and the camels die, the legatee receives nothing from other assets. If he bequeaths 'one-third of my estate' (unrestricted), the legatee shares the loss proportionally.
The key difference is that in a restricted will, the legatee's right is tied to the specific asset; in an unrestricted will, it is tied to the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أنواع الوصية بهما فالوصية نوعان مرسلة ومقيدة. فالمرسلة أن يوصي بجزء شائع من ماله نحو يوصي بثلث ماله وربعه، والمقيدة أن يوصي بثلث مال بعينه بأن يوصي بثلث دراهمه أو دنانيره أو بثلث الغنم فالوصية المقيدة حكمها أن يكون حقه مقدماً على حق الورثة وعلى حق الوصية المرسلة، ولو هلك شيء منها قبل القسمة يصرف الهلاك إلى الورثة لا إلى الموصى له حيث كانت الوصايا تخرج من ثلث مال الميت بأن كان له مال آخر يعطى للموصى له كل الموصى به لأنه قيدها بنوع من المال فتقيد بذلك النوع ولهذا لا يزداد حقه بزيادة مال الميت وكذا لا ينقص بنقصانه لأن حقه لم يثبت شائعاً في جميع التركة فكان حقه مقدماً على حق الورثة لقوله تعالى من بعد وصية يوصى بها أو دين﴾ حقاً فصار الهلاك مصروفاً إلى المؤخر حقه لا إلى المقدم لأنه ما لم يفضل عن الوصية لا يصير للورثة وإنما حكم الوصية المرسلة فهو أن صاحبها بمنزلة واحد من الورثة لأن حقه ثبت شائعاً في جميع التركة حتى يزاد حقه بزيادة المال وينقص بنقصانه كحق الورثة فصارت التركة كالمشتركة بينه وبين الورثة فما توى من شيء من التركة يتوى على الشركة، وما بقي يبقى على الشركة فكان وراثاً حكماً ومعنى وموصى له اسماً والعبرة للحكم والمعنى
As for the types of will with them [i.e., property types], the will is of two types: unrestricted (mursalah) and restricted (muqayyadah). The unrestricted is that one bequeaths a common share of his wealth, such as bequeathing a third or a quarter of his wealth. The restricted is that one bequeaths a third of specific wealth, such as bequeathing a third of his dirhams or dinars, or a third of the sheep. The ruling of the restricted will is that his right takes precedence over the right of the heirs and over the right of the unrestricted will. If something of it is lost before division, the loss is attributed to the heirs, not to the legatee, provided that the legacies come out of the third of the deceased's wealth, because he had other wealth from which the legatee is given all that was bequeathed, since he restricted it to a type of property, so it is restricted to that type. Therefore, his right does not increase with an increase in the deceased's wealth, nor does it decrease with its decrease, because his right was not established as a common share in all the estate. So his right takes precedence over the right of the heirs, due to the Almighty's saying: 'After any bequest they make or debt' [Quran 4:12] as a right. Thus, the loss is attributed to the one whose right is postponed, not to the one whose right is advanced, because as long as nothing remains beyond the bequest, nothing becomes for the heirs. As for the ruling of the unrestricted will, its owner is like one of the heirs, because his right is established as a common share in all the estate, so his right increases with an increase in wealth and decreases with its decrease, like the right of the heirs. Thus the estate becomes jointly owned between him and the heirs. So whatever is destroyed from the estate is destroyed according to the joint ownership, and whatever remains remains according to the joint ownership. So he is an heir in meaning and essence, and a legatee in name, and consideration is given to the ruling and meaning.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq categorizes wills into two types: restricted (muqayyada) and unrestricted (mursala). A restricted will specifies a particular type of property (e.g., 'one-third of my dirhams'), while an unrestricted will gives a share of the entire estate (e.g., 'one-third of my wealth'). The key legal difference is that in a restricted will, the legatee's right is tied to that specific type, so it takes precedence over both the heirs and an unrestricted legatee. If the specified property is damaged, the loss falls on the heirs, not the legatee, because the legatee's right is 'advanced' (muqaddam) based on the Quranic verse (4:12). In contrast, an unrestricted legatee shares in the estate like an heir—gains and losses are proportional. The author emphasizes that the unrestricted legatee is treated as an heir in legal effect, even though called a legatee.

Key Terms
وصية مرسلة (waṣiyyah mursalah): A will that gives a common share (e.g., one-third) of the entire estate without specifying a particular type of property.
وصية مقيدة (waṣiyyah muqayyadah): A will that specifies a particular type of property (e.g., one-third of dirhams), giving the legatee priority over heirs and unrestricted legatees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The legatee
B) Heirs
C) Both proportionally
D) The state

Key Takeaway
The classification of wills into restricted and unrestricted determines priority and loss allocation in estate distribution.

Loss in Unrestricted Wills
Ruling with proof for unrestricted will loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that loss in an unrestricted will is shared proportionally between the legatee and the heirs.

Core Idea
An unrestricted will makes the legatee a partner; any loss is shared.

This passage explains how loss (halak) of property before distribution affects the legatee's share when the will is unrestricted. The legatee becomes like a co-owner in the entire estate, so any loss is shared proportionally.

Guided Path
1
Identify will type
Determine that the will is unrestricted: the testator bequeaths a fraction of his entire wealth without specifying a particular type of property (e.g., 'one-third of my wealth').
Key indicator: the bequest is added to general wealth (مال مطلق).
2
Recognize legatee's status
The legatee is treated like a partner (شريك) in the estate. He owns a proportional share of every asset from the moment of the testator's death.
This partnership analogy is unique to unrestricted wills in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply loss rule
If some property is lost or claimed by a third party, the loss is divided between the legatee and the heirs according to their respective shares in the estate.
Loss is shared (يهلك على الشركة).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما يتعلق بمسائل الهلاك والاستحقاق فلو أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله فما هلك أو استحق فهو على الحقين لأن الوصية مطلقة مرسلة لأنه أضاف الوصية إلى ماله على العموم والشيوع فيكون له ثلث كل شيء من ماله فكان شريكاً في التركة جميع بمنزلة أحد الورثة فما هلك يهلك على الشركة، فإن أوصى بثلث الدراهم وثلث الدنانير ثم هلك عشرون ديناراً بعد موت الموصى أو قبل موته كان له ثلث ما بقي نصفه من الدراهم ونصفه من الدنانير لأن هذه وصية مقدمة لأنه أوصى له بثلث دراهمه و دنانيره فقد قيد الوصية بنوع مال مخصوص ولم يضفها إلى مال مرسل فكانت وصية مقيدة فتعلق بذلك المال بقاء وبطلاناً. ولو كان أوصى بسدس الدراهم وسدس الدنانير أخذ السدس كله من الباقي لأن الهلاك مصروف إلى حق الورثة فيبقى حق الموصى له في سدس جميع المال وذلك خمسة دنانير كما كان قبل الهلاك فكان له خمسة دنانير من العشرة الباقية إذ أصله ثلاثون وخمسون درهماً من الدنانير وكذلك الإبل والبقر على هذا.
As for matters related to loss and entitlement: If someone bequeaths a third of his wealth to a man (unrestricted), then whatever is lost or claimed becomes according to both rights because the will is absolute and unrestricted, since he added the will to his wealth in a general and common manner. So he has a third of every item of his wealth, and he becomes a partner in the entire estate like one of the heirs; whatever is lost is lost according to the partnership. If he bequeaths one-third of the dirhams and one-third of the dinars, then twenty dinars are lost after the testator's death or before his death, the legatee has one-third of what remains, half from dirhams and half from dinars, because this is an advanced will since he bequeathed one-third of his dirhams and dinars, thus restricting the will to a specific type of property and not adding it to a general wealth; so it is a restricted will, attached to that property in existence and nullity. And if he had bequeathed one-sixth of the dirhams and one-sixth of the dinars, he takes the entire one-sixth from the remainder because the loss is attributed to the right of the heirs, so the legatee's right remains in one-sixth of all the wealth, which is five dinars, as it was before the loss; so he has five dinars from the remaining ten, since its origin is thirty, and fifty dirhams from the dinars. And likewise for camels and cows.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage provides concrete examples illustrating the rules for loss (halak) and entitlement (istihqaq) for both types of wills. For an unrestricted will (e.g., one-third of total wealth), the legatee is like a partner—any loss in the estate is shared proportionally. For a restricted will (e.g., one-third of dirhams and dinars), the legatee's right is fixed to that specific property type; if part of that property is lost, the legatee still receives his share from what remains, because the loss falls on the heirs. The example with one-sixth is similar: since the will is restricted to a specific type (dirhams and dinars), the loss is borne by the heirs, and the legatee gets his full one-sixth of what remains. The text also notes that this rule applies to property like camels and cows (i.e., specific types).

Key Terms
الهلاك (al-halāk): Loss or destruction of property before distribution.
الاستحقاق (al-istiḥqāq): Entitlement or claim, here referring to the legatee's right to the bequeathed property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an unrestricted will, if some of the estate is lost before distribution, how is the loss allocated?
A) The loss is borne entirely by the heirs
B) The loss is borne entirely by the legatee
C) The loss is shared proportionally between legatee and heirs
D) The loss is ignored and the legatee gets his full original share

Key Takeaway
In unrestricted wills, the legatee shares proportionally in any loss of the estate.

Loss in Restricted Wills
Ruling with proof for restricted will loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that loss in a restricted will falls solely on the heirs, preserving the legatee's share.

Core Idea
In a restricted will, the legatee's right is tied to a specific property class; loss is borne by heirs, not legatee.

This passage presents the rule for restricted wills: when the bequest is limited to a specific type of property (e.g., one-third of dinars), the legatee's share becomes fixed to that property. If some of that property is lost, the loss does not reduce the legatee's entitlement; instead, the heirs bear the loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify will type
Determine that the will is restricted: the testator bequeaths a fraction of a specific property type (e.g., 'one-third of my dirhams and dinars') rather than a fraction of total wealth.
Key indicator: the addition of the bequest to a specific type of مال (e.g., دراهم, دنانير).
2
Recognize legatee's fixed right
The legatee's entitlement is attached to that specific property class (تعلق بذلك المال بقاء وبطلاناً). His share does not increase or decrease due to loss of other property types.
The legatee's share in that class is determined as a fraction of the original amount of that class? Actually it's a fraction of the original class, but if part is lost, the legatee still gets that fraction of what remains.
3
Apply loss rule
If some of the specified property is lost, the loss is attributed to the right of the heirs (الهلاك مصروف إلى حق الورثة). The legatee receives his full fraction of the remaining property of that class.
Example: one-third of dinars; if 20 out of 30 dinars remain, legatee gets 1/3 of the remaining 20 = 6.67, not 1/3 of original 30 = 10.

Complex Case: Wills of Emancipation, One-Third, and One-Sixth
Calculating shares when multiple wills (including emancipation) coexist with loss and claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of bequests when emancipation and fractional bequests coexist, applying the Hanafi method of 'awl and mudarabah.

Core Idea
When multiple bequests involve the same slave but only one ties to his person, division is by proportional allocation, not contest.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed computational scenario where a testator bequeaths freedom to his slave, one-third of his estate to one person, and one-sixth of a specific cash amount to another. The estate includes both cash and the slave. The Hanafi jurists explain that since the unrestricted legatee's right attaches to the slave's earnings, not his person, no contest arises over the slave, allowing division by proportional adjustment. The calculations illustrate the method when bequests exceed the one-third limit and when partial loss or claim occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify estate and bequests
Note the total estate: 1000 cash + slave worth 1000 = 2000. Identify the three bequests: (1) freedom of slave (value 1000, half of estate), (2) unrestricted bequest of one-third of total wealth, (3) restricted bequest of one-sixth of cash (i.e., 1000/6 = 166.67, but the cash is only 1000, so the restricted bequest is from the cash).
The unrestricted bequest attaches to the entire estate, while the restricted bequest is tied to the cash specifically.
2
Determine the one-third limit
The bequests are limited to one-third of the estate: 1/3 of 2000 = 666.67. The total value of bequests is 1000 (slave) + 666.67 (third) + 166.67 (sixth) = 1833.33, which exceeds the third. Therefore, the third must be divided proportionally among the three legatees.
The slave's bequest is for freedom, valued at the slave's price.
3
Set up initial division base
The bequest shares are half (slave), third (unrestricted), and sixth (restricted). The least common multiple of denominators 2, 3, 6 is 12. Half = 6, third = 4, sixth = 2. Sum = 12, but the total of bequests relative to the third? Actually, the text gives a ratio of 6:4:1 for the third, meaning the total for the third is 11 parts. This is derived because the unrestricted third bequest is a fraction of the whole, not of the third itself. The step is complex: the third is divided among them in the ratio of their bequests, but adjusted because the unrestricted bequest is a share of the whole, not of the third. The text says the third is on 11: 6 for slave, 4 for third legatee, 1 for sixth legatee.
The method uses 'awl: the base is increased from 12 to 11 to accommodate the fractions within the third.
4
Scale up to full estate
Since the third equals 11 parts, the whole estate is 33 parts (11 * 3). The slave gets 6 parts from the third, which is 6/33 of the whole estate = 2/11? Actually, the slave gets 6/11 of the third, which is 6/33 of the whole = 2/11 of the whole. But the slave's bequest is for freedom worth half the estate = 16.5 parts (since half of 33 is 16.5). So the slave is freed to the extent of 6 parts from the third, and must earn the remaining 10.5 parts by sa'yah. The third legatee gets 4 parts from the third, and the sixth legatee gets 1 part from the third. The heirs are entitled to 2/3 of the estate = 22 parts.
The slave's freedom is partial: he is free in proportion to 6/33 of his value, and must work for the rest.
5
Handle sub-case with loss and claim
If half the slave is claimed and half the cash is lost, the estate reduces. The slave's bequest reduces by half (to 3 parts), the unrestricted third bequest reduces proportionally (to 2 parts), while the restricted sixth bequest remains intact (1 part) because it is tied to the cash, and loss falls on heirs. The total for the third becomes 6, so the whole estate is 18 parts. The slave is freed in 3 parts and must earn 6 parts. The third legatee gets 2 parts, the sixth legatee gets 1 part, and the heirs get 12 parts. Muhammad al-Shaybani simplifies by canceling common factors, reducing the base to 7.
The restricted bequest is not reduced because loss is attributed to the heirs, per Hanafi rules.

If someone dies leaving a thousand (dirhams) and a slave worth a thousand, and he bequeaths that his slave be freed, and to a man one-third of his wealth, and to another one-sixth of his wealth, then the third is divided among them on eleven: for the slave six, for the owner of the third four, and for the other one. In this case, it is divided on the basis of 'awl (increase) and mudarabah (proportionate division), not on the basis of contest, by consensus, because contest is not realized here, as two wills do not combine in the slave's neck. Because the right of the legatee of the third is in the earnings (sa'y), not in the slave's neck. Similarly, the right of the heirs is in the earnings when the slave is bequeathed to be freed, because they do not own the slave bequeathed to be freed even if it does not come out of the third, because he is a partial manumitter, and a partial manumitter does not own. Likewise for the legatee of the unrestricted third. Since his right is not established in the slave's neck, there is no contest over the slave, so it is divided by 'awl and mudarabah, not by contest. The method: we need a division with half, third, and sixth, because the slave is bequeathed half of his wealth (since his wealth is 2000: 1000 cash + slave worth 1000), and another legatee gets one-third, and another gets one-sixth. The smallest number from which these shares emerge is 12: half is 6, third is 4, sixth is 2, but the total is 11 (6+4+1=11? Actually sixth is 2 but the text says 1? Wait: read carefully: the text says 'الثلث بينهم على أحد عشر للعبد ستة ولصاحب الثلث أربعة ولآخر واحد' so the total of shares is 11, not 12, because the sixth becomes 1 due to the attribution to the third? The calculation is complex. Then: when the third becomes over 11, the total becomes 33, the slave gets 6 from the third of the wealth, and the slave from the total wealth is half of it, which is 16.5, so he is freed in 6 parts and he earns 10.5 shares. The legatee of the sixth gets 1 part from one third, and 22 remain as double that for the heirs, so the third and two-thirds are established. If half the slave is claimed and half the thousand is lost, then the third becomes over six: 3 for the slave, 2 for the owner of the third, and 1 for the owner of the sixth. Because when half the slave was claimed, half the slave's bequest decreased, leaving his bequest in 3 shares. When half the thousand was lost, half the bequest of the legatee of the third decreased, which is 2 shares, because they were lost on him and on the heirs, as he is like one of the heirs. The bequest of the owner of the sixth remains as is in 1 share, because his bequest is restricted to the thousand, so loss is attributed to the heirs, because it comes out of his third wealth when it is specifically the sixth of the thousand. When half of it was lost, his third becomes a sixth of what remains, because a sixth of the whole is a third of the half. When the third of the wealth becomes 6, the total becomes 18, half is 9, so the slave is freed in 3 parts out of 9 and he earns in 6. That is added to the other half, making all 15. For the legatee of the sixth: one share from 9 from the remaining 500, leaving 14. So the wealth remains on 14: 2 shares for the owner of the third, and 12 for the heirs. And Muhammad (al-Shaybani) derived it as 7, because between the share of the owner of the third and the heirs there is commonality by half: the share of the owner of the third is 2 and the heirs' share is 12, and between the slave and what is due there is commonality by half, so he reduced each share to its half, making 7.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This is a detailed faraidi (inheritance computation) case from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq involving multiple bequests: emancipation of a slave, a one-third unrestricted bequest, and a one-sixth restricted bequest (to a specific 1000). The total estate is 2000 (1000 cash + slave worth 1000). The author explains that since the unrestricted legatee's right is in the slave's earnings (sa'y), not his person, there is no direct contest over the slave's person, so division is by 'awl (proportional increase) and mudarabah (relative division), not by contest. The calculation proceeds by first assigning shares for the wills from the allowed third of the estate. The initial calculation yields a division with base 12, but the shares sum to 11 (6+4+1). Then the total is adjusted to 33, with the slave receiving 6 (part of the third) and his freedom in 16.5 of his value, etc. Then a sub-case where half the slave is claimed (by a third party) and half the cash is lost: this changes the numbers. The text then applies the rules: the restricted bequest (one-sixth of the specific 1000) remains intact because loss is on heirs, while the unrestricted bequest shares the loss proportionally. The final shares are: the slave is partially freed and must earn the remainder. Muhammad al-Shaybani gives a different method of reducing the fractions to achieve a simpler base of 7.

Key Terms
العول (al-‘awl): Proportional increase of the base denominator when prescribed shares exceed the estate, but here used in the context of dividing the one-third among multiple legatees.
المضاربة (al-muḍārabah): Proportionate division, here meaning each legatee gets a share of the total in proportion to their entitlement.
السعاية (al-sa‘āyah): Earnings of a slave after partial manumission; the slave works to earn his freedom.
المنازعة (al-munāza‘ah): Contest or conflict over a specific asset, here the slave's person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the base case, what is the total number of parts when the third is divided among the three legatees?
A) 10
B) 11
C) 12
D) 13

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when multiple bequests involve a slave, the unrestricted legatee's right is limited to the slave's earnings, preventing direct contest over his person and allowing division by proportional allocation ('awl).

Bequest of One-Third of Specific Goods: Partial Loss and Different Types
Commentary clarifying a matn ruling on partial loss of bequeathed specific goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when a bequest of one-third of specific goods (e.g., clothes) suffers a two-thirds loss and explain why the legatee takes one-third of the remainder when the goods are of different types.

Core Idea
When goods are of different types, partial loss falls on the legatee; he gets only what remains of his third.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator clarifies a nuanced point from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. When a testator bequeaths one-third of a specific category of property (like slaves, clothes, or houses) and most of that property is lost before execution, the ruling depends on whether the items are all of one type (jins) or of different types. The passage explains the case of different types, citing the view of Imam Zufar, and notes the distinction from the scenario where goods are of the same type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and the loss
The testator bequeaths one-third of a specific type of property – e.g., his slaves, clothes, or houses. Two-thirds of that specific property are lost before the will is executed.
2
Determine the applicable ruling for different types
If the goods bequeathed are of different types (e.g., clothes of different fabrics), the legatee receives one-third of what remains of that property after the loss.
The text says: 'كان له ثلث الباقي' (he gets one-third of what remains).
3
Understand the reasoning
Because the types are different, they cannot be combined into a single unit to apply the bequest proportionally. Hence the loss is not shared proportionally across the whole; the legatee's entitlement is limited to one-third of the surviving items.
The commentator says: 'لأن الجنس مختلف فلا يمكن جمعه' (because the types are different, they cannot be combined).
4
Contrast with the case of a single type
The passage indicates that if the goods are all of one type, the ruling is different. The text cuts off, but the 'first' case (likely a bequest of one-third of all property or of a single-type item) involves sharing the loss proportionally between the legatee and the heirs.
The phrase 'بخلاف الأول على ما بينا' (unlike the first as we explained) refers to a previously explained rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو رقيقاً أو ثياباً أو دوراً له ثلث ما بقي أي إذا أوصى بثلث رقيقه أو ثيابه أو بثلث دوره فهلك ثلثا ذلك وبقي الثلث وهو يخرج من ثلث ما بقي من ماله كان له ثلث الباقي كما قال زفر لأن الجنس مختلف فلا يمكن جمعه بخلاف الأول على ما بينا . قالوا هذا إذا كانت الثياب من أجناس مختلفة، وإن كانت من جنس واحد فهي
He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: (And if slaves, or clothes, or houses, he gets one-third of what remains) meaning: if he bequeaths one-third of his slaves, or his clothes, or one-third of his houses, then two-thirds of that are lost and one-third remains, and it comes out of one-third of what remains of his wealth, he gets one-third of the remainder as Zufar said, because the types are different, so they cannot be combined, unlike the first as we explained. They said: this is if the clothes are of different types; and if they are of one type, then...
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining a scenario where a will is made for a specific type of property like slaves, clothes, or houses, and most of that property is lost. The commentator clarifies that if the goods are of different types (e.g., clothes of various fabrics), the legatee simply takes one-third of what remains, because the types cannot be pooled together. This differs from a case of a single type (like coins) where the loss might be treated differently. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating that the discussion continues on the next page.

Key Terms
الرقيق (al-raqīq): Slaves (male and female) as a type of property.
الجنس (al-jins): Type or category of goods; if different, cannot be combined for the purpose of the will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) One-third of what remains
C) Nothing, because loss is on legatee
D) The value of one-third of the clothes only

Key Takeaway
For different types of goods in a restricted bequest, partial loss is borne by the legatee; he receives one-third of the remainder.

Ruling on Bequeathing One-Third with Cash and Debt
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forced partition in bequest distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on payment of a bequest from mixed assets and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on forced partition.

Core Idea
A bequest is paid from cash first; debts are given as collected; forced partition of assets is disputed.

When an estate contains both cash (عين) and debts (دين), the legatee's right attaches to the cash first. The debt is paid as it is collected, similar to dirhams. However, a dispute arises regarding assets like slaves and houses: Abu Hanifa does not allow forced partition, while his two students allow it if a judge orders it. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the underlying disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify that the legatee initially receives one-third of the cash. The debt is given as it comes in, treated like dirhams.
Cash is the primary source; debt is secondary.
2
Identify the disputed point
Recognize that the dispute concerns assets like slaves and houses: whether forced partition (جبر على المقاسمة) can be applied.
Forced partition would combine assets with cash to fulfill the bequest.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa does not allow forced partition for slaves and houses; the bequest must come from cash and debts only.
His view is based on the difficulty of combining without a judge.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow forced partition if a judge rules after ijtihad.
They consider that partition can be achieved judicially.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If heirs refuse to partition, Abu Hanifa would not force them; the legatee waits for debt. The Sahibayn would allow a judge to compel partition.
The difference affects how quickly the legatee receives his full share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلث العين دفع إليه وإلا فثلث العين وكلما خرج شيء من الدين فإن خرج بمنزلة الدراهم، وكذا كل مكيل أو موزون كالدراهم لما بينا وقيل : هذا قول أبي حنيفة في الرقيق والدور لأنه لا يرى الجبر على المقاسمة فيهما. وقيل: هذا قول الكل لأن الجميع إنما يتحقق بقضاء القاضي عن اجتهاد عندهما ولا يتحقق بدون القضاء بل يتعذر ولا قضاء هنا فلم يتحقق الجمع إجماعاً، والأشبه أن يكون على الخلاف لأن كل ما أمكن جمعه بدون القضاء أمكن جمعه تقديراً وهذا هو الفقه في هذا الباب ألا ترى أنه أمكن الجمع بدون القضاء عندهما فيما إذا كانت الوصية بثلث الدراهم أو الغنم على ما بينا.
One-third of the cash is given to him, otherwise one-third of the cash, and whenever something comes out of the debt, it comes out like dirhams, and likewise every measurable or weighable item like dirhams as we explained. And it was said: This is the saying of Abu Hanifa regarding slaves and houses because he does not see forced partition in them. And it was said: This is the saying of all because the collection is only realized by the judge's ruling based on ijtihad according to them, and it is not realized without a ruling, rather it is impossible, and there is no ruling here, so collection is not realized by consensus. And the more appropriate is that it is based on disagreement because whatever can be collected without a ruling can be collected in estimation, and this is the fiqh in this chapter. Do you not see that collection without a ruling is possible according to them when the bequest is one-third of dirhams or sheep, as we explained.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author presents the ruling: when a person bequeaths one-third of his estate, and the estate consists of both cash (عين) and debts (دين), the bequest is initially given from the cash. The cash is treated like dirhams; similarly, any measurable or weighable item is treated the same. Then a dispute is mentioned: some say this is Abu Hanifa's position regarding slaves and houses because he does not permit forced partition (جبر) of such assets between heirs and legatees. Others say this is the opinion of all Hanafi scholars, since actual division requires a judge's ruling based on ijtihad, and without that, partition cannot be enforced. The author prefers the view that the disagreement remains, because if partition is possible without a judge (as in the case of a bequest of one-third of dirhams or sheep), it can be done by estimation. The key point is that the legatee's right attaches to the cash first, and he takes from the debt as it is collected.

Key Terms
عين (‘ayn): Tangible, present property (cash or goods) in the estate.
دين (dayn): Debt owed to the deceased, receivable in the future.
جبر على المقاسمة (jabr ‘ala al-muqasamah): Forced partition of shared property among heirs and legatees by judicial order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the initial source from which a bequest of one-third is paid?
A) From both cash and debt equally
B) From the cash only
C) From the debt only
D) From whatever the heirs choose

Key Takeaway
When an estate includes cash and debt, the legatee takes from cash first, and the debt is given as collected; forced partition of certain assets is disputed within the Hanafi school.

Calculating Shares with a Debtor Heir and Bequest
Complete faraid calculation for a bequest with cash and debt from one son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares for two sons, a legatee, cash, and a debt from one son, applying the Hanafi qisas rule to offset the debtor's share.

Core Idea
When an heir owes a debt to the estate, his inheritance share offsets the debt, not paid to him.

A man dies leaving two sons, 100 dirhams in cash, and one son owes 100 dinars to the estate. He also bequeaths one-third of his estate to a stranger. How do you distribute the cash and handle the debt? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq demonstrates the Hanafi method, where the debtor son's share is not physically given but used to reduce his liability. This lesson walks you through the calculation step by step.

Guided Path
1
List all heirs and their categories
Identify the heirs: two sons (asabah) and a legatee (non-heir with a will). Note the cash (100 dirhams) and the debt (100 dinars from one son). The total estate value for the will is cash plus receivables? Here only cash is tangible; the debt is an asset.
The legatee is not a Quranic heir; his share is from the will, permitted up to one-third.
2
Apply hajb (partial exclusion) to the debtor son
The debtor son's share of cash is theoretically one-third, but because his debt exceeds his share (he owes 100 dinars > his cash share of 33.33 dirhams), his cash share is not given to him; it offsets his debt. This is qisas (offsetting).
Cash and debt are of different units, but the text treats them as comparable after conversion? Actually, the text uses 'the estate is of the same type as the debt'—both are monetary, so offsetting applies.
3
Divide the cash among the legatee, non-debtor son, and the (offset) debtor
The cash (100 dirhams) is divided into three equal shares: 1/3 for the legatee, 1/3 for the non-debtor son, and 1/3 for the debtor. But the debtor's share is immediately absorbed by his debt. So effectively, the legatee and non-debtor son each get 50 dirhams (half of the cash after adjustment).
The text says 'the legatee gets half the cash, and half for the non-debtor son' after considering the debtor's share.
4
Calculate the offset and remaining debt
The debtor's cash share (33.33 dirhams) is deducted from his debt of 100 dinars, reducing his debt to 66.67 dinars. He also pays an additional 33.33 dirhams? Actually, the text says he pays 33 and 1/3 to be divided between the legatee and non-debtor son. This requires careful reading: the debtor's theoretical share from cash is 33.33, which he doesn't receive; instead, it reduces his debt. Then he pays an additional 33.33 from his own pocket? The text: 'ويؤدي ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث بين الابن غير المدين والموصى له نصفين'—he pays 33.33 to be split between them. This may reflect that the debtor's share of the estate (cash) is not enough to cover his debt, so he must also pay extra to satisfy the bequest? Alternatively, it's a different calculation. For simplicity, we will stick to the text's result: legatee and non-debtor son each end up with 50 dirhams.
The exact arithmetic is nuanced; the key is that the debtor son receives no cash and his debt is reduced by his inheritance.
5
Generalize to a bequest of one-fourth
If the bequest is one-fourth instead of one-third, the calculation changes: total estate values are 200 dirhams (100 cash + 100 debt assumed as asset). The legatee gets 1/4 = 50 dirhams. Each son's share is 75 dirhams. The debtor's share (75) is deducted from his debt, leaving him 25 to pay more? The text shows a different distribution: the remaining cash (100) is divided between legatee and non-debtor son in a 2:3 ratio, etc. This illustrates the method's flexibility.
The one-fourth example reinforces the same principle: the debtor's share offsets his debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل مات وترك ابنين ومائة درهم عيناً ومائة دينار على أحد ابنيه وأوصى لرجل بالثلث كان له نصف العين والنصف لغير المدين لأن العين أثلاثاً ثلثه للموصى له وثلثه لمن لا دين عليه وثلثه للدين إلا أن المدين لا تقسم بينهم يعطيه نصيبه لأن ما عليه أكثر مما له والتركة من جنس الدين فيحسب ما له قصاصاً بما عليه لأن ما عليه أكثر مما له والتركة من جنس الدين فإن ما يخص الابن المدين ذهب بحصته مما عليه ستة وستون وثلثان ويؤدي ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث بين الابن غير المدين والموصى له نصفين لأن حقهما سيان ولو أوصى بربع العين والدين كان له نصف العين لأن جميع مال الميت مائتا درهم للموصى له ربعه وذلك خمسون يبقى مائة وخمسون لكل ابن خمسة وسبعون إلا أنه لا يعطى للمدين شيء من العين بل يطرح عنه نصيبه من الدين لأنه لا فائدة في ذلك فيطرح مما عليه نصيبه وذلك خمسة وسبعون ويؤدي ذلك خمسة وعشرون ويقسم ما بقي عليه وهو المائة العين بين الموصى له وبين غير المدين على خمسة أسهم مع سهمان للموصى له وذلك خمسة وثلاثة أخماسه للابن الذي لا دين عليه ويبرأ المدين عن
A man dies leaving two sons, 100 dirhams in cash, and 100 dinars as a debt from one of his sons, and he bequeaths to a man one-third. The legatee gets half the cash, and half for the non-debtor son, because the cash is thirds: one-third for the legatee, one-third for the one with no debt, and one-third for the debt. But the debtor son is not given his portion because what he owes is more than what he has, and the estate is of the same type as the debt, so what he has is counted as offsetting what he owes. Since what he owes is more than what he has and the estate is of the same type as the debt, the share of the debtor son is taken from his debt: 66 and 2/3, and he pays 33 and 1/3 to be divided between the non-debtor son and the legatee half each because their claims are equal. And if he bequeaths one-fourth of the cash and debt, the legatee gets half the cash because all of the deceased's property is 200 dirhams; the legatee gets one-fourth which is 50, leaving 150, each son gets 75, except that nothing is given to the debtor from the cash; rather his share is deducted from his debt because there is no benefit in it. So his share (75) is deducted from his debt, and he pays 25. And what remains of the cash (100) is divided between the legatee and the non-debtor son on five shares: two shares for the legatee and three-fifths for the son with no debt, and the debtor is freed from
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents a complete faraid case involving a bequest when the estate includes cash and a debt from one heir. The deceased leaves two sons, 100 dirhams cash, and 100 dinars as a debt from one son. He bequeaths one-third to a stranger. The key is that the cash is divided into three parts: one for the legatee, one for the non-debtor son, and one for the debt. But the debtor son's share of the cash is not given to him because his debt exceeds his share; instead, his share offsets his debt. The calculation shows the legatee and the non-debtor son each get half the cash (50 dirhams each) after the debtor's share is absorbed. The text also covers a variation where the bequest is one-fourth, showing similar logic. The debtor's share is deducted from his debt, and the remaining cash is divided between the legatee and the non-debtor son in proportion to their claims. The case illustrates the Hanafi principle that when a debtor heir owes more than his inheritance share, his share is used to reduce his debt.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Offsetting the debtor's inheritance share against his debt.
مدين (madyin): The son who owes a debt to the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of two sons where one owes a debt, how is the cash divided when the bequest is one-third?
A) The legatee gets 1/3, the non-debtor son gets 1/3, and the debtor son gets 1/3
B) The legatee and non-debtor son each get half the cash
C) The legatee gets all the cash
D) The debtor son gets the cash to pay his debt

Key Takeaway
When an heir owes a debt to the estate, his inheritance share is used to reduce that debt, not paid to him, in accordance with the Hanafi principle of qisas.

Multiple Legatees and Debtor Heirs in Wills
Faraid calculations with multiple legatees and debtor heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate estate distribution when there are multiple legatees and a debtor heir, applying the Hanafi faraid method.

Core Idea
Debts of an heir reduce the estate; bequests are proportional from the residue.

This lesson extends faraid to scenarios where bequests interact with heir debts. We examine two cases: one with multiple legatees and a debtor son, and another with a wife debtor. Master these calculations to avoid common errors in will distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify all parties
List heirs, legatees, and debtors. In case one: two sons (one debtor), two legatees (1/4 and 1/3). In case two: wife (debtor), son, and a legatee (1/3).
Debtor heirs are still heirs but their share is affected.
2
Determine the base denominator (asl al-mas'alah)
Find the LCM of the fractions involved. For legatees 1/3 and 1/4, base is 12. For wife case with 1/3 and 1/8, base is 11 (as explained).
The base distributes the shares among the legatees.
3
Apply hajb nuqsan for debtor heir
If an heir's debt exceeds his share, his portion is dropped from the current distribution. The debtor son's share is set aside, effectively treated as if he is absent for now.
This is a reduction (nuqsan), not total exclusion (hirman).
4
Distribute the cash among eligible parties
Divide the available estate (cash) proportionally: legatees receive their fractions of the residue; the non-debtor son gets the remainder.
The debtor son's potential share is held to cover his debt.
5
Reassess if debtor becomes solvent
If the debtor later pays, the estate is recalculated with the full value (including the paid debt), and distributions are adjusted accordingly.
This shows the contingent nature of faraid with debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أوصى لرجل بربع ماله ولآخر بثلث ماله كان نصف العين بينهما على ثمانية لصاحب الربع أربعة وأربعة لصاحب الثلث لأن أصل الفريضة من ثلاثة إذا لم تجز الورثة سهم الموصى له بقي سهمان بين الاثنين نصفين لكل واحد سهم ما يصيب المدين من العين يطرح لأن ما عليه أكثر مما له وأقسم المائة العين بين الابن غير المدين وبين الموصى لهما نصفين لكل واحد خمسون ويحسب للابن المدين ما عليه خمسون مثل ما حصل للابن غير الابن فصار العين من مال الميت حقيقة وحكماً مائة وخمسين مئة عين حقيقة وخمسون عين حكماً وهو قدر ما استوفاه الابن المدين وبقي على المدين خمسون ناوياً ما دام معتبراً فلا بد من مال الميت ثم ما أصاب الموصى له من نصف العين يقسم بينهما على سبعة لأن أقل حساب له ثلث وربع اثنان عشر فحق الموصى له بالثلث في أربعة وحق الموصى له بالربع في ثلاثة فصار جميع ذلك سبعة، فاقسم الثلث على سبعة أربعة لصاحب الثلث وثلاثة لصاحب الربع فإن أيسر الابن المدين وقدر على الأداء اعتبر المال كله فيكون بين الورثة والموصى لهما أثلاثاً، ثم مال الموصى لهما بينهما على سبعة لأنه لما أيسر ظهر أن مال الميت كان مائتين فيكون ثلث ماله ستة وستين وثلاثين فيقسم دين الموصى لهما على سبعة كما وصفنا، وإذا كان له مائة درهم عيناً وديناً على امرأته ثم مات وترك امرأته وابنه وأوصى بثلث ماله لرجل قسم العين بين الابن والموصى له على أحد عشر للموصى له أربعة فإن قدرت المرأة على الأداء كان للموصى له ثلث كل المال ستة وستون وثلثان وللمرأة ثمن الباقي ستة عشر وثلثان تؤدي الفضل، فإذا أدت قسم بين الابن والموصى له على أحد عشر .
And if he bequeaths to a man one-fourth of his wealth and to another one-third of his wealth, half the cash is between them on eight: for the owner of the fourth, four, and four for the owner of the third, because the origin of the estate is from three, if the heirs do not consent, the share of the legatee remains, two shares remain between the two, half each, each one share. What falls to the debtor from the cash is dropped because what he owes is more than what he has. And I divide the 100 cash between the non-debtor son and the two legatees half each: each gets fifty. And the debtor son's debt is counted as fifty like what the non-debtor son got, so the cash from the deceased's property becomes in reality and by estimation 150: 100 real cash and 50 estimated cash, which is the amount the debtor son collected, and there remains on the debtor fifty outstanding as long as it is considered, so the deceased's property must be... Then what falls to the legatees from half the cash is divided between them on seven, because the least denominator for third and fourth is twelve: the share of the legatee of the third is four, and the share of the legatee of the fourth is three, so all becomes seven. So divide the third on seven: four for the owner of the third and three for the owner of the fourth. If the debtor son becomes wealthy and able to pay, the entire wealth is considered, and it is between the heirs and the two legatees in thirds. Then the amount of the two legatees is divided on seven, because when he became wealthy, it appears that the deceased's wealth was 200, so one-third is 66 and a third, and it is divided as described. And if he has 100 dirhams cash and a debt from his wife, then he dies leaving his wife and son and bequeaths one-third to a man, the cash is divided between the son and the legatee on eleven: for the legatee four. If the wife can pay, the legatee gets one-third of all the wealth: 66 and two-thirds, and the wife gets one-eighth of the remainder: 16 and two-thirds, she pays the excess. When she pays, it is divided between the son and the legatee on eleven.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage contains two complete faraid cases. The first involves bequests of one-fourth and one-third to two different persons, with the same two-son scenario (one debtor). The calculation shows how the cash is divided: first, the legatees share half the cash proportionally (using base 12 for 1/4 and 1/3). The debtor son's share is dropped. If the debtor later becomes able to pay, the entire estate value is reconsidered. The second case involves a wife who owes a debt to the deceased. The deceased leaves a wife and a son, and bequeaths one-third to a stranger. The cash is divided between son and legatee on base 11 (a common fraction for 1/3 and 1/8). If the wife pays her debt, the legatee gets 1/3 of total, and the wife gets 1/8 of the remainder, then the residue is divided on 11. The calculations illustrate Hanafi inheritance with bequests and debts from heirs.

Key Terms
أصل الفريضة (asl al-faridah): The base denominator used for fractional share distribution.
أيسر (aysara): Became wealthy or able to pay a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the wife case, if the wife can pay her debt, what does the legatee receive?
A) One-third of the cash only
B) One-third of the total estate (66.67)
C) One-eighth of the estate
D) Half of the cash

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, debtor heirs' shares are contingent, and solvency recalculates the estate for accurate distribution.
