Ruling When a Beneficiary Is Dead at the Time of the Will
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest distribution when one beneficiary is already dead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distribution when one beneficiary is dead at the time of the will and distinguish Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
A dead beneficiary cannot inherit; the living receives the entire bequest.

When a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to two persons, but one of them is already dead at the time the will is made, how is the share distributed? This lesson examines the Hanafi position, the intra-madhhab difference with Abu Yusuf, and the principle of legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the passage deals with a bequest to two named individuals where one is dead at the time of the will. The ruling depends on whether the testator knew of the death.
The text contrasts knowledge vs. ignorance.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, the living beneficiary takes the entire one-third because a dead person lacks legal capacity (ahliyyah) to receive a bequest. The will to the dead is void ab initio.
The analogy with a wall (jidaar) illustrates that the dead is like an inanimate object.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on the testator's knowledge: if the testator was unaware of the death, the bequest to the dead is considered valid in intention, so the living only gets half the third. If the testator knew, the entire third goes to the living.
The dispute is over the effect of the testator's intention.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view: the living gets the entire third regardless of knowledge, because the dead is not eligible.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah favors this view.
5
Apply the principle
Practice: if a testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and Amr, and Amr died before the will, Zayd takes the full third. No share is lost due to the death.
This is based on the principle that the dead lacks ahliyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وبثلثه لزيد وعمرو وهو ميت فلزيد (كله أي إذا أوصى لزيد وعمرو وعمرو ميت فالثلث كله لزيد لأن الميت ليس بأهل للوصية فلا يشارك الحي الذي [؟] أهل كما إذا أوصى لزيد وجدار. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا لم يعلم بموته كان له نصف الثلث لأن الوصية عنده صحيحة لعمرو فلم يوص للحي إلا بنصف الثلث بخلاف ما إذا علم بموته لأن الوصية لعمرو لم تصح فكان راضياً بكل الثلث للحي. هذا إذا كان المزاحم معدوماً من الأصل، أما إذا خرج المزاحم بعد صحة الإيجاب يخرج بحصته ولا يسلم للآخر كل الثلث لأن الوصية صحت لهما وتثبت الشركة بينهما فبطلان حق ذلك لا أحدهما بعد يوجب زيادة حق الآخر مثاله إذا قال ثلث مالي لفلان ولفلان ابن عبد الله إن مت وهو فقير فمات الموصي وفلان ابن عبد الله غني كان لفلان نصف الثلث، وكذا لو قال ثلث مالي لفلان إن كان عبد الله في البيت ولم يكن عبد الله في البيت كان لفلان نصف الثلث لأن بطلان استحقاقه لفقد شرطه لا يوجب الزيادة في حق الآخر، ومتى لم يدخل في الوصية لفقد الأهلية كان الكل للآخر وقد قدمناه في بعض هذه المسائل.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And by one-third to Zayd and Amr, and he (Amr) is dead, then for Zayd (all of it).' Meaning: if he bequeaths to Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, then the entire one-third is for Zayd, because the dead is not eligible for bequest, so he does not share with the living person who is eligible, just as if he bequeathed to Zayd and a wall. And from Abu Yusuf: if he did not know of his death, then Zayd gets half of the third, because according to him the bequest to Amr is valid, so he did not bequeath to the living except half the third, contrary to if he knew of his death, because the bequest to Amr is invalid, so he was content with the entire third for the living. This is when the competing beneficiary is nonexistent from the origin. However, if the competing beneficiary leaves after the validity of the offer, he leaves with his share, and the other does not get the entire third, because the bequest was valid for both and partnership is established between them, and the nullification of the right of one does not cause an increase in the right of the other. Example: if he says 'one-third of my wealth is for so-and-so and for so-and-so, son of Abdullah, if he dies poor,' and the testator dies and so-and-so is rich, then so-and-so gets half the third. Likewise, if he says 'one-third of my wealth is for so-and-so if Abdullah is in the house,' and Abdullah is not in the house, then so-and-so gets half the third, because the nullification of his entitlement due to the loss of its condition does not cause an increase in the right of the other. And whenever he does not enter the bequest due to lack of eligibility, then the entire amount is for the other, and we have presented this in some of these issues.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses two distinct scenarios regarding bequests to multiple beneficiaries. The first is when one of two named beneficiaries is already dead at the time the will is made. In that case, the living beneficiary receives the entire one-third because a dead person lacks the legal capacity (ahliyyah) to receive a bequest. This is the position of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf adds a nuance: if the testator was unaware of the death, the living gets only half because the bequest to the dead is considered valid in itself (though unenforceable), so the testator's intention was to give half to each. The second scenario is when a condition attached to the bequest fails after the will is made, e.g., 'if he is poor' or 'if Abdullah is in the house.' In such cases, the other beneficiary does not receive the extra share; he only gets half, because the bequest was validly made to both initially, and the subsequent failure of the condition for one does not increase the other's share. The key principle: if the competing beneficiary is nonexistent from the outset (dead), the living gets all; if the competing beneficiary becomes invalid later (condition fails), the other's share is not increased.

Key Terms
المزاحم (al-muzahim): The competing beneficiary who is entitled to a share but may be excluded due to death or condition failure.
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity to receive a bequest; the dead lacks it.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest of up to one-third of the estate to a non-heir, effective after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does the living beneficiary receive when the other named beneficiary is dead at the time of the will?
A) Half the one-third
B) The entire one-third
C) Nothing, the will is void
D) One quarter

Key Takeaway
A dead beneficiary cannot inherit; the living receives the entire bequest, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Ruling When a Condition Attached to a Bequest Fails Later
Clarifying that condition failure after the will does not cause the other beneficiary to gain the lapsed share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that failure of a condition after the will does not increase the other beneficiary's share.

Core Idea
Loss of one beneficiary's share due to condition failure does not benefit the other; the share remains as originally divided.

Sometimes a bequest is conditional, such as 'if he is poor' or 'if Abdullah is in the house.' When the condition fails, does the other beneficiary get the extra share? This lesson explains the Hanafi rule: because the bequest was validly made to both initially, the failure of the condition for one does not increase the other's portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that this passage deals with a bequest to two persons where a condition attached to one beneficiary's entitlement fails after the will is made (e.g., the condition is not met at the testator's death).
The condition is not about death but about an uncertain future event.
2
Understand the initial validity
At the time the will is made, both beneficiaries have valid potential rights. The bequest creates a shared right between them (partnership).
The phrase 'the bequest was valid for both' indicates a valid legal relationship.
3
Contrast with the dead beneficiary case
In the dead beneficiary case, the competing beneficiary never had capacity, so the other gets all. Here, the condition fails later, so the right of the other is not increased.
The key distinction: initial vs. subsequent invalidity.
4
Apply to the examples
Example 1: 'One-third to X and Y if Y is poor'; Y is rich at death → X gets half the third, not the whole. Example 2: 'One-third to X if Abdullah is in the house'; Abdullah is not in the house → X gets half the third, not the whole.
The ruling is consistent: the share of the one whose condition fails does not go to the other.
5
State the principle
The principle: 'Nullification of entitlement due to loss of condition does not cause an increase in the right of the other.' This is because the bequest was initially made to both.
This principle is a corollary of the rule that a validly created right (here, a share in the bequest) is not expanded by another's loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وبثلثه لزيد وعمرو وهو ميت فلزيد (كله أي إذا أوصى لزيد وعمرو وعمرو ميت فالثلث كله لزيد لأن الميت ليس بأهل للوصية فلا يشارك الحي الذي [؟] أهل كما إذا أوصى لزيد وجدار. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا لم يعلم بموته كان له نصف الثلث لأن الوصية عنده صحيحة لعمرو فلم يوص للحي إلا بنصف الثلث بخلاف ما إذا علم بموته لأن الوصية لعمرو لم تصح فكان راضياً بكل الثلث للحي. هذا إذا كان المزاحم معدوماً من الأصل، أما إذا خرج المزاحم بعد صحة الإيجاب يخرج بحصته ولا يسلم للآخر كل الثلث لأن الوصية صحت لهما وتثبت الشركة بينهما فبطلان حق ذلك لا أحدهما بعد يوجب زيادة حق الآخر مثاله إذا قال ثلث مالي لفلان ولفلان ابن عبد الله إن مت وهو فقير فمات الموصي وفلان ابن عبد الله غني كان لفلان نصف الثلث، وكذا لو قال ثلث مالي لفلان إن كان عبد الله في البيت ولم يكن عبد الله في البيت كان لفلان نصف الثلث لأن بطلان استحقاقه لفقد شرطه لا يوجب الزيادة في حق الآخر، ومتى لم يدخل في الوصية لفقد الأهلية كان الكل للآخر وقد قدمناه في بعض هذه المسائل.

Meaning: if he bequeaths to Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, then the entire one-third is for Zayd, because the dead is not eligible for bequest, so he does not share with the living person who is eligible, just as if he bequeathed to Zayd and a wall. The first is when one of two named beneficiaries is already dead at the time the will is made. In that case, the living beneficiary receives the entire one-third because a dead person lacks the legal capacity (ahliyyah) to receive a bequest. This is the position of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf adds a nuance: if the testator was unaware of the death, the living gets only half because the bequest to the dead is considered valid in itself (though unenforceable), so the testator's intention was to give half to each. The second scenario is when a condition attached to the bequest fails after the will is made, e.g., 'if he is poor' or 'if Abdullah is in the house.' In such cases, the other beneficiary does not receive the extra share; he only gets half, because the bequest was validly made to both initially, and the subsequent failure of the condition for one does not increase the other's share. The key principle: if the competing beneficiary is nonexistent from the outset (dead), the living gets all; if the competing beneficiary becomes invalid later (condition fails), the other's share is not increased.

Key Terms
المزاحم (al-muzahim): The competing beneficiary who is entitled to a share but may be excluded due to death or condition failure.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest of up to one-third of the estate to a non-heir, effective after death.
شرط (shart): Condition attached to a bequest. Failure of condition does not increase other's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths one-third to 'X and Y' with the condition 'if Y is a resident of the city.' Y is not a resident. What does X receive?
A) The entire one-third
B) Half the one-third
C) Nothing, the bequest is void
D) One quarter

Key Takeaway
Failure of a condition attached to a bequest does not cause the other beneficiary to gain the lapsed share; only initial lack of eligibility (like death) does.

Bequest to Non-Existent or Conditional Beneficiaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a bequest to a non-existent or conditionally defined beneficiary is void and apply the Hanafi principle that conditions are interpreted literally.

Core Idea
A bequest to a non-existent person is void; conditional bequests are evaluated at death.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines several bequest scenarios where the beneficiary is either nonexistent at the time of the will or described by a condition. The Hanafi school strictly requires the beneficiary to exist at death, and conditions are interpreted according to their literal meaning. Understanding these rules prevents common errors in drafting wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Determine whether the bequest is to an existing person alongside a nonexistent group (e.g., 'descendants'), a non-existent specific person (e.g., 'child of Abdullah'), a conditional person (e.g., 'if he dies free'), or a described group (e.g., 'whoever becomes poor').
The key distinction is whether the beneficiary is determined at death or at the time of the will.
2
Apply the rule on non-existence
For bequests to nonexistent persons (like 'descendants' or a child not yet born), the bequest to that part is void. The entire bequest goes to the existing beneficiary.
This is because the offer (ijab) to a nonexistent is invalid in Hanafi law.
3
Evaluate conditions and descriptive phrases
For conditional bequests (e.g., 'if he dies free'), the condition must be literally fulfilled at death. For descriptive phrases like 'whoever becomes poor,' the description is interpreted strictly: it applies only to those who change from rich to poor, not those originally poor.
The time of determination is the testator's death, not the time of the will.
4
Synthesize the ruling
Combine the above steps to state the final distribution: the existing or non-conditionally described beneficiary receives the bequest; the nonexistent or non-fulfilling part is void.
If the condition fails, or if no one meets the description, the other beneficiary takes all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال ثلث مالي لفلان ولعقبه ثم مات الموصي فالثلث كله لفلان والوصية لعقبه باطلة لأنه جمع بين الموجود والمعدوم في الإيجاب لأن عقب فلان من يخلفه بعد موته فلا يتصور له عقب في حياته واستحقاقه الوصية حال حياة الموصى له والعقب معدوم والإيجاب للمعدوم لا يصح ولو قال لفلان ولولد عبد الله فالثلث كله لفلان لأن الوصية لولد عبد الله إنما تتناول ولده عند موت الموصي لا عند الإيصاء لأنه أرسل الموصى له ولو أرسل الموصى به فقال ثلث مالي لفلان فينصرف إلى ثلث ماله يوم موت الموصي لا يوم الوصية فكذلك الموصى له ولا ولد لعبد الله فلا يصح إيجاب الوصية له فصار كأنه أوصى لفلان لا غير وتحقيقه أن العين تعرف الموصى. يوم موت بالإشارة إليها لا بالصفة فلم يشترط الوصف لتناول الإيجاب وغيره الدين إنما يعرف بصفته وإنما يتناول الإيجاب إذا وجد فيه تلك الصفة عند موت الموصي فلم توجد الصفة فلم يتناوله الإيجاب فكان الثلث للآخر. وكذلك لو قال ثلث مالي لفلان إن مت وهو حر ولفلان بن فلان، فإن مات وهو حر فالثلث بينهما، وإن مات قبل موته كان للثاني النصف لا غير لما قلنا ولو قال ثلث مالي لفلان ولمن افتقر من ولد فلان ثم مات الموصي وولد فلان كلهم أغنياء فالثلث كله لفلان لأنه ضم إلى فلان شخصاً موصوفاً بأنه فقير، وما أشار إلى العين فيكون مرسلاً لا معيناً فتتعين فيه حال الموت ولا وقت الإيصاء. وقوله «لمن افتقر» يتناول من احتاج بعد أن كان غنياً دون من كان فقيراً من الأصل لأن هذا اللفظ إنما يستعمل فيمن احتاج بعد الغناء وفي المبرة معه زيادة ثواب وقد ندب الشرع إليه لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام اكرموا ثلاثة عزيز قوم ذل وغنياً افتقر وعالماً بين جهال فيجوز أن يكون للموصي بالتخصيص هذه الزيادة. ولو أوصى لامرأته بأحد العبدين وللأجنبي بالآخر كان للأجنبي ثلثا عبده يبدأ به أربعة من ستة فصار كل عبد على ستة وكلاهما اثنا عشر وللمرأة ربع ما بقي من العبدين سهمان من ثمانية بالميراث سهم ونصف من عبدهما ونصف سهم من يبقى لهما من وصيتها أربعة ونصف ويبقى للأجنبي من وصيته اثنان فيضرب كل واحد بذلك في الستة الباقية، فإذا أردت تصحيح الفريضة جعلت كل عبد مائة وستة وخمسين سهماً لأن قصد الأجنبي
And if he says: 'One-third of my wealth for so-and-so and for his descendants,' then the testator dies, so the entire third is for so-and-so, and the bequest to his descendants is void, because he combined the existing and the nonexistent in the offer, since the descendant of so-and-so is one who succeeds him after his death, so he has no descendant in his lifetime, and entitlement to the bequest at the time of the testator's life, and the descendant is nonexistent, and an offer to a nonexistent person is invalid. And if he says: 'for so-and-so and for the child of Abdullah,' then the entire third is for so-and-so, because the bequest to the child of Abdullah only applies to his child at the time of the testator's death, not at the time of the will, because he sent the legatee (in a general sense). And if he sent the bequeathed item, saying 'one-third of my wealth for so-and-so,' it refers to one-third of his wealth on the day of death, not the day of the will. Similarly for the legatee. And there is no child of Abdullah, so the offer of bequest to him is invalid, so it becomes as if he bequeathed only to so-and-so. Its verification: the tangible property is known by pointing to it, not by description, so the description was not required for the offer to include it. But a debt is known by its description, and the offer only includes it if that description exists at the time of the testator's death, so if the description is not found, the offer does not include it, so the third is for the other. Likewise, if he says: 'One-third of my wealth for so-and-so if he dies a free man, and for so-and-so, son of so-and-so,' then if he dies a free man, the third is between them; but if he dies before his death, then the second gets only half, as we said. And if he says: 'One-third of my wealth for so-and-so and for whoever becomes poor among the children of so-and-so,' then the testator dies and all the children are rich, so the entire third is for so-and-so, because he joined to so-and-so a person described as poor, and he did not point to a specific person, so it is unqualified, not specific, so it is determined at the time of death, not the time of the will. And his saying 'whoever becomes poor' includes one who becomes needy after being rich, not one who was originally poor, because this expression is used for one who becomes needy after wealth, and there is increased reward in charity for him, and the Law has encouraged it due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Honor three: a noble people who have become low, a rich man who has become poor, and a scholar among ignoramuses.' So it is permissible for the testator to specify this increase. And if he bequeaths to his wife one of the two slaves and to the stranger the other, then the stranger has two-thirds of his slave, starting with four out of six, so each slave becomes six, and both together twelve. The wife has a quarter of what remains of the two slaves, two shares out of eight by inheritance, one and a half shares of their slave, and half a share of ... remains for them from her bequest four and a half, and for the stranger from his bequest two. So each is multiplied by the remaining six. If you want to correct the division, make each slave one hundred and fifty-six shares, because the stranger intended...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios of bequests when the beneficiary is nonexistent or conditional. First, a bequest to someone and his 'descendants' (aqib) is void for the descendants because at the time of the will, the descendants do not exist; only the named person takes the whole third. Similarly, a bequest to 'the child of Abdullah' is void if Abdullah has no child at the testator's death, so the other beneficiary takes all. Second, a conditional bequest like 'if he dies free' — if the condition is met, they share; if not, the other gets only half (because the condition failed, not because of initial ineligibility). Third, a bequest to 'whoever becomes poor' among a group: only those who become poor after being rich are included, not those who were poor originally. The word 'iftaqara' (became poor) implies a change from wealth to poverty. The passage ends with a complex calculation involving bequest of two slaves to wife and stranger, where the shares are adjusted for the wife's inheritance and the stranger's bequest; the calculation involves setting a base number of shares to resolve fractions.

Key Terms
عقب (aqib): Descendants; in this context, future generations who do not exist at the time of the will.
افتقر (iftaqara): Became poor after being rich; used in the condition 'whoever becomes poor'.
مرسل (mursal): Unqualified or general; a bequest to an unspecified group determined at death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zayd and the children of Amr share the third equally
B) Zayd gets the entire third
C) The bequest is invalid
D) The children of Amr get the third

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to a non-existent person is void, and conditions are interpreted literally; the time of determination is the testator's death.

Bequests: Wording Distinctions and the Killer Case
Commentary on bequest wording and killer bequest dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests using 'bayna' vs 'li' and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on bequests to a killer.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'bayna' forces equal sharing; 'li' gives entire shares to each, but a killer's bequest splits Hanafi opinions.

The testator's choice of words in a bequest can dramatically change the distribution. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq unpacks a key distinction: using 'bayna' (between) versus 'li' (to) when naming multiple beneficiaries. It then enters a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a bequest to a person who killed the testator is valid. Understanding these rulings is essential for anyone drafting or interpreting a will under Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'bayna' from 'li'
Identify the two key Arabic words used in bequests. 'Bayna' implies sharing and halving; 'li' grants exclusive entitlement to each named person.
The difference is not just semantic—it changes who takes what when one beneficiary is dead.
2
Analyse the 'bayna' scenario
When the testator says 'one-third of my wealth between Zayd and ʿAmr' and ʿAmr is dead, Zayd gets only half of that third because 'bayna' forces a 50/50 split, and the dead man's share is lost.
The sharing is due to the wording, not competition.
3
Analyse the 'li' scenario
When the testator says 'to Zayd and ʿAmr' and ʿAmr is dead, Zayd takes the entire third because 'li' gives each the whole, so the live person absorbs the dead one's share.
This outcome is based on the principle of exclusive grant (mulk).
4
Examine the bequest to a killer dispute
Identify the three Hanafi positions: Abu Hanifa equates it to a bequest to an heir (requires heirs' permission); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad deem it absolutely invalid.
The disagreement hinges on whether killing the testator creates a strong presumption of fraud.
5
Apply the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative position) is Abu Hanifa's view, but with the condition that if there are no other heirs, the bequest to the killer is valid.
This is the point of thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

المانع من
قال رحمه الله: (ولو) قال بين زيد وعمر ولزيد (نصفه أي إذا قالت ثلث مالي بين زيد وعمرو وعمرو ميت كان لزيد نصف الثلث لأن كلمة بين توجب التنصيف فلا يتكامل لعدم المزاحمة بخلاف ما إذا قال لفلان وفلان فبان أحدهما ميتاً حيث يكون للحي كل الثلث لأن الجملة الأولى كلام يقتضي الاختصاص بالحكم لأن العطف يقتضي المشاركة في الحكم
Book of bequests, chapter on bequest of one-third. ... between ... one of them alive ... for the validity of the making of obligation for both due to the existence of legal capacity in both; if one of them is not eligible for entitlement at the time of making the obligation, then the whole third is for the eligible one, as if he bequeathed the third to so-and-so and a wall. If he says 'I bequeath one-third of my wealth between so-and-so and so-and-so' and one of them is dead, then half of the third is for the other. Similarly, if he says 'between so-and-so and this' pointing to a wall and the like, because the word 'between' necessitates sharing or halving. Do you not see that if he said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so and so-and-so' and remained silent, he would not have except half of the third? And the word 'between' is uttered, whether both are alive or the other is dead, so sharing is by virtue of the wording, not by virtue of competition in the place, contrary to if he said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so and so-and-so' and one of them is dead, because here sharing and halving is by virtue of competition, not by virtue of the wording, because the wording necessitates singular bestowal of the whole, as we explained. And if he said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so and to his offspring', then the testator dies, the whole third is for so-and-so, and the bequest to his offspring is void, because he combined the existent and the non-existent in the making of obligation, because the offspring of so-and-so are those who succeed him after his death, so it is not conceivable that he has offspring in his lifetime, and entitlement to the bequest is at the lifetime of the legatee, while the offspring is non‑existent, and the making of obligation to a non‑existent is invalid. And if he said 'to so-and-so and to the child of Abdullah', then the whole third is for so-and-so, because the bequest to the child of Abdullah only applies to his child at the death of the testator, not at the time of the bequest, because he left the legatee unspecified; and if he left the bequest unspecified and said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so', it is diverted to one-third of his wealth on the day of the testator's death, not on the day of the bequest; so similarly the legatee; and there is no child of Abdullah, so the making of the bequest to him is invalid, so it is as if he bequeathed only to so-and-so. And its verification: that the physical thing is known by pointing to it, not by description, so description is not a condition for the application of the making of obligation and other things; while a debt is known by its description, and the making of obligation only applies if that description is found at the death of the testator; the description was not found, so the making of obligation did not apply to it, so the third is for the other. Similarly, if he said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so if I die while he is free, and to so-and-so son of so-and-so', then if he dies while he is free, the third is between them; if he dies before his death, then the second gets only half, as we said. And if he said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so and to whoever among the children of so-and-so becomes poor', then the testator dies while the children of so-and-so are all rich, then the whole third is for so-and-so, because he attached to so-and-so a person described as poor, and he did not point to a specific thing, so it is unspecified not specific, so it is determined at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest. And his statement 'whoever becomes poor' applies to one who becomes needy after having been rich, not to one who was originally poor, because this word is only used for one who becomes needy after wealth, and there is an extra reward in charity, and the Law has encouraged it due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Honour three: a noble people who become base, a rich man who becomes poor, and a scholar among ignorant.' So it is permissible that the testator has this extra merit in specification. And if he bequeathed to his wife one of the two slaves and to a stranger the other, then the stranger has two‑thirds of his slave? He starts with four from six, so each slave becomes six and both are twelve; and the wife has a quarter of what remains of the two slaves, two shares from eight by inheritance: one and a half shares from his two slaves and half a share from what remains for them from her bequest four and a half; and for the stranger remains from his bequest two; then each one is multiplied by that in the remaining six. So if you want to correct the estate, you make each slave one hundred and fifty‑six shares, because? the stranger's intention... and 'Amr and Zaid half of it and one‑third of it he has no property, he has one‑third of what he owns at death and one‑third for mothers. The remainder for the wife four and for the stranger two shares, so it becomes six and a half, it is broken by half, so double to remove the break, so it becomes thirteen. So if half the wealth becomes upon thirteen, the whole becomes twenty‑six; so multiply the original calculation, that is twelve, by twenty‑six, so it becomes three hundred and fifty‑two? The legatee takes one hundred and four, and the remainder for the wife by her bequest and inheritance, because the stranger first takes two‑thirds of his slave, that is one hundred and four shares; the wife takes a quarter of the remainder, that is two and? one hundred and fifty‑two?; remains one hundred and sixty‑five shares divided among them? three? nine shares of that? three hundred and forty‑eight? for the stranger from his slave bequeathed to him; if you add that to one hundred and four it becomes two hundred and fifty‑two. ... Its origin: that the bequest to the killer is like the bequest to an heir, so it is not permissible except with the permission of the heirs according to Abu Hanifa; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not permissible at all, as will come in its chapter. And if he bequeaths all his wealth to his killer and he has no heirs, and all to a stranger, then the stranger gets one‑third of the wealth and one‑third for the killer, because two‑thirds of the wealth became due to the stranger by a strong bequest, and what is due by a strong bequest invalidates in it the weak bequest in terms of share and entitlement; one‑third of the wealth remains, their two bequests are equal in it, because their bequests beyond the third are weak so they are not executed without the permission of heirs; so if they are equal in the bequest, they are equal in the division. ... And if a woman dies leaving her husband and she bequeaths to a stranger one‑third of her wealth and to her killer all her wealth, then for the husband two‑thirds and the remaining third between the stranger and the killer in thirds? According to Muhammad, the killer gets two shares? and it becomes! all nine? for the stranger first three, for the husband three, for the stranger one share, for the killer two shares; and according to Muhammad the remainder between them in halves, because according to him the killer does not strike against what became due to the husband by inheritance, but only strikes against what remains, which is the third, and similarly the stranger; so the third becomes between them halves, and the division from six: for the stranger half three, for the husband two shares, for the killer one share; and according to Abu Yusuf, the bequest to the killer is not permissible at all, even if he is not an heir, and it is clear that if she has no heir other than the husband, her acknowledgment is valid because the validity of a sick person's acknowledgment to his heir is the right of the remaining heirs, so if they confirm him, the acknowledgment is valid, and the impediment has disappeared due to the non‑existence of the heir for her, so her acknowledgment is valid. And if her husband and a stranger kill her intentionally, then she pardons them both, and she bequeaths to the stranger half her wealth, the bequest is valid and there is no inheritance for the husband because he is her killer, and intentional killing prohibits inheritance; so she becomes like one who has no heir at all, so the bequest to the killer is valid, because the impediment to permissibility of the bequest is the existence of an heir, and she has no heir, so the impediment is absent. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'If he says between Zaid and 'Amr and for Zaid half of it' i.e. if she says one‑third of my wealth between Zaid and 'Amr while 'Amr is dead, then Zaid gets half of the third because the word 'between' necessitates halving, and it does not become complete due to lack of competition, contrary to if he said 'to so‑and‑so and so‑and‑so' and it turns out that one of them is dead, where the living gets the whole third, because the first sentence is a speech that necessitates exclusive application of the ruling, because conjunction necessitates sharing in the ruling.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage from al‑Bahr al‑Rāʾiq is a detailed commentary (sharḥ) on the chapter of bequests from Kanz al‑Daqāʾiq. It explains the legal distinctions based on the wording used in a bequest. The author first contrasts two key phrases: 'between so‑and‑so and so‑and‑so' (using the word 'bayna') versus 'to so‑and‑so and so‑and‑so' (using the preposition 'li'). If the testator says 'one‑third of my wealth between Zayd and ʿAmr' and one of them is dead, the living recipient only gets half of that third, because the word 'bayna' implies sharing and halving by virtue of the wording itself, not due to competition. But if he says 'to Zayd and ʿAmr' with the letter lām, and one is dead, the living recipient takes the entire third, because the lām grants exclusive ownership to each, and the dead person cannot take, so his share falls away, leaving the full third for the living. This distinction is crucial: the cause of the distribution (sharing vs. exclusive grant) changes the outcome. The commentary then covers several special cases: bequeathing to someone and his offspring (invalid because the offspring are non‑existent at the testator's death), bequeathing to a contingent condition (e.g., 'if he is free'), and bequeathing to 'whoever becomes poor' (which only applies to those who fall from wealth to poverty, not the originally poor, citing a hadith). The passage also includes a complex illustration involving a bequest to a wife and a stranger concerning two slaves, with a detailed calculation to correct the shares. Finally, it addresses the bequest to a killer (qātīl). There is an intra‑Hanafi dispute: Imām Abū Ḥanīfa holds that a bequest to a killer is like a bequest to an heir – it requires the permission of the other heirs to be valid. Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad (the Ṣāḥibayn) hold that it is absolutely invalid, even with permission. The commentary gives scenarios where the testator has no heirs besides the killer, and the differences among the three imāms. The passage ends with a reminder that if the testator's death is caused by the killer, the killer is barred from inheritance, so the ban on bequest to an heir is lifted.

Key Terms
بين (bayna): A word used in bequests to indicate sharing/halving between multiple recipients.
الوصية للقاتل (al-wasiyya li-l-qātil): A bequest made to the person who killed the testator.
مزاحمة (muzāḥamah): Competition or conflict among beneficiaries over the bequest amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'I bequeath one-third of my wealth between Zayd and ʿAmr' (using 'bayna') and it turns out that ʿAmr was dead at the time of the bequest, what does Zayd receive?
A) The entire one-third
B) Half of the one-third
C) Nothing, the bequest is void
D) One-third of the one-third

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, the precise wording ('bayna' vs 'li') determines the share of a surviving beneficiary when one is dead, and a bequest to a killer is valid only with the permission of other heirs according to the relied-upon view.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Dividing a Bequest Among Multiple Categories: The Definite Common Noun Principle
Intra-Hanafi dispute on share allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on dividing a bequest among multiple categories and apply the principle of the definite common noun (ism al-jins al-muḥallā bi al-alif wa al-lām) to determine the number of shares.

Core Idea
A definite common noun indicates one minimum; so a bequest to 'the poor' means at least one share.

When a testator bequeaths one-third of the estate to multiple categories such as three ummahat awlad, the poor, and the needy, the method of dividing the one-third among them depends on how many individuals each category represents. This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that each category receives at least one share (fifths), while Muhammad argues for at least two shares per category (sevenths). The disagreement hinges on a subtle principle of Arabic linguistics – the interpretation of the definite common noun (ism al-jins al-muḥallā bi al-alif wa al-lām).

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest scenario and the two positions
The testator bequeaths one-third to three specific ummahat awlad (three individuals), to 'the poor' (al-fuqara), and to 'the needy' (al-masakin). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf divide the one-third into fifths: three shares for the three ummahat awlad, one for the poor, one for the needy. Muhammad divides into sevenths: two shares per category plus three for the ummahat awlad, totaling seven shares.
The dispute is purely about the number of shares, not the validity of the bequest.
2
Analyze the linguistic argument: definite common noun vs plural minimum
Muhammad argues that the plural form (جمع) in inheritance contexts implies a minimum of two, citing Quran 4:11 (إذا كان له اخوة and فوق اثنتين). The Hanafi response distinguishes that the nouns here (الفقراء والمساكين) are definite common nouns (اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام), which indicate the genus as a whole and encompass the minimum possible, which is one. This is like the definite singular noun (e.g., العبد in an oath means one).
The key is whether the noun is definite or indefinite; the Hanafi position applies only to definite nouns.
3
Apply the oath analogy
The Hanafi argument uses the example of an oath: if someone swears not to buy 'the slave' (العبد), he breaks his oath by buying one slave. This shows that the definite common noun indicates a minimum of one, not the whole genus. Similarly, the definite nouns in the bequest (الفقراء, المساكين) each indicate at least one individual.
This analogy strengthens the Hanafi view that the definite form implies a single minimum instantiation.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, if only one poor person and one needy person exist, the bequest is easily divided into fifths. Under Muhammad, each category would require at least two recipients, so if only one exists, the bequest might be problematic or require adjustment. The chosen view (mufta bihi) is the division into fifths.
The dispute affects distribution when a category has fewer than two members.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبثلثه لأمهات أولاده وهن ثلاث وللفقراء والمساكين وأمهات أولاده يقسم الثلث أخماساً فلهن ثلاثة أسهم ولكل طائفة من المساكين والفقراء سهم) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد: يقسم أسباعاً لأن المذكور لفظ الجمع وأدناه في الميراث اثنان قال الله تعالى فإن كان له اخوة فلامه السدس ﴾ [النساء : ١١] وقال فإن كن نساء فوق اثنتين﴾ [النساء : ١١] الآية والمراد بالأثنتين اثنان فكان من كل طائفة اثنان وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة فكان المجموع سبعة فيقسم أسباعاً . قلنا : اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام يتناول الأدنى احتمال الكل كالمفرد المحلى بهما لأنه يراد بهما الجنس إذا لم يكن ثم معهود قال الله تعالى لا يحل لك النساء من بعد ﴾ [الأحزاب : ٥٢] وقال الله تعالى وجعلنا من الماء كل شيء حي ﴾ [الأنبياء : ۳۰] ولا يحتمل ما بينهما فتعين الأدنى لتعذر إرادة الكل، ولهذا لو حلف لا يشتري العبد يحنث بواحد فيتناول من كل فريق واحداً وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة فتبلغ السهام خمسة وليس فيما تلي زيادة على ما ذكر لأن المذكور في الأثنين نكرة وكلامنا في المعرفة حتى لو كان فيما تحن فيه منكراً قلنا كمال قال
He (the author) said: (And with his one-third to his ummahat awlad, and they are three, and to the poor and the needy, and his ummahat awlad, the one-third is divided into fifths: they have three shares, and each group of the needy and the poor has one share.) This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: It is divided into sevenths, because the mentioned word is a plural and its minimum in inheritance is two. Allah said: 'If he has brothers, then for his mother the sixth' [4:11] and He said: 'If they are women above two' [4:11] and the intended by 'two' is two. So from each group there are two, and the ummahat awlad are three, so the total is seven; thus it is divided into sevenths. We said: The definite common noun (ism al-jins al-muhalla bi al-alif wa al-lam) encompasses the minimum with the possibility of the whole, like the definite singular noun, because it is intended for the genus when there is no specific referent. Allah said: 'Women are not lawful for you after that' [33:52] and Allah said: 'And We made from water every living thing' [21:30]. And it does not imply what is between them, so the minimum is determined because intending the whole is impossible. Hence, if someone swore not to buy 'the slave', he would break his oath by buying one. Thus it takes from each group one. The ummahat awlad are three, so the shares reach five. And there is no increase in what follows beyond what was mentioned, because the mentioned in 'two' is indefinite, and our discussion is about the definite. So even if in what we are discussing it were indefinite, we said as he said.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of a bequest of one-third of the estate to three categories: three ummahat awlad (slave mothers of children), the poor, and the needy. The base text (matn) states the division is into fifths: three shares for the ummahat awlad and one each for the poor and needy. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad argues for sevenths: he contends that the minimum of a plural (جمع) in inheritance contexts is two, citing Quranic verses on inheritance (4:11) where 'brothers' implies at least two and 'above two' indicates two. Thus each of the three groups (poor, needy, ummahat awlad) would receive two shares, and with three ummahat awlad that totals seven shares. The Hanafi response (from Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf) is that the definite common noun (اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام) indicates the minimum possible (one), like the definite singular noun. They support this with Quranic verses where the definite form denotes the genus without implying a number. For example, 'women' in 33:52 and 'water' in 21:30. So each group receives at least one share: the ummahat awlad are three specific individuals, so they get three shares, and each of the poor and needy groups gets at least one share, totalling five. The argument is further supported by an oath example: if one swears not to buy 'the slave' (العبد), he breaks his oath by buying one slave, showing the definite singular implies one. Thus the correct division is into fifths.

Key Terms
اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام (ism al-jins al-muḥallā bi al-alif wa al-lām): A common noun defined by the definite article (al-), which indicates the genus without specifying a number; its minimum is one.
أمهات الأولاد (ummahāt al-awlād): Slave women who have born children to their master; they become free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how many shares are used to divide the one-third when bequeathing to three ummahat awlad, the poor, and the needy?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Seven
D) Three

Key Takeaway
A definite common noun in a bequest indicates a minimum of one per category, leading to division into fifths in this case.

Validity of Bequest to Ummahat al-Awlad by Istihsan
Ruling and justification for bequest to umm walad who is a slave at the time of the will, with istihsan overriding qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a bequest to an umm walad by istihsan despite the qiyas to the contrary.

Core Idea
A bequest to an umm walad is valid by istihsan because it takes effect after death when she is free.

This lesson examines a key application of istihsan in Hanafi inheritance law. The bequest (wasiyyah) to an umm walad who is a slave at the time of the will would be invalid by qiyas (analogical reasoning) because a slave cannot own property. However, the Hanafi school permits it by istihsan, considering the testator's intent and the fact that the bequest operates after death when the umm walad becomes free automatically (by being an umm walad). We will trace the reasoning and the response to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the qiyas ruling
Recognize that the umm walad is a slave at will-making, so qiyas would deny validity of property bequest to her. What is the basis of this qiyas?
The qiyas stems from the general rule that a slave cannot own property.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The bequest is suspended on death; at that moment she is free. The testator's intent for a valid bequest indicates the bequest is added to after manumission.
Istihsan overrides qiyas based on the testator's apparent intent.
3
Examine the objection from al-'Inaya
Why is a bequest to a regular slave valid (as bequest of freedom) but to an umm walad invalid by qiyas? Note the distinction.
The objection highlights an apparent inconsistency.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The bequest to a slave is actually a bequest of manumission (one-third of his person); for the umm walad, freedom already occurs by death, so a second cause would conflict.
Thus the umm walad case is different and requires istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هذه الوصية تكون لأمهات أولاده اللاتي يعتقن بموته دون اللاتي عتقن في حياته من أمهات الأولاد لأن الاسم لهن في العرف واللاتي عتقن حال حياته موال لا أمهات أولاده وإنما تصرف إليهن الوصية عند عدم أولئك لعدم من يكون أولى منهن بهذا الاسم، ولا يقال إن الوصية لمملوكه بماله لا تجوز لأن العبد لا يملك شيئاً وإنما يجوز له الوصية بالعتق أو برقبته لكونه عتقاً فوجب أن يكون لأمهات أولاده اللاتي يعتقن حال حياته لأنا نقول : القياس أن لا تجوز الوصية لهن لأنها لو جازت لهن لكنه حال تزول العتق بهن لكون العتق والتمليك معلقاً بالموت والتعليق يقع عليهن وهن إماء فكذا تملكهن يقع وهن إماء وهو لا يجوز إلا أنا جوزناه استحساناً لأن الوصية مضافة إلى ما بعد عتقهن لا حال حلول العتق بهن بدلالة حال الموصي لأن الظاهر من حاله أن يقصد بإيصائه وصية صحيحة لإباطلة، والصحيحة هي المضافة إلى ما بعد عتقهن ؛ كذا عامة في الشروح وعزاه جماعة من الشراح إلى الذخيرة ولعل الإمام قاضيخان والإمام المحبوبي عن هذا فقالا : أما جواز الوصية لأمهات أولاده فلأن أو أن ثبوت الوصية وعملها بعد الموت وهن حرائر بعد الموت فتجوز الوصية لهن كما ذكره صاحب النهاية نقلاً عنهما. ثم قال في العناية : فإن قيل الوصية بثلث المال لعبده جائزة ولا يعتق بعد موته وأم الولد ليست أقل حالاً منه فكيف لم تصح لها الوصية قياساً؟ وأجيب بأن الوصية بثلث المال للعبد إنما جازت لتناوله ثلث رقبته فكانت وصية برقبة إعتاقاً وهو يصح منجزاً ومضافاً بخلاف أم الولد فإن الوصية ليست إعتاقاً لأنها تعتق بموت المولى وإن لم يكن ثمة وصية أصلاً. ولقائل أن يقول الوصية بثلث المال إما أن صادفتها بعد موت المولى وهي حرة أو أمة، فإن كان الأول فلا وجه لنفي القياس، وإن كان الثاني فكذلك لأنها كالعبد الموصى له بثلث المال. والجواب أنها ليست كالعبد لأن عتقها لا بد وأن يكون بموت المولى فلو كان بالوصية أيضاً توارد علتان مستقلتان على معلول واحد بالشخص وهو ثلث رقبتها وذلك باطل؛ إلى هنا لفظ العناية.
Then this bequest is for his ummahat awlad who become free by his death, not those who became free during his life, because the name applies to them customarily. Those who became free in his lifetime are clients (mawali), not ummahat awlad. The bequest is given to them only in the absence of those who are more entitled to this name. And it cannot be said that a bequest to his slave of his property is not valid because a slave does not own anything; rather, a bequest of manumission or of his person is valid because it is manumission. So it must be for his ummahat awlad who become free at his death? We say: Qiyas would dictate that the bequest to them is not valid, because if it were valid, it would occur at the time when manumission occurs for them—since both manumission and ownership are suspended on death, and the suspension falls on them while they are slaves. Similarly, their ownership would occur while they are slaves, which is not valid. However, we have permitted it by istihsan, because the bequest is added to the time after their manumission, not at the time of manumission, as indicated by the testator's circumstances, for it is apparent that he intends a valid bequest, not an invalid one. A valid bequest is one added to after their manumission. This is widespread in the commentaries, and a group of commentators attribute it to al-Dhakhira. Perhaps Imam Qadikhan and Imam al-Mahbubi said: As for the permissibility of a bequest to his ummahat awlad, it is because the bequest is established and operative after death, and they are free after death, so the bequest is valid for them, as mentioned by the author of al-Nihaya quoting them. Then it is said in al-'Inaya: If it is said: 'A bequest of one-third of the wealth to his slave is valid, and he does not become free after his death, whereas the umm walad is not less in status than him; so how is the bequest not valid for her by qiyas?' The answer is: The bequest of one-third of the wealth to the slave is valid only because it encompasses one-third of his person, so it is a bequest of his person as manumission, which is valid whether immediate or delayed, unlike the umm walad, because the bequest is not manumission, since she becomes free by the master's death even if there is no bequest at all. One might say: The bequest of one-third of the wealth either meets her after the master's death while she is free or while she is a slave. If the first, there is no basis to reject qiyas. If the second, then similar, because she is like the slave who is bequeathed one-third of the wealth. The answer is that she is not like the slave, because her manumission must occur by the master's death; if it were also by the bequest, two independent causes would converge on one specific effect, namely one-third of her person, and that is invalid. Up to here is the wording of al-'Inaya.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a bequest (وصية) to an umm walad (a slave mother of children) who is still a slave at the time the will is made. The issue: Since she does not own property at that time, qiyas (analogical reasoning) would suggest the bequest is invalid, as a bequest to a slave is generally not valid for property (slaves cannot own). However, the Hanafi school permits it by istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning: The bequest takes effect after the testator's death, at which point the umm walad becomes free automatically (by being an umm walad). Thus the bequest is considered to be made to a free person. The istihsan is based on the testator's apparent intent to make a valid bequest. The text also addresses an objection from al-'Inaya: Why is a bequest to a regular slave (who does not become free) valid, but to an umm walad it would be invalid by qiyas? The answer distinguishes: a bequest to a slave is effectively a bequest of freedom (the slave's person is part of the bequest), while for an umm walad, freedom already occurs by death, so a second cause would conflict. Thus the bequest to an umm walad is valid by istihsan.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon the master's death and cannot be sold.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of legal reasoning that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome based on stronger evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a bequest to an umm walad valid by istihsan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because she is already free at the time of the will
B) Because the bequest takes effect after death when she is free
C) Because she can own property as a slave
D) Because the bequest is considered manumission

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a bequest to an umm walad by istihsan, overriding qiyas, because the bequest takes effect after death when she is free.

Division of One-Third with Two Ummahāt al-Awlād
Clarification of share division when number of ummahat awlad is two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of shares when a testator bequeaths one-third to two ummahat awlad along with the poor and needy, and explain the principle behind the division.

Core Idea
Two ummahat awlad receive two shares out of four, not five.

This passage clarifies the division of a one-third bequest when the number of ummahat awlad is two instead of three. The earlier matn specified a five-share division for three ummahat awlad; here the commentator shows that the number of shares adjusts proportionally, maintaining the principle that each beneficiary group receives at least one share and additional ummahat awlad add to their share count.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to two ummahat awlad (slave mothers of his children), the poor, and the needy. These are four beneficiary groups.
All groups receive an equal base share.
2
Determine total shares
Since there are two ummahat awlad, they receive two shares. The poor and needy each receive one share. Total shares = 2 (umahat) + 1 (poor) + 1 (needy) = 4 shares.
The one-third is divided into four equal parts.
3
Assign shares
Each of the two ummahat awlad gets one share (total two), the poor gets one, and the needy gets one. Thus each receives 1/4 of the one-third.
This follows from the principle that each group gets a minimum of one share, and the number of ummahat awlad determines their share count.
4
Compare with three ummahat awlad
If there were three ummahat awlad, they would receive three shares, plus one each for the poor and needy, totaling five shares. The number of shares increases with the number of ummahat awlad.
The base minimum (one share each for poor and needy) remains constant; only the ummahat awlad share count changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر قوله «وهن ثلاثة أنهن لو كن ثنتين يقسم المال على أربعة لهن
And it is apparent from his saying 'and they are three' that if they were two, the wealth would be divided into four for them.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This brief statement clarifies the previous ruling. The matn specified that the three ummahat awlad receive three shares out of five. Here, the commentator notes that if there were only two ummahat awlad, the division would be into fourths: two shares for them, one for the poor, and one for the needy, totaling four shares. This follows logically from the same principle: each group gets one share as a minimum, and the number of ummahat awlad determines their shares.

Key Terms
أمهات الأولاد (ummahāt al-awlād): Slave mothers of a free man's children who become free upon his death; here, they are beneficiaries of a bequest.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will; the ruling here pertains to the division of a one-third bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third to two ummahat awlad, the poor, and the needy, into how many shares is the one-third divided?
A) Five
B) Four
C) Seven
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The number of shares in a one-third bequest to ummahat awlad and other fixed categories equals the number of ummahat awlad plus two (one each for the poor and needy).

Bequests to Specific Groups: Conditions for Validity
Rulings on bequests to various groups with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on bequests to various groups and apply the condition that the group must be defined or needy.

Core Idea
A bequest to a group is valid only if the group is clearly defined or predominantly in need.

Bequests to general categories of people raise the question of who exactly receives. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position: a bequest to a broad group like 'jurists' is invalid unless the group is either specified or its members are in need. In this lesson, we will parse the various rulings and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups
List each group mentioned in the text: children of the Prophet, Alids, Shi'a, lovers of the family, jurists, scholars of hadith, students of knowledge. For each, note the ruling given.
Pay attention to how the ruling changes with qualifiers like 'poor' or 'Alid jurists'.
2
Extract the condition for validity
For each ruling, determine what makes the bequest valid or invalid. The key factors are: (a) the group is well-defined and countable (e.g., children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn), or (b) the group is predominantly poor (e.g., teachers in a mosque).
The text uses the principle that if poverty is predominant, the ruling is based on need as if it were stipulated.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on distributing to a single poor individual. Note the underlying reasoning: Abu Yusuf allows it because the bequest is for the poor; Muhammad requires distribution to at least two because the bequest is to a group.
This shows how the same principle (need vs. group identity) can lead to different conclusions.
4
Apply the principle to a new case
Given a bequest to 'students of knowledge' in a town where most students are poor, decide if it is valid. According to the text, it is valid based on the analogy from teachers in a mosque.
This illustrates the importance of factual determination of whether the group is predominantly needy.

Source Text

And if he bequeathed to the children of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), and to the Alids, and to the Shi'a, and to the lovers of the children of the Messenger of God, and to the jurists, and to the scholars of hadith. The jurist Abu Ja'far was asked about a man who bequeathed to the children of the Messenger of God. Abu Nasr ibn Yahya mentioned he used to say: The bequest is for the children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn, not for others. As for the Alids, do they enter into this bequest? Because al-Hasan (may God be pleased with him) had a daughter married to a descendant of 'Umar (may God be pleased with them). And if he bequeathed to the Alids, it has been narrated from the jurist Abu Ja'far that it is not valid because they are not countable and this name does not indicate poverty or need. If he bequeathed to the jurists of the Alids, it is valid. On this, a bequest to jurists generally is not valid, but if to their poor, it is valid. It has been narrated from some of our shaykhs that an endowment (waqf) for a teacher in the mosque who teaches children there is valid, because most of them are poor, and the poor are predominant among them, so the ruling is based on the predominance of poverty as if it were stipulated. And Shaykh al-Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The Judge Imam used to say on this analogy: if he bequeaths to students of knowledge of a town or to such-and-such students of knowledge, it is valid. And if the executor gives to one of the poor students or to one of the poor Alids, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, it is not valid unless he distributes to two or more. And if he bequeaths to the Shi'a and the lovers of the family of Muhammad residing in such-and-such a town, know that in reality every Muslim is a Shi'a and a lover of the family of the Messenger of God, and nothing else is valid in their religion. But as for what the testator intended, his intention is those who are known to incline towards them and are marked by that.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on bequests to various groups. The key principles: (1) A bequest to the 'children of the Prophet' is generally restricted to the descendants of al-Hasan and al-Husayn. (2) A bequest to 'Alids' (العلوية) is invalid if the group is indefinite or does not indicate poverty; but if restricted to 'jurists of the Alids' or 'poor of the Alids', it may be valid. (3) A bequest to 'jurists' alone is not valid (since it is too general and does not imply need), but to 'poor jurists' is valid. (4) By analogy, bequests to 'students of knowledge' are valid if the group is predominantly poor. (5) There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on whether the executor can give to just one poor person: Abu Yusuf allows it, Muhammad requires at least two. (6) For bequests to 'Shi'a and lovers of the family of Muhammad' residing in a specific place, the intended meaning is those who are distinctively known as such, even though all Muslims love the family in principle.

Key Terms
العلوية (al-‘Alawiyyah): Descendants of Ali ibn Abi Talib (excluding the children of Fatima? The text mentions children of al-Hasan and al-Husayn, so Alids may include other descendants of Ali).
الشيعة (al-Shī‘ah): Here, those who are known for their attachment to the family of the Prophet, distinct from the general Muslim population.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest to a general group hinges on the group being either countable or predominantly needy.

Validity of Bequest to Ummahat al-Awlad
Ruling with proof on bequest to ummahat al-awlad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests to ummahat al-awlad and explain the proof based on the timing of the will and their freedom after death.

Core Idea
A bequest to an umm walad is valid because the will takes effect after death, when she is already free.

In this passage, the author addresses a specific point of inheritance law: whether a master can validly bequeath part of his estate to his umm walad (mother of his child). Some early Hanafi jurists questioned its validity by analogy to a bequest to a slave. This lesson unpacks the debate and the reasoning that leads to the established Hanafi position of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the explicit statement of the Hanafi position: bequest to ummahat al-awlad is valid. Note the condition: the will must be muḍāfah (deferred) to after death.
The ruling is found in the first lines: 'الصحيحة هي المضافة إلى ما بعد عتقهن' – the valid will is that which is added to after their freedom.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The proof is that the will operates after death, at which time the umm walad is free (because she becomes free upon the master's death). Therefore, the bequest is to a free person, which is valid.
The text says: 'لأن ثبوت الوصية وعملها بعد الموت وهن حرائر بعد الموت فتجوز الوصية لهن'.
3
Trace the rebuttal of the opposing analogy
The opposing view analogized the umm walad to a slave, arguing that a bequest to a slave is valid only because it is an emancipation, but an umm walad does not need emancipation. The text refutes this by showing that the bequest to an umm walad is not an emancipation; she is already free by death, so the two causes (death and will) cannot both effect freedom on the same portion.
The answer from al-Inayah: 'فالوصية ليست إعتاقاً لأنها تعتق بموت المولى وإن لم يكن ثمة وصية أصلاً'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf
Some earlier Hanafis (Qadikhan, al-Mahbubi) held it invalid, but the later relied-upon view (al-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah) is validity. The Nawadir narration from Abu Yusuf also supports inclusion of ummahat al-awlad in bequests to mawālī.
The text cites al-Nihāyah and al-ʿInāyah to affirm the majority position.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf)
If the bequest is invalid, the share reverts to the general estate; if valid, the umm walad receives her bequest. The relied-upon view is validity, so she takes the bequest.
This is important for estate distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من حاله أن يقصد بإيصائه وصية صحيحة لإباطلة، والصحيحة هي المضافة إلى ما بعد عتقهن ؛ كذا عامة في الشروح وعزاه جماعة من الشراح إلى الذخيرة ولعل الإمام قاضيخان والإمام المحبوبي عن هذا فقالا : أما جواز الوصية لأمهات أولاده فلأن أو أن ثبوت الوصية وعملها بعد الموت وهن حرائر بعد الموت فتجوز الوصية لهن كما ذكره صاحب النهاية نقلاً عنهما. ثم قال في العناية : فإن قيل الوصية بثلث المال لعبده جائزة ولا يعتق بعد موته وأم الولد ليست أقل حالاً منه فكيف لم تصح لها الوصية قياساً؟ وأجيب بأن الوصية بثلث المال للعبد إنما جازت لتناوله ثلث رقبته فكانت وصية برقبة إعتاقاً وهو يصح منجزاً ومضافاً بخلاف أم الولد فإن الوصية ليست إعتاقاً لأنها تعتق بموت المولى وإن لم يكن ثمة وصية أصلاً. ولقائل أن يقول الوصية بثلث المال إما أن صادفتها بعد موت المولى وهي حرة أو أمة، فإن كان الأول فلا وجه لنفي القياس، وإن كان الثاني فكذلك لأنها كالعبد الموصى له بثلث المال. والجواب أنها ليست كالعبد لأن عتقها لا بد وأن يكون بموت المولى فلو كان بالوصية أيضاً توارد علتان مستقلتان على معلول واحد بالشخص وهو ثلث رقبتها وذلك باطل؛ إلى هنا لفظ العناية. وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف ولو أوصى لأمهات أولاده بألف ولمواليه بألف وله أمهات أولاد عتقن في حياته ومواليات اعتبر كل فريق على حدة، ولو أوصى بثلث ماله لمواليه ولم يذكر أمهات الأولاد دخلت أمهات الأولاد في الوصية.
From his condition that he intends by his will a valid will for invalidation, and the valid one is that which is added to after their freedom; thus it is common in the commentaries and a group of commentators attributed it to al-Dhakhirah. Perhaps Imam Qadikhan and Imam al-Mahbubi said about this: As for the validity of the bequest to mothers of children, because the establishment of the will and its operation is after death, and they are free after death, so the bequest to them is valid, as mentioned by the author of al-Nihayah quoting them. Then he said in al-Inayah: If it is said: The bequest of one-third of the wealth to his slave is valid, and he is not freed after his death, and the umm walad is not lesser in status than him, so why is the bequest not valid for her by analogy? And it was answered that the bequest of one-third of the wealth to the slave is permitted only because it includes one-third of his person, so it is a bequest of emancipation, which is valid whether immediate or deferred, unlike the umm walad, for the bequest to her is not emancipation because she is freed by the death of her master even if there is no will at all. And it may be said: The bequest of one-third of the wealth either finds her after the master's death as free or as a slave. If the first, then there is no basis for negating the analogy; if the second, then likewise because she is like a slave to whom one-third of the wealth is bequeathed. The answer is that she is not like a slave because her freedom must be by the master's death, so if it were also by the will, two independent causes would apply to a single effect, namely one-third of her person, and that is invalid. Up to here is the wording of al-Inayah. And in Nawadir Bishr from Abu Yusuf: If one bequeaths to his ummahat awlad a thousand and to his mawali a thousand, and he has ummahat awlad who were freed during his life and mawaliyat, each group is considered separately. And if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to his mawali and does not mention the ummahat al-awlad, the ummahat al-awlad are included in the bequest.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof discussing the validity of bequests to ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children). The discussion arises because some early jurists held that a bequest to an umm walad is invalid, citing a narration that a bequest to one's own slave is invalid unless permitted by the master, but umm walad is like a slave. The author presents the correct Hanafi position: bequests to ummahat al-awlad are valid. The proof is that the will takes effect after death, at which point they are free (since umm walad becomes free upon the master's death), and a free person can receive a bequest. The objection that a bequest to a slave is valid only because it includes emancipation, while an umm walad does not need emancipation, is answered by noting that the bequest is valid because she is free at the time the will operates. The discussion from al-Inayah refutes the qiyas to a slave, arguing that two independent causes (death and will) cannot both effect freedom on the same portion. The Nawadir narration from Abu Yusuf provides a specific case: if one bequeaths separately to ummahat awlad and mawali, each group is considered separately; if only mawali are mentioned, ummahat al-awlad are included because they are also mawali in a sense. The authority weight: the main discussion is from al-Inayah and al-Dhakhirah, which are later commentaries, but the position is consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah (umm walad becomes free upon death).

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, thus gaining the status of being freed upon the master's death.
الوصية المضافة (al-wasiyyah al-mudafah): A will that is conditioned on a future event, such as after the death of the testator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she is a free person at the time the will is written.
B) Because she becomes free upon the master's death, so the will operates when she is free.
C) Because the master can emancipate her through the will.
D) Because she is considered a separate legal entity from the master.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an umm walad is valid because the will operates after death when she is free, and the analogy to a slave fails due to the distinct nature of her freedom.
