Division of Third and Partnership in Bequests
Matn and commentary on bequest partnership calculations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of a legatee who is made a partner in a bequest, distinguishing between equal and unequal bequests, and state the intra-Hanafi disagreement on slave girls.

Core Idea
Partnership implies equality; the partner's share depends on equality of original bequests and divisibility of items.

This lesson involves parsing a passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that lays out rules for when a testator adds a third person as a partner to existing bequests. The rulings hinge on the linguistic meaning of 'shirkah' (partnership) which implies equality, and on the Hanafi position regarding division of slaves. Understanding these calculations is essential for correctly distributing bequests in cases of multiple legatees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of partnership (al-shirkah)
The text states that partnership linguistically implies equality (al-musawat). This principle is used to interpret the testator's statement 'I make you a partner with them'.
The Quranic verse 'they are partners in the third' (4:12) is cited as supporting this equality.
2
Apply to equal bequests
When the original bequests are equal (e.g., 100 each), the third person gets one-third from each. The result is that he receives two-thirds of one of the bequest amounts (e.g., 66.66).
The text's phrase 'فتم له ثلثا المائة' may be a copyist error; the standard ruling is one-third from each.
3
Apply to unequal bequests
When the original bequests are unequal (e.g., 400 and 200), the third person gets half from each, receiving 200 from the first and 100 from the second, totaling 300.
Equality cannot be established among all three due to disparity, so the partner is made equal with each legatee separately.
4
Analyze the slave girl case
If bequests are slave girls of equal value, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa gives half each (considering slaves indivisible), while the two companions give one-third each (treating them like dirhams). If values differ, consensus gives half each.
This derives from Abu Hanifa's view that division of slaves (qismat al-raqiq) is invalid.
5
Distinguish between matn and commentary
The commentary from al-Inayah notes that the author's ruling (one-third for the partner in equal bequests) is istihsan; by qiyas, he should get half of each hundred because partnership implies equality.
The commentator points out the underlying legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وبثلثه لزيد وللمساكين لزيد نصفه ولهم نصفه) أي إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد والمساكين كان لزيد النصف وللمساكين النصف وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد ثلثه لفلان وثلثاه للمساكين وقد بينا مأخذ كل واحد من الفريقين قال رحمه الله : (وبمائة لرجل وبمائة لآخر فقال لآخر اشركتك معهما له ثلث ما لكل منهما وبأربعمائة له وبمائتين لآخر فقال لآخر أشركتك معهما له نصف ما لكل واحد منهما يعني إذا أوصى لرجل بمائة درهم ولآخر بمائة ثم قال لآخر قد أشركتك معهما فله ثلث كل مائة ولو أوصى لرجل بأربعمائة درهم ولآخر بمائتين ثم قال لآخر قد أشركتك معهما كان له نصف ما لكل واحد منهما لأن الشركة للمساواة لغة ولهذا حمل قوله تعالى فهم شركاء في الثلث [النساء: ١٢] على المساواة وقد أمكن إثبات المساواة بين الكل في الأول لاستواء المالين فيأخذ هو من كل واحد منهما ثلث المائة فتم له ثلثا المائة ويأخذ من كل واحد منهما ثلثي المائة ولا يمكن المساواة بين الكل في الثانية لتفاوت المالين فحملناه على مساواة الثالث مع كل واحد منهما بما سماه له فيأخذ النصف من كل واحد من المالين. ولو أوصى لرجل بجارية ولآخر بجارية أخرى ثم قال لآخر أشركتك معهما، فإن كانت قيمة الجاريتين متفاوتة له نصف كل واحدة منهما بالإجماع، وإن كانت قيمتهما على السواء فله ثلث كل واحدة منهما عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة له نصف كل واحدة منهما بناء على أنه لا يرى قسمة الرقيق فيكونان كجنسين مختلفين وهما يريانها فصار كالدراهم المتساوية. ولو أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ثم قال لآخر أشركتك أو أدخلتك أو جعلتك معه فالثلث بينهما لما ذكرنا . قال صاحب العناية : وما ذكره المؤلف استحسان والقياس له نصف كل مائة لأن لفظ الاشتراك يقتضي التسوية عند الإطلاق قال
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And with his third to Zayd and to the poor: for Zayd half of it and for them half of it). Meaning: if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd and the poor, then Zayd gets half and the poor get half. This is according to the two companions; according to Muhammad, one-third to so-and-so and two-thirds to the poor, and we have explained the reasoning of each of the two groups. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And with one hundred to a man and one hundred to another, then he said to another: I have made you a partner with them: he gets one-third of what each has; and with four hundred to him and two hundred to another, then he said to another: I have made you a partner with them: he gets half of what each has). Meaning: if one bequeaths to a man one hundred dirhams and to another one hundred, then says to a third: I have made you a partner with them, he gets one-third of every hundred. And if one bequeaths to a man four hundred dirhams and to another two hundred, then says to another: I have made you a partner with them, he gets half of what each has. Because partnership implies equality linguistically, and for this reason the verse 'they are partners in the third' [4:12] is interpreted as equality. And it is possible to establish equality among all in the first case because the two amounts are equal, so he takes from each one-third of the hundred, making for him two-thirds of a hundred? Actually the text: 'فيأخذ هو من كل واحد منهما ثلث المائة فتم له ثلثا المائة ويأخذ من كل واحد منهما ثلثي المائة' seems garbled. Correct reading: In the first case, the two bequests are equal (100 each), so the third person shares equally with each original legatee, taking one-third from each, resulting in him having two-thirds of 100? But the text says 'فتم له ثلثا المائة' which is contradictory. Actually the meaning: The third person gets one-third from each of the two, so he gets two-thirds of one of the hundreds? But then each original legatee gets two-thirds of his original hundred? That does not sum to 300. There is likely a textual corruption. In the standard Hanafi texts, when bequests are equal, the third person shares equally, so he gets one-third of each bequest, i.e., one-third of 100 from each, total 66.66, and the original legatees each get 66.66, summing to 200. But the text as scanned is problematic. The second case: amounts are 400 and 200, so not equal; the third person gets half of each, i.e., 200 from the first and 100 from the second, total 300, and the original legatees retain 200 and 100 respectively, summing to 600? Actually total bequest is 600 (400+200), but the third is one-third of the estate? The matn seems to assume the bequests are from the third. Anyway, the text continues: And if one bequeaths to a man a slave girl and to another a slave girl, then says to another: I have made you a partner with them. If the values of the two slave girls are different, he gets half of each by consensus. If their values are equal, then according to the two companions he gets one-third of each, and according to Abu Hanifa he gets half of each, based on his view that division of slaves is not valid, so they are considered like different types, while they consider it valid, so it becomes like equal dirhams. And if one bequeaths to a man one-third of his wealth and then says to another: I have made you a partner or I have included you or I have made you with him, then the third is between them, as we mentioned. The author of al-Inayah said: What the author mentioned is istihsan, and the qiyas is that he gets half of every hundred because the word partnership implies equality when unqualified.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a parsing_exercise of the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first ruling: if one bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd and to the poor, the division is half each according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (calling them al-Sahibayn), but Muhammad al-Shaybani in his own view (as stated earlier) gives one-third to Zayd and two-thirds to the poor. The author then explains the reasoning, which is not fully quoted. The second ruling: when someone makes a bequest of specific amounts to two people, then says to a third 'I have made you a partner with them,' the share of the third depends on whether the bequests are equal or not. If equal (100 each), he gets one-third from each, so he ends up with two-thirds of the amount of one bequest? The text is mathematically confusing. However, the principle is that partnership implies equality. The third person is treated as a partner with each original legatee separately. When the amounts are equal, the partnership yields a share of one-third from each, but the total to the third is two-thirds of 100? Actually the standard rule: The third person's share is calculated by treating him as an additional legatee sharing equally with each. For equal bequests, the total number of legatees becomes 3 for each share, so each gets one-third of the original bequest amount. So the third gets 33.33 from each, total 66.66, and each original gets 66.66, summing to 200. The text says 'فتم له ثلثا المائة' which might be a copyist error for 'فتم له ثلثمائة'? Unclear. In the unequal case (400 and 200), partnership yields half from each: he gets 200+100=300, and each original gets 200 and 100 respectively. The next case involves bequests of slave girls: if values differ, consensus gives half each; if equal, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa gives half each (considering slaves indivisible, so each bequest is a distinct type), while the two companions give one-third each (treating them as divisible like dirhams). The final case: if one bequeaths a third to one person and then says to another 'I share you with him,' the third is divided equally between them. The author of al-Inayah notes that the author's ruling (giving one-third to the third when bequests are equal) is istihsan; by qiyas, he should get half of each hundred because partnership implies equality.

Key Terms
الشركة (al-shirkah): Partnership; here refers to the testator declaring a third person a partner in the bequest made to others.
قسمة الرقيق (qismat al-raqiq): Division of slaves as property; Abu Hanifa considers it invalid because slaves are not divisible in fractions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if someone bequeaths 400 dirhams to Zayd and 200 dirhams to 'Amr, then says to Bakr: 'I have made you a partner with them,' what share does Bakr receive from each bequest?
A) One-third from each
B) Half from each
C) Two-thirds from each
D) The same as the smaller bequest

Key Takeaway
When a testator adds a partner to a bequest, the partner's share is determined by the principle of equality, with detailed rules for equal and unequal amounts and for divisible versus indivisible items.

Definition of 'Ahl al-Ilm' and 'Ashab al-Hadith' in Bequests
Defines who qualifies as 'people of knowledge' or 'hadith scholars' in a bequest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'ahl al-ilm' and 'ashab al-hadith' in the context of bequests and apply it to classify who is included or excluded.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'people of knowledge' means only fuqaha and muhaddithun—not philosophers or theologians.

When a testator leaves a bequest to a category of people, the exact scope of that category must be determined by Islamic legal usage. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq clarifies that in Hanafi law, 'ahl al-ilm' (people of knowledge) is restricted to jurists and hadith scholars, excluding those who study philosophy or speculative theology. Similarly, 'ashab al-hadith' (hadith scholars) refers specifically to those who actively read and seek hadith, regardless of their madhhab. Understanding these definitions is essential for correctly executing the testator's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories in the bequest
The passage discusses two different bequests: one to 'people of knowledge of a town' and another to 'poor students of knowledge from among the hadith scholars'. Note how each category is defined.
2
Determine the inclusions and exclusions for 'ahl al-ilm'
According to the Hanafi school, 'ahl al-ilm' includes fuqaha (jurists) and muhaddithun (hadith scholars). It explicitly excludes those who study philosophy (hikmah). Based on analogy from Abu al-Qasim, theologians (mutakallimun) are also excluded.
The text from al-Khaniyah leaves some ambiguity about students of legal rulings and theologians, but the analogy resolves it.
3
Define 'ashab al-hadith'
For the bequest to 'hadith scholars', the term includes those who read, listen, and seek hadith, regardless of their madhhab. A Shafi'i who does not engage in hadith is not included.
This definition is independent of one's fiqh affiliation.
4
Apply the definitions to hypothetical scenarios
Consider whether a philosopher, a theologian, a Hanafi jurist, or a Shafi'i who only studies fiqh would be included under each bequest. This reinforces the practical implications.
The key is the testator's likely intent based on legal custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى لأهل العلم ببلدة كذا فإنه يدخل فيه أهل الفقه وأهل الحديث ولا يدخل فيه من يتعلم الحكمة وفي الخانية : وهل يدخل فيه من يتعلم الحكم؟ وهل يدخل فيه المتكلمون؟ لا ذكر فيه. وعن أبي القاسم : فعلى قياس هذه المسألة لا يدخل في الوصية المتكلمون. وإذا أوصى بثلث ماله لفقراء طلبه العلم من أصحاب الحديث الذين يختلفون إلى مدرسة منسوبة في كورة كذا لا يدخل متعلموا الفقه إذا لم يكونوا من جملة أصحاب الحديث ويتناول من يقرأ الأحاديث . ويكون في طلب ذلك، سواء كان ويسمع شافعي المذهب أو حنفي المذهب أو غير ذلك، ومن كان شافعي المذهب إلا أنه لا يقرأ الأحاديث ولا يسمع ولا يكون في طلب ذلك لا يتناوله اسم أصحاب الحديث.
And if he bequeaths to the people of knowledge of such a town, then it includes jurists and hadith scholars, and it does not include one who learns philosophy. In al-Khaniyah: Does it include one who learns legal rulings (al-hukm)? And does it include the theologians (mutakallimun)? There is no mention of it. From Abu al-Qasim: So by analogy on this issue, theologians are not included in the bequest. And if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the poor students of knowledge from among the hadith scholars who attend a school affiliated with a particular district, then students of fiqh are not included if they are not part of the hadith scholars. It includes one who reads hadith and is seeking it, whether he is Shafi'i or Hanafi or other, and one who is Shafi'i but does not read hadith nor listen nor seek it is not included by the term 'hadith scholars'.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses how to interpret bequests made to categories of people. When a testator bequeaths to 'people of knowledge' of a town, the Hanafi school clarifies that this includes jurists (fuqaha) and hadith scholars (muhaddithun), but excludes those who study philosophy (hikmah) or speculative theology (kalam). The text notes from al-Khaniyah that there is no explicit mention about students of legal rulings or theologians, but based on a statement from Abu al-Qasim, theologians are analogically excluded. Similarly, if the bequest is specifically to 'poor students of knowledge from among the hadith scholars' who attend a particular school, then fiqh students are not included unless they actively engage in hadith study. The term 'hadith scholars' (ashab al-hadith) specifically refers to those who read, listen, and seek hadith, regardless of their madhhab (Shafi'i, Hanafi, etc.). A Shafi'i who does not read or seek hadith is not included by that term.

Key Terms
أهل العلم (ahl al-ilm): People of religious knowledge; specifically jurists and hadith scholars in the context of bequests.
أصحاب الحديث (ashab al-hadith): Hadith scholars who actively read and seek hadith, regardless of madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a bequest to 'people of knowledge' of a town, which of the following is NOT included according to the Hanafi school?
A) Jurists (fuqaha)
B) Hadith scholars (muhaddithun)
C) Philosophers learning wisdom (hikmah)
D) Theologians (mutakallimun) are not included by analogy

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'ahl al-ilm' in bequests means only fuqaha and muhaddithun, and 'ashab al-hadith' means those who actively study hadith, regardless of madhhab.

Bequeathing One-Third to Zayd and the Poor: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on dividing a bequest to a named person and the poor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a bequest to a named person and the poor jointly, and identify the difference between the views of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
A bequest to a named person and the poor divides the third equally according to the two Imams; Muhammad gives the poor two-thirds.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a specific wrinkle in the law of bequests (wasiyyah). When a testator leaves one-third of his estate to a named individual and the poor jointly, there is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. The relied-upon ruling is that the bequest is split equally, but Imam Muhammad offers a different distribution. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists balance textual indications and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the matn ruling
Read the matn: 'And with one-third to Zayd and to the poor: for Zayd half of it, and for them half of it.' This is the ruling stated in the base text.
The matn presents a clear equal split.
2
Recognize the authority behind the matn
The sharh clarifies that this ruling is according to 'the two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Note that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees.
'The two' (الصاحبان) refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Contrast Muhammad's opposing view
According to Muhammad, Zayd gets one-third of the bequested third and the poor get two-thirds. This is a significant shift in distribution.
Muhammad's view gives Zayd less, the poor more.
4
Understand the practical difference
Compute the shares as fractions of the entire estate. Under the two: Zayd gets 1/6, poor get 1/6. Under Muhammad: Zayd gets 1/9, poor get 2/9.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual portion each recipient receives.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The matn states the view of the two, and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Al-Marghinani's inclusion as the matn indicates tarjih.
Mufta bihi: Zayd gets half of the bequested third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وبثلثه لزيد وللمساكين لزيد نصفه ولهم نصفه) أي إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد والمساكين كان لزيد النصف وللمساكين النصف وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد ثلثه لفلان وثلثاه للمساكين وقد بينا مأخذ كل واحد من الفريقين
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And with one-third of his wealth to Zayd and to the poor: for Zayd half of it, and for them half of it) meaning if he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to Zayd and the poor, Zayd gets half and the poor get half. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, one-third of it is for so-and-so (Zayd) and two-thirds for the poor. And we have already explained the basis of each of the two groups.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of a bequest of one-third of the estate to a named individual (Zayd) and to the poor collectively. The matn states the ruling that Zayd receives half and the poor receive half of that one-third. The sharh clarifies that this ruling is according to 'the two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that Zayd should receive only one-third of the bequested third and the poor two-thirds. The author notes that the basis for each view has been explained earlier in the text. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is the one stated in the matn and considered stronger. This dispute affects the actual shares: under the first view, Zayd gets 1/6 of the estate, and the poor get 1/6; under Muhammad's view, Zayd gets 1/9, and the poor get 2/9.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum fraction that can be bequeathed.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest made after death, executed from one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the bequest of one-third to Zayd and the poor, how much does Zayd receive according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)?
A) One-third of the estate
B) Half of the bequested one-third (i.e., 1/6 of the estate)
C) Two-thirds of the bequested one-third
D) The entire one-third

Key Takeaway
In a bequest of one-third to a named person and the poor, the Hanafi mufta bihi is equal division, with each receiving half of that one-third.

Partnership Bequests: Equal and Unequal Amounts
Explains calculation of shares in partnership bequests with equal/unequal amounts and a slave‑girl dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of a third party added to bequests of equal and unequal amounts, and explain how the Hanafi principle of istihsan overrides strict qiyas in these cases.

Core Idea
Partnership implies equality: when bequest amounts are equal, the third gets one‑third from each; when unequal, the third gets half from each.

In this passage, al-Marghinani explains how to compute a third person’s share when a testator adds him as a partner to existing bequests. The key is the linguistic implication of partnership (shirkah) which demands equality (musawah). The ruling differs depending on whether the original bequests are equal or unequal, and the author notes that his ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) overriding strict qiyas (analogy).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testator saying 'I have made you a partner with them' after bequeathing to others. The ruling is that the third person receives a calculated share based on equality.
2
Locate the dalil
The verse 'they are partners in the third' (Quran 4:12) is cited to support that partnership implies equality.
The word 'shuraka' is interpreted as requiring equal shares.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'shuraka' indicates that partners share equally by default. This is applied to the bequests.
However, when the original amounts are unequal, absolute equality is impossible, so the equality is redefined as the third taking half of each bequest.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
In the case of two slave-girls of equal value, Abu Hanifa gives the third half of each, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad give one‑third of each.
The difference stems from whether division of slaves is permitted (the two) or not (Abu Hanifa).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The matn adopts the view of the two (one‑third from each) for the slave‑girl case, making it the mufta bihi position.
The author of al‑‘Inayah states that the ruling is based on istihsan, not qiyas.

قال رحمه الله : (وبمائة لرجل وبمائة لآخر فقال لآخر اشركتك معهما له ثلث ما لكل منهما وبأربعمائة له وبمائتين لآخر فقال لآخر أشركتك معهما له نصف ما لكل واحد منهما يعني إذا أوصى لرجل بمائة درهم ولآخر بمائة ثم قال لآخر قد أشركتك معهما فله ثلث كل مائة ولو أوصى لرجل بأربعمائة درهم ولآخر بمائتين ثم قال لآخر قد أشركتك معهما كان له نصف ما لكل واحد منهما لأن الشركة للمساواة لغة ولهذا حمل قوله تعالى فهم شركاء في الثلث [النساء: ١٢] على المساواة وقد أمكن إثبات المساواة بين الكل في الأول لاستواء المالين فيأخذ هو من كل واحد منهما ثلث المائة فتم له ثلثا المائة ويأخذ من كل واحد منهما ثلثي المائة ولا يمكن المساواة بين الكل في الثانية لتفاوت المالين فحملناه على مساواة الثالث مع كل واحد منهما بما سماه له فيأخذ النصف من كل واحد من المالين. ولو أوصى لرجل بجارية ولآخر بجارية أخرى ثم قال لآخر أشركتك معهما، فإن كانت قيمة الجاريتين متفاوتة له نصف كل واحدة منهما بالإجماع، وإن كانت قيمتهما على السواء فله ثلث كل واحدة منهما عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة له نصف كل واحدة منهما بناء على أنه لا يرى قسمة الرقيق فيكونان كجنسين مختلفين وهما يريانها فصار كالدراهم المتساوية. ولو أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ثم قال لآخر أشركتك أو أدخلتك أو جعلتك معه فالثلث بينهما لما ذكرنا . قال صاحب العناية : وما ذكره المؤلف استحسان والقياس له نصف كل مائة لأن لفظ الاشتراك يقتضي التسوية عند الإطلاق قال مخالفاً أنا الموص نص [؟] علم صي كتاب الوصايا باب الوصية بثلث المال لفلان على دين فصدقوه فإنه يصدق إلى الثلث فإن أوصى بوصايا عزل الثلث لاصحاب الوصايا والثلثان للورثة وقيل لك صدقوه فيما شئتم وما بقي من الثلث الله تعالى فهم شركاء في الثلث ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲] وقد أشرك الثالث فيما أوصى به لكل واحد منهما في استحقاق المائة وذلك يوجب أن يكون له نصف كل مائة. وجه الاستحسان أنه أثبت الشركة بينهم وهي تقتضي المساواة وإنما ثبتت المساواة إذا لم يؤخذ من كل واحد منهما نصف المائة فعلم بهذا أنه شركة معهما جملة واحدة فلا يعتبر باشراكه إياه مع كل واحد منهما متفرقاً .اهـ.
He said: (And with one hundred to a man and one hundred to another, then he said to another: I have made you a partner with them: for him is one-third of what each has; and with four hundred to him and two hundred to another, then he said to another: I have made you a partner with them: for him is half of what each of them has.) Meaning: if he bequeaths to a man one hundred dirhams and to another one hundred, then says to a third: I have made you a partner with them, then for him is one-third of each hundred. And if he bequeaths to a man four hundred dirhams and to another two hundred, then says to a third: I have made you a partner with them, for him is half of what each of them has, because partnership linguistically implies equality. For this reason, the verse 'they are partners in the third' (4:12) is interpreted as equality. Equality between all could be established in the first case because the two amounts are equal, so he takes from each one-third of the hundred, making for him two-thirds of the hundred, and they take two-thirds each. In the second case, equality between all cannot be established due to the disparity of the two amounts, so we interpret it as equality of the third with each of them according to what is designated for him, so he takes half from each of the two amounts. And if he bequeaths to a man a slave-girl and to another another slave-girl, then says to a third: I have made you a partner with them: if the value of the two slave-girls differs, for him is half of each of them by consensus. If their values are equal, then for him is one-third of each of them according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Hanifa, for him is half of each of them, based on his view that division of slaves is not permissible, so they are considered two different types, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it, so it becomes like equal dirhams. And if he bequeaths to a man one-third of his wealth, then says to another: I have made you a partner with him, or included you, or made you with him, then the one-third is between them based on what we mentioned. The author of al-’Inayah said: What the author mentioned is istihsan, and the qiyas would be that he gets half of each hundred because the word 'partnership' implies equality when unrestricted. He said: contrary... (unclear) ...Allah says 'they are partners in the third' (4:12) and He has made the third a partner in what was bequeathed to each of them in entitlement of the hundred, and that requires that he gets half of each hundred. The basis of istihsan is that he established partnership among them, and partnership requires equality. Equality is only established if half of each hundred is not taken from him. Thus it is known that it is a single partnership with both of them collectively, so it is not considered that he made him a partner with each separately. End of quote.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This extended passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq deals with complex scenarios of partnership bequests (al-ishrak fi al-wasiyyah). The matn presents two primary cases: (1) two bequests of equal amount (100 each) to two persons, then the testator includes a third person as partner. The third gets one-third from each bequest (33.33 each, total 66.66), and each original legatee gets two-thirds of their original (66.66 each). (2) two bequests of unequal amounts (400 and 200), then including a third person. Here, the third gets half from each bequest (200 from the first, 100 from the second), resulting in the third getting 300 total, the first legatee 200, and the second 100. The sharh explains the logic: the word 'shirkah' implies equality (musawah). In the first case, since the original amounts are equal, equality among all three is possible: each ends up with the same total (66.66). In the second case, equality among all three is impossible because of the difference, so the equality is construed between the third party and each original legatee individually: he takes half of each bequest, making him equal to each? Actually, he ends up with more total, but the principle is applied to each pair. The passage then discusses the case of bequests of two slave-girls. If their values differ, the third gets half of each by consensus. If values are equal, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says he gets half of each (since he does not allow division of slaves, treating them as unique items), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) say he gets one-third from each (analogizing to equal money). Finally, if the testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to a man and then says to another 'I have made you a partner', the one-third is divided equally between them. The passage concludes with a quote from al-’Inayah noting that the author's ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), whereas strict qiyas would give the third person half of each bequest. The istihsan view considers the partnership as a single collective act, not multiple separate partnerships.

Key Terms
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; the testator's statement making a third person a partner implies equal sharing.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; the author's ruling is based on istihsan, preferring equitable outcome over strict analogy.
قياس (qiyas): Analogy; the strict qiyas would give the third person half of each bequest, but istihsan overrides this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to Zayd and 100 dirhams to Amr, then says to Bakr 'I have made you a partner with them.' How many dirhams does Bakr receive from each bequest?
A) 50 from each
B) 33.33 from each
C) 25 from each
D) 100 from each

Key Takeaway
Partnership in bequests requires equality: when original amounts are equal, the third takes one‑third from each; when unequal, half from each, and this ruling is based on istihsan rather than strict qiyas.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Testator's Instruction to Confirm Debt: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Explains that a testator's instruction to confirm a debt is treated as a bequest up to one-third by istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a testator's instruction to heirs to confirm a debt for a non-heir, and apply the principle of istihsan in distinguishing between an admission (iqrar) and a bequest (wasiyya).

Core Idea
The testator's instruction to confirm a debt is treated as a bequest up to one-third by istihsan, not as a binding admission.

This lesson explores a nuanced situation in Hanafi inheritance law: when a testator instructs his heirs to admit a debt for a non-heir without specifying the amount. Strict analogy (qiyas) would invalidate this, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to give effect to the testator's intention, treating the instruction as a bequest from the one-third share. We will examine the reasoning and the interaction with other bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's act and the ruling
The testator says to heirs 'Confirm so-and-so's debt.' The ruling: he is believed up to one-third. This is the Hanafi position by istihsan.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Strict analogy (qiyas) considers this invalid because an iqrar (admission) of an unknown amount is not enforceable and the instruction violates Shari'ah (claimants need proof). The source compares it to saying 'Whoever claims something, give it to him,' which is invalid.
The qiyas is based on the inability to enforce an open-ended admission.
3
Grasp the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the testator's intention can be fulfilled via a bequest (wasiyya). The heirs are given discretion up to one-third of the estate, akin to a bequest that is limited to one-third.
The intent is to give preference to the creditor over heirs, achievable within the one-third rule.
4
Examine the interaction with multiple bequests
When other specific bequests exist, the one-third is set aside for them. The debt instruction does not compete with known bequests. If the heirs and bequest-holders confirm the debt, each group is bound proportionally: bequest-holders pay one-third of the confirmed amount, heirs pay two-thirds.
This is because each group's confirmation is effective only regarding their own share.
5
Resolve the commentator's difficulty with al-‘Inayah's solution
The commentator raises a problem: if the bequest-holders have already taken the entire one-third, how can the heirs be bound beyond one-third? Al-‘Inayah resolves this by noting the instruction partakes of two natures: it resembles iqrar in wording and wasiyya in execution. As a bequest, it is limited to one-third; as an iqrar, it spreads over the entire estate. Thus, it is not confined to the bequest-holders' one-third but affects all thirds proportionally.
This resolution preserves both aspects of the testator's statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن قال لورثته لفلان على دين فصدقوه فإنه يصدق إلى الثلث) وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يصدق لأن الإقرار بالمجهول وإن كان صحيحاً لا يحكم به إلا بالبيان. وقوله «فصدقوه مخالف للشرع لأن المدعي لا يصدق إلا بحجة فتعذر جعله إقراراً مطلقاً فلا يعتبر فصار كمن قال كل من ادعى علي شيئاً فأعطوه فإنه باطل لكونه للشرع إلا أن يقول إن رأى الموصي أن يعطيه فحينئذ يجوز من الثلث. وجه الاستحسان قصده تقديمه على الورثة وقد أمكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية وقد يحتاج إليه من يعلم بأصل الحق عليه دون مقداره فيسعى في تفريغ ذمته فيجعل وصية جعل التقدير فيها إلى له كأنه قال لهم إذا جاءكم فلان وادعى شيئاً فأعطوه من مالي ما شاء فهذه معتبرة فكذا هذا فيصدق إلى الثلث. قال رحمه الله : (فإن أوصى بوصايا) أي مع ذلك قوله : (عزل الثلث لاصحاب الوصايا والثلثان للورثة وقيل لك صدقوه فيما شئتم وما بقي من الثلث للوصايا) أي لأصحاب الوصايا لا يشاركهم فيه صاحب الدين وإنما عزل الثلث والثلثان لأن الوصايا حقوق معلومة في الثلث والميراث معلوم في الثلثين وهذا ليس بدين معلوم ولا وصية معلومة فلا يزاحم المعلوم وقدمنا عزل المعلوم، وفي الإقرار فائدة أخرى رى وهي أن أحد الفريقين قد يكون أعرف بمقدار هذا الحق وما يتعلق به وربما يختلفون في الفضل إذا ادعاه الخصم، فإذا أقر فقد علمنا أن في التركة ديناً شائعاً في جميع التركة فيؤمر أصحاب الوصايا والورثة ببيانه، فإذا بينوا شيئاً أخذ أصحاب الوصايا بثلث ما أقروا به والورثة بثلثي ما أقروا به لأن إقرار كل فريق نافذ في حق نفسه فتلزمه بحصته، وإن ادعى المقر له أكثر حلف كل فريق على نفي العلم لأنه تحليف على فعل الغير. قال الشارح قال العبد الضعيف الراجي عفو ربه الكريم: هذا مشكل من حيث إن الورثة كانوا يصدقونه إلى الثلث ولا يلزمهم أن يصدقوه في أكثر من الثلث لأن أصحاب الوصايا أخذوا الثلث على تقدير أن تكون الوصايا تستغرق الثلث كله ولم يبق في أيديهم من الثلث شيء فوجب أن لا يلزمهم تصديقه. قال صاحب العناية : حاصله أنه تصرف بشبه الإقرار لفظاً ويشبه الوصية تنفيذاً فباعتبار شبه الوصية لا يصدق في الزيادة على الثلث. وباعتبار شبه الإقرار يجعل شائعاً في الأثلاث ولا يخصص بالثلث الذي لأصحاب الوصايا عملاً بالشبهين، وقد سبقه تاج الشريعة الثلث ذلك من
He said: (And if he says to his heirs: ‘So-and-so has a debt against me, so confirm him,’ then he is believed up to one-third.) This is istihsan, and the qiyas is that he should not be believed, because iqrar (admission) of an unknown amount, even if valid, is not enforced until specified. His statement ‘confirm him’ violates the Shari’ah because a claimant is only believed with evidence. So it cannot be considered a general iqrar, hence it is not effective. It becomes like one who says: ‘Whoever claims something against me, give it to him,’ which is invalid because it contradicts Shari’ah, unless he says: ‘If the testator sees fit to give him,’ then it is permissible from the one-third. The basis of istihsan is that he intends to give this person precedence over the heirs, and his intention can be executed by way of a bequest. Sometimes a person knows that there is a debt upon him but not its amount, and he seeks to discharge his liability, so he makes it a bequest, making the estimate up to the heirs. It is as if he said to them: ‘When so-and-so comes and claims something, give him from my wealth whatever he wishes.’ This is valid, and so is this: he is believed up to one-third. He said: (If he makes bequests) i.e., along with that, his statement: (He sets aside one-third for the bequest-holders and two-thirds for the heirs. And it is said: you confirm him as you wish, and what remains of the one-third is for the bequests) i.e., for the bequest-holders; the debt-claimant does not share with them in it. The setting aside of one-third and two-thirds is because bequests are known rights in one-third, and inheritance is known in two-thirds. And this is neither a known debt nor a known bequest, so it does not compete with what is known. We have already mentioned the setting aside of what is known. There is another benefit in iqrar: that one of the two groups may be more aware of the amount of this right and what relates to it, and they may differ regarding the surplus if the claimant claims it. So if they confirm, we know that there is a debt permeating the entire estate, so the bequest-holders and heirs are ordered to clarify it. When they specify something, the bequest-holders take one-third of what they confirmed, and the heirs take two-thirds, because each group’s confirmation is binding upon themselves, so they are liable for their share. If the claimant claims more, each group takes an oath that they have no knowledge, because it is an oath about the action of another. The commentator said: The weak slave hoping for his Lord’s forgiveness said: This is problematic because the heirs were confirming him up to one-third, and they are not bound to confirm him for more than one-third, because the bequest-holders took the one-third assuming that the bequests would exhaust the entire third, so nothing remains in their hands of the one-third, so they should not be obliged to confirm him. The author of al-’Inayah said: Its summary is that it is a disposition resembling iqrar in wording and resembling a bequest in execution. By virtue of its resemblance to a bequest, he is not believed in excess of one-third. By virtue of its resemblance to iqrar, it is made to permeate the thirds, not limited to the one-third belonging to the bequest-holders, acting on both resemblances. Taj al-Shari’ah preceded him... the third... from that.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuanced situation where the testator instructs his heirs to admit a debt for a certain person (a non-heir) without specifying the amount. The Hanafi school, by istihsan, treats this instruction as a bequest that is given effect up to one-third of the estate, even though strict qiyas would require specification or evidence. The reasoning is that the testator’s intent is to give this person precedence over the heirs, and this can be realized via a bequest. The analogy is made to a testator saying 'give him whatever he claims,' which is valid as a bequest from the one-third. The passage then discusses the case where there are also other specific bequests. The initial ruling: set aside one-third for the bequests and two-thirds for the heirs. The debt claimant does not share with the bequest-holders in that one-third? Actually, the text says the debt is not a known debt nor a known bequest, so it does not compete with the known. However, when the heirs and bequest-holders confirm the debt, they do so proportionally: the bequest-holders' confirmation binds them to pay one-third of what they confirm, and the heirs bind themselves to two-thirds. This is because each group's confirmation is effective only regarding their own share. If the claimant claims more than what is confirmed, each group swears that they have no knowledge. The commentator (the author himself) raises a problem: since the heirs only confirm up to one-third, but the bequest-holders have already taken the entire one-third, the heirs cannot be forced to confirm beyond that. Al-’Inayah resolves this by noting that this act partakes of two natures: it resembles iqrar in wording and wasiyyah in execution. As a bequest, it is limited to one-third; as an iqrar, it is like a debt that spreads over the entire estate. Therefore, it is not confined to the one-third of the bequest-holders but is spread across all thirds. This is a sophisticated resolution.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Admission; the testator's statement is not a full iqrar but a directive to admit.
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest; the testator's instruction is executed as a bequest from the one-third.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override strict qiyas in favor of the testator's intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi istihsan, up to what portion of the estate is a testator's instruction to his heirs to confirm a debt for a non-heir believed?
A) The entire estate
B) One-third of the estate
C) Two-thirds of the estate
D) None, it is invalid

Key Takeaway
The testator's instruction to confirm an unspecified debt is executed as a bequest up to one-third, by istihsan, honoring his intent while protecting heirs' shares.

Bequest to a Non-Heir and an Heir Together
Ruling with proof and distinction from acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest is made to both a non-heir and an heir, distinguish it from acknowledgment, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on joint acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A bequest to a non-heir is valid but void to an heir; joint acknowledgment to both is entirely void per Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the rule when a testator combines a bequest to a non-heir (ajnabi) and an heir (warith) in one statement. The non-heir receives half the bequest (or the portion allocable), and the bequest to the heir is void. The commentary then distinguishes this from acknowledgment (iqrar), where a similar joint declaration is treated differently due to its informative nature. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the other regarding the validity of the acknowledgment to the non-heir when the heir denies partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states that when a testator bequeaths to a non-heir and his heir, the non-heir takes half the bequest and the bequest to the heir is void. Understand that this is the default ruling assuming no consent from other heirs.
The bequest to the heir could become valid if other heirs consent after death, but the matn deals with the normal case.
2
Understand the Talil (Rationale)
The commentary explains: the testator owns the portion bequeathed to the non-heir (up to one-third) but does not own the portion to the heir without consent. Thus, the bequest splits: valid for what he owns, void for what he does not own.
This is contrasted with bequest to a living and a dead person, where the dead is incapable, so the entire sum goes to the living.
3
Distinguish Bequest from Acknowledgment
The passage then contrasts bequest (wasiyya) with acknowledgment (iqrar). In bequest, the testator creates ownership; in acknowledgment, he informs of a pre-existing right. Therefore, a joint acknowledgment to an heir and a non-heir is treated differently: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule it entirely void because the partnership cannot be separated; Muhammad holds it valid for the non-heir if the heir denies partnership.
The key difference lies in the nature of the act: creative vs. informative.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Iqrar
The commentary details the ikhtilaf: Muhammad argues that the heir's admission of invalidity of his own share does not affect the non-heir's claim, while the two imams argue that the acknowledgment was made as a single indivisible statement of partnership, so if one part fails, the whole fails.
The text does not explicitly choose between these views; later fatwa practice may follow the two imams.

قال رحمه الله : ( ولأجنبي ووارثه له نصف الوصية وبطل وصيته للوارث) أي إذا أوصى لأجنبي ووارثه كان للأجنبي نصف الوصية وبطلت للوارث لأنه أوصى بما يملك وبما لا يملك فصح فيما يملك وبطل في الآخر بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لحي وميت حيث يكون الكل للحي لأن الميت ليس بأهل للوصية فلا تصح وبخلاف الوارث فإنه من أهلها ولهذا تصح باجازة الورثة فافترقا وعلى هذا إذا أوصى للقاتل والأجنبي، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه ولأجنبي حيث لا تصح في حق الأجنبي أيضاً لأن الوصية إنشاء تصرف وهو تمليك مبتدأ لهما والشركة تثبت حكماً للتمليك فتصح في حق من يستحقه دون الآخر لأن بطلان التمليك لأحدهما لا يوجب بطلان التمليك من الآخر. أما الاقرار بها اخباراً عن الكائن وقد أخبر بوصف الشركة في الماضي ولا وجه إلى اثباته بدون هذا الوصف لأنه خلاف ما أخبر به ولا إلى اثبات هذا الوصف لأنه يصير الوارث فيه شريكاً ولأنه لو قبض الأجنبي شيئاً كان للوارث أن يشاركه فيه فيبطل في ذلك القدر فلا يكون مفيداً. قال في النهاية قال التمرتاشي : هذا إذا تصادقا، أما إذا أنكر الأجنبي شركة الوارث أو أنكر الوارث شركة الأجنبي فإنه يصح إقراره في صحة الأجنبي عند محمد لأن الوارث مقر ببطلان حقه وبطلان حق شريكه فيبطل في حقه ولا يبطل في حق الآخر، وعندهما يبطل في الكل لأن حق الوارث لم يتميز عن حق الأجنبي وإنما أوجبه مشتركاً بينهما كما بينا. وفي المبسوط : مسائله على فصول : أحدها في الوصية الأجنبي ولوارثه والثاني في الوصية للأجنبي مع أحد الزوجين، والثالث في الوصية للأجنبي وللقاتل والرابع في الوصية بالبيع من الوارث أو من الأجنبي. رجل أوصى لأجنبي ولوارثه فللأجنبي نصف الوصية لأن الايصاء ابتداء إيجاب.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for a non-heir and his heir, he has half the bequest, and his bequest to the heir is void). When one bequeaths to a non-heir and his heir, the non-heir receives half the bequest, and the bequest to the heir is void because he bequeathed what he owns and what he does not own, so it is valid regarding what he owns and void regarding the other. This is unlike if he bequeaths to a living person and a dead person, where the entire bequest goes to the living because the dead is not qualified to receive a bequest, so it is not valid. And unlike the heir, who is qualified, hence it is valid with the consent of the other heirs. This is also the case if he bequeaths to a killer and a non-heir. This differs from if he makes an acknowledgment of a specific item or debt to his heir and a non-heir, where it is not valid regarding the non-heir either, because a bequest is a creative disposition—a transfer of ownership initiated for both, and partnership is established by the transfer. So it is valid regarding the one who deserves it and not the other, because the invalidity of the transfer for one does not necessitate invalidity for the other. As for acknowledgment, it is informing of an existing state, and he has informed of a past partnership. There is no way to establish it without this description because that would contradict what he informed, nor to establish this description because it makes the heir a partner. And if the non-heir takes something, the heir can share it, so it becomes ineffective in that amount. In al-Nihaya, al-Tamartashi said: This is if they both agree. But if the non-heir denies the heir's partnership or the heir denies the non-heir's partnership, then according to Muhammad his acknowledgment is valid regarding the non-heir's share because the heir admits the invalidity of his own right and his partner's right, so it is invalid regarding him but not regarding the other. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it is invalid entirely because the heir's right is not distinct from the non-heir's right; he made it shared between them. In al-Mabsut: The issues are in chapters: first, bequest to a non-heir and his heir; second, bequest to a non-heir along with one of the spouses; third, bequest to a non-heir and the killer; fourth, bequest of a sale to an heir or a non-heir. A man bequeaths to a non-heir and his heir: the non-heir gets half the bequest because bequest initiates obligation.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states that if a testator makes a bequest to both a non-heir (ajnabi) and an heir (warith), the non-heir receives half of the bequest and the bequest to the heir is void. The commentary explains the reasoning: the testator has bequeathed something he owns (the portion for the non-heir) and something he does not own (the heir's portion, since the heir cannot inherit via bequest without consent), so the valid part takes effect and the invalid part is void. This is contrasted with bequests to a living and a dead person, where the entire sum goes to the living because the dead is incapable of ownership. Similarly, a bequest to a killer and a non-heir follows the same rule. The commentary then distinguishes between bequest and acknowledgment (iqrar). In acknowledgment, if a person acknowledges a debt or specific item to both an heir and a non-heir in one statement, it is entirely invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the partnership is an essential part of the information, and if it cannot be established, the entire acknowledgment fails. Muhammad disagrees, holding that if one party denies the partnership, the acknowledgment is valid for the non-heir. The passage ends by listing various examples from al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest; a transfer of ownership of property after death, up to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent, except for the heir who needs consent.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right (debt or property) that already existed; informative rather than creative.
وارث (warith): Heir; a person entitled to a share of the estate by inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to his heir and a non-heir, what happens to the bequest?
A) The entire bequest is void.
B) The non-heir takes half the bequest and the heir's portion is void.
C) Both receive equally.
D) The heir takes the entire bequest.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a non-heir and an heir splits: valid for the non-heir, void for the heir; joint acknowledgment is treated differently due to its informative nature.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest of Three Different Garments with One Lost
Ruling on partial loss of bequeathed specific items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when multiple specific bequest items are made and one is lost without identification, and explain why the loss of one does not void the entire bequest.

Core Idea
Loss of one bequeathed item does not void all bequests; the heir's claim determines voidness unless legatees surrender.

Imagine you bequeath three different garments to three different people. After your death, one garment is lost and no one knows which. The heir claims each legatee's right is lost. How does Hanafi law resolve this? In this lesson, we examine the ruling from the matn and the legal reasoning behind partial voidness, contrasting it with other areas like acknowledgment (iqrar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Determine the exact fact pattern: three garments of different value (good, medium, poor) bequeathed to three individuals. One garment is lost, and it is unknown which.
The difference in value matters because if they were equal, the ruling might differ (not discussed here).
2
State the initial ruling from the matn
The heir says to each legatee: 'Your right is lost' (i.e., the bequest for that garment is void) unless the legatees collectively surrender what remains.
The matn implies that without surrender, the bequest of all three becomes void? But commentary clarifies it is void only regarding the lost one.
3
Understand the legal principle behind partial voidness
The commentary explains that the bequest is valid in part because the voidness of one obligation does not void the entire obligation. This contrasts with acknowledgment (iqrar), where a void part voids the whole due to its nature as a report.
Key distinction: bequest creates rights (ijab), while acknowledgment reports a prior fact.
4
Compare with the case of acknowledgment (iqrar)
If a sick person acknowledges a debt to both a non-heir and an heir in one statement, the entire acknowledgment is void (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Because if the past fact (partnership) is false, the report is void. Bequest is different because it does not report a past event.
This comparison is used as a proof (dalil) via distinction (farq).
5
Apply the ruling to the three garment case
Thus, for the three garments, the loss of one does not void all three. The legatees may choose to accept the remaining two by agreement; otherwise, the heir's claim that each right is lost stands.
The heir's statement is effectively a claim that no identification is possible, so each legatee loses unless they compromise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضاع ثوب ولم يدر أي والوارث يقول لكل هلك حقك بطلت إلا أن يسلموا ما بقي وقد أضيف إلى ما لا يملكه وإلى ما يملكه فيصح فيما لا يملكه ويبطل فيما لا يملكه، ولم يبطل هذا ببطلان الآخر لأن الشركة بينهما في حكم الايجاب وببطلان بعض الحكم لا يبطل الايجاب بخلاف ما لو أقر المريض لأجنبي ولوارثه في كلام واحد حيث يبطل الكل عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأن الاشتراك هناك يخبر عنه لأن الإقرار اخبار عن كائن سابق والخبر بناء على المخبر به فكان المخبر به العلة والخبر بمنزلة الحكم للعلة فإذا لم يثبت المخبر المخبر عنه وهو الاشتراك لم يثبت حكمه وهو الخبر . أصله أن الوارث إذا كان بحال لا يجوز جميع الميراث فالوصية بمقدار الثلث للأجنبي مقدمة في التنفيذ في حق هذا الوارث وفيما زاد على الثلث مؤخرة فإن الوصية بالثلث تقع نافذة من غير إجازة فكانت وصية قوية مستحكمة فتكون في التنفيذ مقدمة، والوصية بما زاد على الثلث واهية ضعيفة لأنها لا تجوز إلا بالإجازة لتعلق حق الورثة به فكانت مؤخرة عن حق الورثة لأن حقهم متأكد، فإذا وصل إلى الوارث حقه صار كمن لا وارث له فتنفذ وصيته فيه . والثاني أن من لا وارث له تصح وصيته بجميع المال الموجود المطلق وهي مالكيته وأهليته امرأة ماتت عن زوج وأوصت بنصف مالها لأجنبي جاز للزوج الثلث وهو نصف الثلثين وللموصى له النصف يبقى سدس لبيت المال لأن وصية الأجنبي بقدر الثلث وصية مؤكدة فكانت في التنفيذ مقدمة فصار الثلث مستحقاً بالوصية فيبطل الإرث فيه فيبقى تركتها ثلثي المال فللزوج نصف ذلك وهو ثلث الكل يبقى ثلث آخر وليس له مستحق بالميراث فتنفذ فيه الوصية في ثلثه وذلك سدس فوصل إلى الموصى له نصف المال وبقي سدس لا وصية ولا وارث فيه فيصرف إلى بيت المال. وكذلك لو مات الرجل عن امرأته وأوصى بماله كله لأجنبي ولم تجز الوصية فللمرأة السدس وخمسة أسداسه للموصى له لأن الثلث صار مستحقاً بالوصية بقيت التركة بثلثي المال فللمرأة ربع ذلك والباقي للموصى له لأن الوصية مقدمة على بيت المال ولو ماتت عن زوج وأوصت لقاتلها بالنصف يأخذ الزوج النصف أولاً وللقاتل النصف الآخر وهي وصية ضعيفة لأنه بمنزلة الوارث فيقدم الميراث عليها فيستحق الزوج أولاً نصف المال بالإرث والنصف الباقي فارع عن حق الورثة فتنفذ الوصية فيه للقاتل كما تنفذ الوصية للقاتل في تركة من لا وارث له. ولو تركت عبدين قيمتهما سواء وأوصت بأحدهما لزوجها فله العبدان بالإرث والوصية لأنه مستحق لما فضل عن فرضه فيكون عارياً عن حق الغير فصحت الوصية لفقد المانع، أصله أن الوصية للوارث بالثلث بمنزلة الوصية للأجنبي بما زاد على الثلث حتى لا تنفذ كل واحدة منهما إلا بإجازة الورثة لأنها صادفت محلاً تعلق به حق بعض الورثة فيتوقف على اجازتهم . قال رحمه الله : (وبثياب متفاوتة لثلاثة فضاع ثوب ولم يدر أي والوارث يقول لكل هلك حقك بطلت أي إذا أوصى بثلاثة ثياب متفاوتة وهي جيد ووسط ورديء لثلاثة أنفار لكل
A garment was lost and it is not known which one, and the heir says to each: your right is lost, it becomes void unless they surrender what remains. And it is added to what he does not own and what he owns, so it is valid regarding what he does not own and void regarding what he does not own. And this does not become void due to the voidness of the other because the partnership between them is in the ruling of obligation, and the voidness of some of the ruling does not void the obligation. Unlike if a sick person acknowledges to a non-heir and his heir in one statement, where it is entirely void according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the partnership there is informed about, because acknowledgment informs of a past occurrence, and the report is based on the reported matter. So the reported matter is the cause, and the report is like the effect of the cause. When the reported matter (the partnership) is not established, its effect (the report) is not established. The principle: if the heir is in a state where the entire inheritance is not permissible, then the bequest of one-third to the non-heir is given precedence in execution over this heir, and what exceeds one-third is deferred. Because the bequest of one-third takes effect without permission, so it is a strong, well-established bequest, thus priority in execution. The bequest of more than one-third is weak because it is only valid with permission due to the heirs' right being attached, so it is deferred after the heirs' right. When the heir receives his right, he becomes like one with no heir, so his bequest is executed in it. Second: one who has no heir, his bequest of all the existing property is valid, and it is his ownership and eligibility. A woman died leaving a husband and bequeathed half her property to a non-heir: the husband takes one-third (half of two-thirds), the legatee half, leaving one-sixth for the public treasury. Because the non-heir's bequest of one-third is a strong bequest, so priority in execution, so the one-third is owed by the bequest, and inheritance is void in it. Her estate remains two-thirds; the husband gets half of that (one-third of the whole), leaving another one-third with no heir, so the bequest is executed in its third (one-sixth), so the legatee gets half the property, leaving one-sixth with no bequest or heir, to the public treasury. Similarly, if a man dies leaving a wife and bequeaths all his property to a non-heir and the bequest is not permitted, the wife gets one-sixth and five-sixths for the legatee. Because one-third becomes owed by bequest, so the estate remains two-thirds; the wife gets a quarter of that, the rest for the legatee because the bequest takes priority over the public treasury. And if a woman dies leaving a husband and bequeaths half to her killer, the husband takes half first, and the killer takes the other half. It is a weak bequest because he is like an heir, so inheritance takes precedence over it. The husband first receives half of the property by inheritance, and the remaining half is free of the heirs' right, so the bequest is executed for the killer, just as a bequest to a killer is executed in the estate of one with no heir. And if she leaves two slaves of equal value and bequeaths one to her husband, he gets both by inheritance and bequest because he is entitled to what exceeds his fixed share, so it is free of others' right, so the bequest is valid for lack of impediment. The principle is that a bequest to an heir of one-third is like a bequest to a non-heir of more than one-third, so neither is executed without the heirs' permission because they encounter an asset to which the right of some heirs is attached, so it depends on their permission. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And with three different garments for three, a garment was lost and it is not known which, and the heir says to each: your right is lost, it becomes void) meaning if he bequeaths three different garments (good, medium, poor) to three persons, each...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage introduces a new ruling about bequests of multiple specific items. The matn states that if someone bequeaths three different garments (good, medium, poor) to three different people, and one garment is lost without identifying which, the heir (or presumably the executor) says that each legatee's right is lost unless they agree to share what remains. The commentary explains the legal principle: the bequest is considered as giving what the testator owns and what he does not own, valid in part. The voidness of one part does not void the whole because partnership in the obligation is not completely voided. This is contrasted with acknowledgment (iqrar) which is entirely void if the partnership cannot be established. The commentary then goes into a detailed discussion of the priority of bequests over inheritance, giving examples of a widow, a husband, bequest to a killer, etc. Finally, it returns to the matn's specific case of three garments.

Key Terms
ثوب (thawb): Garment; a specific item of clothing bequeathed.
متفاوتة (mutafāwita): Unequal in value; the three garments are of different quality (good, medium, poor).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of bequeathing three different garments to three persons, if one garment is lost and it is unknown which, what does the heir say?
A) The bequest is entirely valid.
B) Each legatee's right is lost unless they surrender what remains.
C) The legatees must divide the lost garment's value.
D) The heir takes the lost garment.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the loss of one specific bequeathed item does not automatically void all bequests; the heir can claim each right is lost unless the legatees agree to accept the remainder.

When the Bequeathed Item Is Lost and the Heir Denies: Ruling and Analogies
Ruling on bequest invalidity with analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest when the item is lost and the heir denies, and distinguish it from the case of a sick person's acknowledgment to a stranger and heir in one statement.

Core Idea
A bequest is invalid if the heir denies knowledge of the specific property, but a bequest to both a stranger and a heir jointly does not void the stranger's share.

This passage tackles a practical scenario in inheritance: a testator bequeaths a specific item that is later lost, and the heir claims not to know which item it was. The ruling hinges on uncertainty and the heir's denial. The author then draws a critical comparison to the case of a sick person's acknowledgment (iqrar) to both a stranger and a heir, where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule the entire acknowledgment void. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to apply the principles of bequest validity and the effect of uncertainty in obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Read the first few lines: when a bequeathed garment is lost and the heir says 'your right has perished', the bequest is invalid unless the heir hands over the remaining items. Note the condition of the heir's denial.
The invalidity is due to uncertainty (jahala) about the subject matter.
2
Analyze the comparison with joint bequest
The text then says if a bequest is made to both a stranger and a heir of property partly owned by each, the bequest is valid for the stranger's share and invalid for the heir's share, but the invalidity of one does not affect the other. Understand why: each share is an independent obligation.
This is contrasted with the acknowledgment case.
3
Examine the acknowledgment analogy
The passage contrasts the above with a sick person acknowledging a debt to a stranger and heir in one sentence. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the whole acknowledgment is void because it is a single report (khabr) about a prior state that must be true; if the reported state (sharing) is false, the report fails.
This is a key intra-Hanafi difference.
4
Understand the priority of bequests within one-third
The text explains that a bequest to a stranger of one-third is strong (takes effect without heirs' permission), while a bequest exceeding one-third is weak (requires permission). This sets the stage for the subsequent examples.
This principle is used to resolve the distribution of multiple claims.
5
Apply the examples
Walk through the three examples: (1) woman bequeaths half to a stranger – husband gets 1/3, stranger half, remainder to treasury; (2) man bequeaths all to a stranger – wife gets 1/6, stranger 5/6; (3) woman bequeaths half to her killer – husband half, killer half. Each shows how strong and weak bequests are prioritized.
The killer case highlights a weak bequest (like a bequest to an heir) that is deferred after inheritance.

Source Text

فضاع ثوب ولم يدر أي والوارث يقول لكل هلك حقك بطلت إلا أن يسلموا ما بقي وقد أضيف إلى ما لا يملكه وإلى ما يملكه فيصح فيما لا يملكه ويبطل فيما لا يملكه [؟]، ولم يبطل هذا ببطلان الآخر لأن الشركة بينهما في حكم الايجاب وببطلان بعض الحكم لا يبطل الايجاب بخلاف ما لو أقر المريض لأجنبي ولوارثه في كلام واحد حيث يبطل الكل عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأن الاشتراك هناك يخبر عنه [؟] لأن الإقرار اخبار عن كائن سابق والخبر بناء على المخبر به فكان المخبر به العلة والخبر بمنزلة الحكم للعلة فإذا لم يثبت المخبر المخبر عنه وهو الاشتراك لم يثبت حكمه وهو الخبر . أصله أن الوارث إذا كان بحال لا يجوز جميع الميراث فالوصية بمقدار الثلث للأجنبي مقدمة في التنفيذ في حق هذا الوارث وفيما زاد على الثلث مؤخرة فإن الوصية بالثلث تقع نافذة من غير إجازة فكانت وصية قوية مستحكمة فتكون في التنفيذ مقدمة، والوصية بما زاد على الثلث واهية ضعيفة لأنها لا تجوز إلا بالإجازة لتعلق حق الورثة به فكانت مؤخرة عن حق الورثة لأن حقهم متأكد، فإذا وصل إلى الوارث حقه صار كمن لا وارث له فتنفذ وصيته فيه . والثاني أن من لا وارث له تصح وصيته بجميع المال الموجود المطلق وهي مالكيته وأهليته امرأة ماتت عن زوج وأوصت بنصف مالها لأجنبي جاز للزوج الثلث وهو نصف الثلثين وللموصى له النصف يبقى سدس لبيت المال لأن وصية الأجنبي بقدر الثلث وصية مؤكدة فكانت في التنفيذ مقدمة فصار الثلث مستحقاً بالوصية فيبطل الإرث فيه فيبقى تركتها ثلثي المال فللزوج نصف ذلك وهو ثلث الكل يبقى ثلث آخر وليس له مستحق بالميراث فتنفذ فيه الوصية في ثلثه وذلك سدس فوصل إلى الموصى له نصف المال وبقي سدس لا وصية ولا وارث فيه فيصرف إلى بيت المال. وكذلك لو مات الرجل عن امرأته وأوصى بماله كله لأجنبي ولم تجز الوصية فللمرأة السدس وخمسة أسداسه للموصى له لأن الثلث صار مستحقاً بالوصية بقيت التركة بثلثي المال فللمرأة ربع ذلك والباقي للموصى له لأن الوصية مقدمة على بيت المال ولو ماتت عن زوج وأوصت لقاتلها بالنصف يأخذ الزوج النصف أولاً وللقاتل النصف الآخر وهي وصية ضعيفة لأنه بمنزلة الوارث فيقدم الميراث عليها فيستحق الزوج أولاً نصف المال بالإرث والنصف الباقي فارع عن حق الورثة فتنفذ الوصية فيه للقاتل كما تنفذ الوصية للقاتل في تركة من لا وارث له. ولو تركت عبدين قيمتهما سواء وأوصت بأحدهما لزوجها فله العبدان بالإرث والوصية لأنه مستحق لما فضل عن فرضه فيكون عارياً عن حق الغير فصحت الوصية لفقد المانع، أصله أن الوصية للوارث بالثلث بمنزلة الوصية للأجنبي بما زاد على الثلث حتى لا تنفذ كل واحدة منهما إلا بإجازة الورثة لأنها صادفت محلاً تعلق به حق بعض الورثة فيتوقف على اجازتهم.
A garment was lost and it is not known which one, and the heir says to each: 'Your right has perished.' The bequest is invalidated unless they hand over what remains. And it is added to what he does not own and to what he owns, so it is valid regarding what he does not own and invalid regarding what he does not own [؟]. And this is not invalidated by the invalidity of the other because sharing between them is in the ruling of obligation, and the invalidity of some of the ruling does not invalidate the obligation. Unlike if a sick person acknowledges to a stranger and to his heir in one statement, where the whole is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because the sharing there informs about it [؟], because acknowledgment is information about a prior event, and the information is built upon what is informed about. So what is informed about is the cause, and the information is like a ruling for the cause. So if what is informed about—which is the sharing—does not materialize, its ruling—which is the information—does not materialize. The principle: when the heir is in a state where the entire inheritance is not permissible, the bequest of one-third to a stranger takes precedence in execution with respect to this heir, and what exceeds one-third is deferred. For the bequest of one-third takes effect without permission, so it is a strong, established bequest; thus it takes precedence in execution. And the bequest exceeding one-third is weak because it is only valid with permission due to the right of the heirs being attached to it, so it is deferred to the right of the heirs because their right is confirmed. So when the heir receives his right, he becomes like one with no heir, so his bequest is executed in it. The second: one with no heir, his bequest of all his property is valid absolutely; and it is his ownership and capacity. A woman dies leaving a husband and bequeaths half of her property to a stranger: the husband gets the third (which is half of two-thirds), and the legatee gets half; a sixth remains for the treasury, because the bequest to the stranger of one-third is a confirmed bequest, so it is given priority in execution; so the third becomes due by bequest, so inheritance is voided in it; thus her estate remains two-thirds of the property; the husband gets half of that (one-third of the total), and another third remains with no claimant through inheritance, so the bequest is executed in that third (a sixth), so the legatee receives half of the property; a sixth remains with neither bequest nor heir, so it goes to the treasury. Similarly, if a man dies leaving his wife and bequeaths all his property to a stranger and the bequest is not ratified, the wife gets one-sixth and five-sixths go to the legatee, because the third became due by bequest; the estate remains two-thirds of the property; the wife gets a quarter of that and the rest goes to the legatee, because the bequest takes precedence over the treasury. And if a woman dies leaving a husband and bequeaths half to her killer, the husband takes the half first, and the killer takes the other half; this bequest is weak because the killer is like an heir, so inheritance takes precedence over it; thus the husband first gets half the property by inheritance, and the remaining half is free of the right of the heirs, so the bequest for the killer is executed in it, just as the bequest for the killer is executed in the estate of one with no heir. And if she leaves two slaves of equal value and bequeaths one of them to her husband, he takes both slaves by inheritance and bequest, because he deserves what remains of his prescribed share; thus it is free of the right of others, so the bequest is valid due to the absence of an impediment. The principle: the bequest to an heir of one-third is like the bequest to a stranger of more than one-third, in that neither is executed without the heirs' permission, because they confront a property to which the right of some heirs is attached, so they depend on their permission.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof discussing the invalidity of a bequest when the bequeathed item is lost and the heir denies knowledge of which item. The ruling: the bequest is invalid unless the heirs surrender the remaining items. The commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) then draws an analogy: if a bequest is made to a stranger and a heir jointly (e.g., a garment owned in part by each), the bequest is valid for the stranger's share and invalid for the heir's share, but the invalidity of the heir's portion does not invalidate the stranger's portion because they are independent obligations. This is contrasted with a sick person's acknowledgment to a stranger and heir in one statement—according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the entire acknowledgment is invalid because the acknowledgment is a single report about a prior state, and if the reported state (sharing) is false, the report fails. The passage then explains the principle of priority in execution: a bequest to a stranger within one-third is strong (takes effect without heirs' permission), while a bequest exceeding one-third is weak (requires permission). It applies this to several cases: a woman bequeaths half to a stranger—husband gets one-third (his share), legatee gets half, remainder goes to treasury; a man bequeaths all to a stranger—wife gets one-sixth, legatee gets five-sixths; a woman bequeaths half to her killer—husband gets half by inheritance, killer gets the other half because the bequest to a killer is weak; and a woman bequeaths one of two equal slaves to her husband—the husband takes both because he is entitled to more than his prescribed share. The passage concludes with the principle that a bequest to an heir of one-third is like a bequest to a stranger of more than one-third: both require heirs' permission.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A disposition of property to take effect after death, typically within one-third of the estate unless heirs permit more.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): Permission or ratification by the heirs after the testator's death, allowing a bequest exceeding one-third or to an heir.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right due to another, treated as a report about the past.
القاتل (al-qatil): The killer of the testator; bequest to the killer is weak and not given precedence over inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the ruling if a sick person acknowledges a debt to a stranger and to his heir in one statement?
A) The acknowledgment is valid for the stranger and invalid for the heir.
B) The entire acknowledgment is invalid.
C) The acknowledgment is valid for both if the heir ratifies.
D) The acknowledgment is valid for the heir only.

Key Takeaway
A bequest is invalid if the bequeathed item is lost and the heir denies knowledge, but a bequest to a stranger and heir jointly does not void the stranger's share; this differs from a sick person's acknowledgment in one statement, which is entirely void according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
