Distribution of Bequeathed Garments When One Is Lost
Ruling with proof and commentary on expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of multiple garments when one is lost and the heir denies knowledge, and calculate the distribution if the remaining garments are surrendered.

Core Idea
Uncertainty of beneficiary invalidates a bequest, but surrendering remaining property restores validity with a probabilistic distribution.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced problem in wasiyyah: when a testator bequeaths three distinct garments (good, medium, poor) to three different persons, and one garment is lost without anyone knowing which, the heir's denial of knowledge can invalidate the entire bequest. However, if the heir cooperates by handing over the two remaining garments, the bequest remains valid and a special distribution method ensures each recipient receives their due as far as possible. The commentator also refines the author's wording regarding the heir's denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the problem of jahalah
Three different garments (jayyid, wasat, radi’) are bequeathed to three persons. One garment is lost and it is unknown which. The heir denies knowledge by claiming each person's right has perished, leading to jahalah (uncertainty) about the beneficiary.
Jahalah prevents delivery of the bequest and invalidates it.
2
Analyze the heir's denial: author's wording vs. correct interpretation
The author's phrasing (the heir says 'your right has perished' to each) is critiqued as factually false because only one garment is lost. The better expression from al-Jami' al-Saghir is that the heir says 'the right of one of you is void, we do not know whose'.
This shows the importance of precise legal expression (sighah).
3
Determine the effect of the heir's denial
With such denial, the bequest is invalidated because the entitlement is uncertain, analogous to bequest to one of two unknown persons.
The ruling is based on qiyas to a known principle.
4
Recognize the exception: heirs hand over remaining garments
If the heirs (the testator's successors) deliver the two remaining garments, the temporary jahalah is removed and the bequest becomes valid again.
The bequest was valid in origin; the impediment is the heir's refusal due to uncertainty.
5
Apply the distribution method
The recipient of the good garment gets 2/3 of the good garment; the recipient of the poor gets 2/3 of the poor; the recipient of the medium gets 1/3 of each of the two remaining garments. Each ends up with 2/3 of a garment.
This methodology respects probability and the testator's preference (tafdil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبثياب متفاوتة لثلاثة فضاع ثوب ولم يدر أي والوارث يقول لكل هلك حقك بطلت أي إذا أوصى بثلاثة ثياب متفاوتة وهي جيد ووسط ورديء لثلاثة أنفار لكل فلذي الجيد ثلثاه ولذى الرديء ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل وببيت عين من دار واحد منهم بثوب فضاع منها ثوب ولا يدرى أيهم والوارث يجحد ذلك بأن يقول لكل واحد هلك حقك أو حق أحدكم ولا يدري من هو الهالك فلا أدفع إليكم شيئاً بطلت الوصية لأن المستحق مجهول وجهالته تمنع صحة القضاء وتحصيل غرض الموصي فيبطل كما إذا أوصى لأحد الرجلين وقول المؤلف والوارث يقول إلى آخره ومعنى جحودهم أن يقول حقك قد هلك أقول : في ظاهر تعبير المؤلف ههنا منهم هو الوارث لكل واحد منهما الثوب الذي فساد لأن هلاك كل واحد منهم إنما يتصور فيما إذا ضاعت الأثواب الثلاثة معاً والغرض في المسألة أن ضياع ثوب واحد منه غير معلوم بخصوصه فكيف يصح أن يقول الوارث لكل واحد منهم الثوب الذي هو حقك قد هلك فإنه كذب ظاهر لا ينبغي أن أن يترتب عليه حكم شرعي بل قوله لواحد منهم الثوب الذي هو حقك قد هلك عن وضع فضلاً يسمع أصلا يقتضي الاعتراف بكون الثوبين الباقيين لصاحبه والأولى في التعبير ما ذكر في الجامع الصغير سيما للصدر الشهيد والإمام قاضيخان وهو أن المراد بجحود الوارث أن يقول حق واحد منكم بطل ولا ندري من بطل حقه ومن بقي حقه فلا نسلم إليكم شيئاً، والذي يمكن في توجيه كلام المصنف أن يكون مراده معنى جحوده أن يقول الوارث لكل واحد بعينه الثوب الذي قد هلك يحتمل أن يكون حقك فكأنه سامح في العبارة بناء على ظهور والمراد، ووافقه صاحب الكافي في هذه العبارة مع ظهور كمالها قال رحمه الله: (إلا أن يسلموا ما بقي) أي إلا أن يسلم الورثة ما بقي من الثياب فحينئذ تصح الوصية لأنها كانت صحيحة في الأصل، وإنما بطلت بجهالة طارئة مانعة من التسليم فإذا سلموا الباقي زال المانع فعادت صحيحة كما كانت فتقسم بينهم قال رحمه الله : فلذي الجيد ثلثاه ولذى الرديء ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل أي لصاحب الجيد ثلثا الثوب الجيد ولصاحب الرديء يعطى ثلثا الثوب الرديء ولصاحب الوسط ثلث كل واحد منهما فيصيب كل واحد منهم ثلثا ثوب لأن الاثنين إذا قسما على ثلاثة أصحاب كل واحد منهما الثلثان، وإنما أعطى لصاحب الوسط ثلث كل واحد منهم وللآخرين الثلثين من ثوب واحد لأن صاحب الجيد لا حق له الرديء بيقين لأنه إنما يكون هو الرديء أو الوسط ولا حق له فيهما، واحتمل أن يكون حقه في الرديء بأن كان الهالك هو الجيد أو الوسط واحتمل أن يكون له فيه حق بأن يكون الهالك أجود، ويحتمل أن يكون في الرديء بأن يكون الهالك أردأ ويحتمل أن يكون له فيهما حق بأن كان الوسط، فإذا كان كذلك أعطى كل واحد منهم حقه من محل يحتمل أن يكون هو له لأن التسوية بإبطال حق كل واحد منهم إليه وهم في احتمال بقاء حقه وبطلانه سواء، وفيما قلنا إيصال حق كل واحد منهم بقدر الإمكان وتحصيل غرض الموصي من التفضيل فكان متعيناً. وفي العيون: إذا أوصى لرجل بثياب جيدة فله ما يلبس من الجباب والقمص الهالك هو
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: '(And with different garments for three, a garment was lost and it is not known which one, and the heir says to each: your right has perished, it is invalidated.)' i.e., if he bequeaths three different garments—a good, a medium, and a poor—to three persons, each: for the owner of the good, two-thirds of it; for the owner of the poor, two-thirds of it; for the owner of the medium, one-third of each. And by a specified house of one of them with a garment, a garment was lost and it is not known which one, and the heir denies that by saying to each: your right has perished, or one of you, and he does not know who the lost one is, so I will not give you anything; the bequest is invalidated because the entitled person is unknown, and ignorance prevents valid judgment and achieving the testator's purpose, so it is invalidated, like if he bequeaths to one of two men. And the author's saying 'and the heir says' etc. The meaning of their denial is that he says: your right has perished. I say: In the apparent expression of the author here, the heir is for each of them the garment which is corrupt? Because the destruction of each of them is only conceivable when the three garments are lost together, but the purpose in the issue is that the loss of one garment of them is not individually known. How can it be correct for the heir to say to each of them: the garment which is your right has perished? For that is an obvious lie, which should not have a legal consequence. Rather, his saying to one of them 'the garment which is your right has perished' for placing [؟], let alone hearing it at all, implies an acknowledgment that the two remaining garments belong to the owner. The better expression is what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, especially for al-Sadr al-Shahid and Imam Qadi Khan, which is that the intended meaning of the heir's denial is that he says: the right of one of you is void, and we do not know whose right is void and whose right remains, so we will not give you anything. And what is possible in directing the author's words is that his intended meaning of his denial is that the heir says to each specific person: the garment that has perished may be your right, so he was lenient in expression based on clarity and the intended meaning. And al-Kafi agreed with this expression with obvious completeness. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'unless they hand over what remains' i.e., unless the heirs hand over the remaining garments; then the bequest becomes valid because it was valid in origin; it was only invalidated by a temporary ignorance preventing delivery. So when they hand over the remainder, the impediment is removed, so it returns to validity as it was, and it is divided among them. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'so for the owner of the good, two-thirds of it, and for the owner of the poor, two-thirds of it, and for the owner of the medium, one-third of each.' That is: the owner of the good gets two-thirds of the good garment; the owner of the poor gets two-thirds of the poor garment; the owner of the medium gets one-third of each. So each of them ends up with two-thirds of a garment, because when two are divided among three owners, each gets two-thirds. And he gave the owner of the medium one-third of each of them and the others two-thirds of one garment because the owner of the good has no right to the poor for certain, since his right is either in the poor or the medium; and he has no right in both [i.e., he cannot claim both]. It is possible that his right is in the poor if the lost garment is the good or medium; it is possible that he has a right in it (the good) if the lost garment is the best; it is possible that he has a right in the poor if the lost garment is the worst; and it is possible that he has a right in both if the lost garment is the medium. So if that is the case, each is given his right from a place that is possibly his, because equalizing by invalidating the right of each would be unfair since they are equal in the probability of their right remaining or being nullified. In what we have said, each receives his right as much as possible, achieving the testator's purpose of preference, so it is determined. In al-'Uyun: If a man bequeaths good garments, he gets what he wears of cloaks and shirts; the lost is...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof that explains the distribution of three bequeathed garments (good, medium, poor) to three different recipients when one garment is lost and the heir denies knowledge. The ruling: if the heir simply says 'your right has perished' to each, the bequest is invalid due to uncertainty. The commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) critiques the author's phrasing, saying it implies a false statement (the heir claiming each person's garment is lost when only one is lost). He provides a better interpretation from al-Jami' al-Saghir: the heir says 'the right of one of you is void, we don't know whose'. However, if the heirs hand over the remaining two garments, the bequest becomes valid again, and the distribution is as follows: the recipient of the good garment gets two-thirds of the good garment; the recipient of the poor gets two-thirds of the poor garment; the recipient of the medium gets one-third of each of the two remaining garments. The reasoning: each person's entitlement is probable given the unknown lost garment. The medium-recipient could have a claim to both remaining garments, so he gets a share of each, while the others get most of their specific garment. The passage ends with a quote from al-'Uyun about bequest of good garments.

Key Terms
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the specific legatee or subject matter of the bequest, leading to invalidity.
جيد (jayyid): The good or high-quality garment in the bequest.
وسط (wasat): The medium-quality garment.
رديء (radi'): The poor or low-quality garment.
جحود (juhud): The heir's denial or refusal to acknowledge the bequest, specifically by claiming ignorance of which garment is lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of three different garments bequeathed to three persons, with one lost and the heir handing over the remaining two, how much does the recipient of the medium garment receive?
A) Two-thirds of the medium garment.
B) The entire medium garment.
C) One-third of both remaining garments.
D) Nothing because the bequest is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest depends on certainty of the beneficiary and subject-matter; when uncertainty arises after the testator's death, it can be resolved by the heirs surrendering the remaining property, and distribution is based on a probabilistic method that respects the testator's intent.

When a Bequest of Multiple Items Becomes Unknown: The Ruling of Lost Garments
Ruling with proof on distribution when one of three bequests is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when one of several bequeathed items of different quality is lost and the heir denies, and apply the distribution method if the heirs surrender the remaining items.

Core Idea
Ignorance of which specific item is lost voids the bequest, but surrender of the remainder revives it with a pro-rata distribution respecting the testator's preference.

This passage explores a nuanced scenario in Hanafi inheritance law: a testator bequeaths three garments of distinct quality (good, medium, poor) to three named legatees. One garment is lost, and the identity of the lost garment is unknown. The heir denies responsibility by claiming uncertainty. The ruling hinges on the principle that ignorance of entitlement prevents enforcement. However, if the heir voluntarily surrenders the two remaining garments, the bequest revives with a specific distribution that balances each legatee's potential claim. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, critiques the precise wording of the heir's denial, preferring the more accurate formulation from earlier Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
Identify the three garments of different quality, each bequeathed to a specific legatee. One garment is lost, and it is unknown which one.
2
Apply the rule when heir denies
When the heir says he doesn't know whose right is lost and refuses to deliver, the bequest becomes void due to ignorance of entitlement.
This is based on the principle that uncertainty in entitlement prevents enforcement.
3
Recognize the exception
If the heirs voluntarily surrender the two remaining garments, the bequest becomes valid again because the impediment (ignorance) is removed.
The bequest was originally valid; the void is due to a supervening impediment.
4
Analyze the distribution method
The legatee of the good gets 2/3 of the good garment; the legatee of the poor gets 2/3 of the poor; the legatee of the medium gets 1/3 of each remaining garment. Understand why this is equitable.
Each legatee receives from the garment(s) that could possibly be theirs, maximizing rights while honoring the testator's preference.
5
Reflect on the rationale
This distribution maximizes each legatee's right given the possibilities, and fulfills the testator's intent of preference.
The method is based on ihtimal (probability) and istihsan (equity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلذي الجيد ثلثاه ولذى الرديء ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل وببيت عين من دار واحد منهم بثوب فضاع منها ثوب ولا يدرى أيهم والوارث يجحد ذلك بأن يقول لكل واحد هلك حقك أو حق أحدكم ولا يدري من هو الهالك فلا أدفع إليكم شيئاً بطلت الوصية لأن المستحق مجهول وجهالته تمنع صحة القضاء وتحصيل غرض الموصي فيبطل كما إذا أوصى لأحد الرجلين وقول المؤلف والوارث يقول إلى آخره ومعنى جحودهم أن يقول حقك قد هلك أقول : في ظاهر تعبير المؤلف ههنا منهم هو الوارث لكل واحد منهما الثوب الذي فساد لأن هلاك كل واحد منهم إنما يتصور فيما إذا ضاعت الأثواب الثلاثة معاً والغرض في المسألة أن ضياع ثوب واحد منه غير معلوم بخصوصه فكيف يصح أن يقول الوارث لكل واحد منهم الثوب الذي هو حقك قد هلك فإنه كذب ظاهر لا ينبغي أن أن يترتب عليه حكم شرعي بل قوله لواحد منهم الثوب الذي هو حقك قد هلك عن وضع فضلاً يسمع أصلا يقتضي الاعتراف بكون الثوبين الباقيين لصاحبه والأولى في التعبير ما ذكر في الجامع الصغير سيما للصدر الشهيد والإمام قاضيخان وهو أن المراد بجحود الوارث أن يقول حق واحد منكم بطل ولا ندري من بطل حقه ومن بقي حقه فلا نسلم إليكم شيئاً، والذي يمكن في توجيه كلام المصنف أن يكون مراده معنى جحوده أن يقول الوارث لكل واحد بعينه الثوب الذي قد هلك يحتمل أن يكون حقك فكأنه سامح في العبارة بناء على ظهور والمراد، ووافقه صاحب الكافي في هذه العبارة مع ظهور كمالها قال رحمه الله: (إلا أن يسلموا ما بقي) أي إلا أن يسلم الورثة ما بقي من الثياب فحينئذ تصح الوصية لأنها كانت صحيحة في الأصل، وإنما بطلت بجهالة طارئة مانعة من التسليم فإذا سلموا الباقي زال المانع فعادت صحيحة كما كانت فتقسم بينهم قال رحمه الله : فلذي الجيد ثلثاه ولذى الرديء ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل أي لصاحب الجيد ثلثا الثوب الجيد ولصاحب الرديء يعطى ثلثا الثوب الرديء ولصاحب الوسط ثلث كل واحد منهما فيصيب كل واحد منهم ثلثا ثوب لأن الاثنين إذا قسما على ثلاثة أصحاب كل واحد منهما الثلثان، وإنما أعطى لصاحب الوسط ثلث كل واحد منهما وللآخرين الثلثين من ثوب واحد لأن صاحب الجيد لا حق له الرديء بيقين لأنه إنما يكون هو الرديء أو الوسط ولا حق له فيهما، واحتمل أن يكون حقه في الرديء بأن كان الهالك هو الجيد أو الوسط واحتمل أن يكون له فيه حق بأن يكون الهالك أجود، ويحتمل أن يكون في الرديء بأن يكون الهالك أردأ ويحتمل أن يكون له فيهما حق بأن كان الوسط، فإذا كان كذلك أعطى كل واحد منهم حقه من محل يحتمل أن يكون هو له لأن التسوية بإبطال حق كل واحد منهم إليه وهم في احتمال بقاء حقه وبطلانه سواء، وفيما قلنا إيصال حق كل واحد منهم بقدر الإمكان وتحصيل غرض الموصي من التفضيل فكان متعيناً.
For the owner of the good quality, two-thirds; for the owner of the poor quality, two-thirds; for the owner of the medium quality, one-third of each. And concerning a specific house from one of them with a garment, and a garment was lost and it is not known which one, and the heir denies that by saying to each one: 'Your right has perished' or 'the right of one of you has perished and I do not know who is the one whose right has perished, so I will not give you anything', the bequest becomes void because the entitled person is unknown, and ignorance of him prevents sound judgment and fulfilling the testator's purpose, so it becomes void just as if he bequeathed to one of two men. The author's statement 'and the heir says' etc. and the meaning of their denial is that he says: 'Your right has perished.' I say: In the apparent expression of the author here, he is the heir for each one of them the garment which is corrupt because the perishing of each one of them is only conceivable when three garments are lost together, but the point of the issue is that the loss of one garment among them is not known specifically, so how can it be valid for the heir to say to each one of them: 'The garment that is your right has perished'? For that is an obvious lie, and a legal ruling should not be based on it. Rather, his statement to one of them 'the garment that is your right has perished' from a position of [؟] even [؟] is heard at all? It implies acknowledgment that the two remaining garments belong to its owner. The better expression is what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, especially by al-Sadr al-Shahid and Imam Qadi Khan: that what is meant by the heir's denial is that he says: 'The right of one of you has become void, and we do not know whose right has become void and whose right remains, so we will not give you anything.' And what is possible in interpreting the author's words is that his intended meaning is that the heir says to each specific one: 'The garment that has perished could be your right' — as if he was lenient in expression based on the obvious meaning. And the author of al-Kafi agreed with him in this expression despite its apparent completeness. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (Except if they surrender what remains) i.e., except if the heirs surrender the remaining garments, then at that time the bequest is valid because it was valid originally, and it was only void due to a supervening ignorance preventing delivery. So if they surrender the remainder, the impediment is removed and it returns to being valid as before, so it is divided among them. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: For the owner of the good quality, two-thirds; for the owner of the poor quality, two-thirds; for the owner of the medium, one-third of each. That is, for the owner of the good, two-thirds of the good garment; for the owner of the poor, he is given two-thirds of the poor garment; for the owner of the medium, one-third of each of them, so each of them gets two-thirds of a garment because the two garments when divided among three owners, each gets two-thirds. And he gave the owner of the medium one-third of each of them, and the others two-thirds of one garment, because the owner of the good has no right in the poor garment definitively, because his entitlement is either the good or the medium, and he has no right in both. And it is possible that his right is in the poor if the lost one is the good or the medium; and it is possible that he has a right in it if the lost one is the finest; and it is possible that he has a right in the poor if the lost one is the poorest; and it is possible that he has a right in both if the lost one is the medium. Since this is the case, each of them is given his right from a place that could be his, because equalizing would cancel the right of each one of them to it, and they are equal in the possibility of their right remaining or being void. In what we have said, there is delivery of the right of each one as much as possible and fulfillment of the testator's purpose of preferring, so it is determined.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the distribution of bequeathed items when one is lost and the heir denies knowledge. It begins by presenting the core ruling: if a testator bequeaths three garments of different quality (good, medium, poor) to three specific legatees, but one garment is lost and the identity of the lost garment is unknown, the bequest becomes void if the heir denies responsibility. The reason is that the entitlement becomes unknown, and ignorance prevents enforcement. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining two garments, the bequest revives and the two garments are divided among the three legatees according to a specific method: the owner of the good garment gets two-thirds of the good garment, the owner of the poor gets two-thirds of the poor garment, and the owner of the medium gets one-third of each garment. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, critiques the author's (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) phrasing of the heir's denial, preferring the formulation from al-Jami' al-Saghir and Qadi Khan: the heir says 'the right of one of you is void, and we do not know whose' rather than falsely claiming each legatee's specific garment is lost. The commentary then explains the rationale for the unequal distribution: the owner of the medium has a potential claim in both garments (since the lost one could be the good or the poor, leaving the medium's garment either in the lost or remaining category), while the owners of good and poor each have a likely claim in only one garment. This distribution maximizes each legatee's right and fulfills the testator's intent of preference. The ruling is based on legal reasoning (istiḥsān) to achieve justice and the testator's purpose.

Key Terms
جحود الوارث (juhūd al-wārith): The heir's denial or refusal to acknowledge the legatees' claims due to uncertainty about which item is lost.
الثلثان (al-thuluthān): Two-thirds, the share given to the owner of the good or poor quality garment from their respective garment.
غرض الموصي (gharaḍ al-mūṣī): The testator's purpose or intention behind the bequest (here, preference among legatees).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of three garments bequeathed to three legatees (good, medium, poor) with one lost, what is the share of the legatee of the medium garment?
A) Two-thirds of the medium garment
B) One-third of the good and one-third of the poor
C) One-third of the remaining garments
D) The entire medium garment if found

Key Takeaway
When one of multiple bequeathed items of different quality is lost and the heir denies knowledge, the bequest is void unless the heirs surrender the remainder, in which case a proportional distribution respecting the testator's preference applies.

Defining Garments (Thiyāb) in Bequests
Definition ruling: clarifies scope of 'thiyab' in a bequest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which items are included in a bequest of 'fine garments' according to Hanafi fiqh and apply the customary definition of thiyab.

Core Idea
A bequest of 'clothes' includes only body-covering garments, not headwear or footwear—custom defines the shar'i meaning.

When someone bequeaths 'fine garments', ambiguity can lead to disputes. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi definition, based on customary usage (urf), and lists included and excluded items as recorded in al-'Uyun and al-Khaniyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Understand that the bequest of 'thiyab' is ambiguous and requires definition. The Hanafi school relies on custom to resolve this.
Custom (urf) is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh for determining meanings.
2
List the included items
From the source: cloaks (jibab), shirts (qumus), robes (ardiyah), tailasans (taylasan), trousers (sarawilat), and blankets (aksiyah) are included.
These are garments covering the torso and lower body.
3
List the excluded items
Bonnets (qalanis), khuffs (leather socks), and stockings (jawarib) are excluded because they are headwear or footwear.
The source explicitly states these are not considered thiyab.
4
Understand the basis
The definition is based on customary understanding of what constitutes 'garments' in the Arabic language and social context.
Hanafi fiqh gives weight to 'urf in such interpretations.
5
Note the authority
The ruling is cited from al-'Uyun and confirmed by al-Khaniyya, both authoritative Hanafi works.
These are later compilations; their rulings are based on earlier Hanafi principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي العيون: إذا أوصى لرجل بثياب جيدة فله ما يلبس من الجباب والقمص والأردية والطيلسان والسراويلات والأكسية ولا يكون له شيء من القلانس والخفاف والجوارب. وفي الخانية : فإن ذلك ليس من الثياب.
And in al-‘Uyun: If a man bequeaths to another fine garments, then what he wears includes cloaks, shirts, robes, tailasans (long scarves), trousers, and blankets. And he does not get any of the bonnets, khuffs (socks), and stockings. And in al-Khaniyya: That is not part of garments.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling from the work al-‘Uyun, clarifying what items are included in a bequest of 'fine garments' (ثياب جيدة). The ruling specifies that the legatee is entitled to items that are commonly worn as outer or inner garments such as cloaks (جباب), shirts (قمص), robes (أردية), tailasans (طيلسان), trousers (سراويلات), and blankets (أكسية). Items like bonnets (قلانس), khuffs (خفاف – leather socks), and stockings (جوارب) are excluded. The citation from al-Khaniyya reinforces that these are not considered garments for the purpose of a bequest. This ruling helps avoid disputes over ambiguous wording in wills.

Key Terms
ثياب (thiyāb): Garments; in this context, limited to outerwear and body-covering clothes, excluding headwear and footwear.
قلانس (qalānis): Bonnet or cap; not included in a bequest of garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-‘Uyun, which of the following is NOT included in a bequest of 'fine garments'?
A) Cloak (جبة)
B) Shirt (قميص)
C) Turban (عمامة)
D) Blanket (كساء)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a bequest of 'garments' is limited to body-covering clothes as per custom, excluding headwear and footwear.

Defining 'Matā'' (Belongings) in Hanafi Bequests
Defines the scope of 'matā'' in bequests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which items are included in a bequest of 'matā'' according to Hanafi rulings and identify the basis for inclusion using custom (urf).

Core Idea
Custom (urf) defines 'matā''—items that protect the body or are worn/spread are included; curtains are disputed.

In Hanafi inheritance, the term 'matā'' (belongings) appears in wills, but its scope depends on custom. This lesson draws from Fatawa Ahl Samarqand and al-Siyar to clarify what items are covered, helping you interpret ambiguous bequests accurately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term
Locate the term 'متاع' (matā') in the passage and note that it is being defined in the context of a bequest (وصية).
The term appears in the phrase 'إذا أوصى بمتاع بدنه'.
2
Extract the inclusion criteria
From Fatawa Ahl Samarqand, identify the criterion: items that protect the body from heat, cold, and harm. From al-Siyar, the criterion is items that people wear and spread.
Both criteria rely on custom (urf).
3
List explicitly included items
Write down the items mentioned: bonnet (قلنسوة), khuff (خف), quilt (لحاف), wrap (دثار), mattress (فراش), garments (ثياب), shirts (قمص).
These are examples, not an exhaustive list.
4
Identify the disputed item
Note the curtain (ستر) is disputed; Muhammad indicated inclusion, but other scholars differed.
The passage leaves the ruling unresolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى أهل سمرقند : إذا أوصى بمتاع بدنه يدخل تحت الوصية القلنسوة والخف واللحاف والدثار والفراش لأنه يصون بهذه الأشياء بدنه عن الحر والبرد والأذى. وفي السير : إن اسم المتاع في العادة يقع على ما يلبسه الناس ويبسط وعلى هذا يدخل في الوصية بالمتاع الثياب والفراش والقمص. والستر هل يدخل فيها أولاً؟ فقد اختلف المشايخ أشار محمد في السير إلى أنه يدخل.
And in the Fatawa of the people of Samarqand: If someone bequeaths the belongings of his body, then under the bequest are included the bonnet, khuff (sock), quilt, wrap, and mattress, because with these things he protects his body from heat, cold, and harm. And in al-Siyar: The term 'belongings' (متاع) customarily applies to what people wear and spread. On this basis, under a bequest of belongings are included garments, mattresses, and shirts. As for the curtain (ستر), does it enter or not? The scholars differed; Muhammad indicated in al-Siyar that it does enter.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling from Fatawa Ahl Samarqand and al-Siyar, clarifying the scope of a bequest of 'متاع' (belongings or goods). According to the Samarqand scholars, items that protect the body from elements—like bonnets, khuffs, quilts, wraps, and mattresses—are included. Al-Siyar states that customarily 'متاع' includes what people wear and spread, so garments, mattresses, and shirts are included. There is a difference of opinion about curtains (ستر); Imam Muhammad indicated inclusion, but the passage leaves it as disputed. This ruling helps resolve ambiguity in wills using the term 'متاع'.

Key Terms
متاع (matā'): Belongings or goods; in this context, items used for bodily protection and household spread, including clothing and bedding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fatawa Ahl Samarqand, which item is included in a bequest of 'متاع بدنه' (belongings of the body)?
A) Sword
B) Quilt (لحاف)
C) Horse
D) Currency

Key Takeaway
A bequest of 'متاع' includes items customarily worn or used for bodily protection and spreading, as per Hanafi reliance on urf.

Definition of 'Weapons' in a Bequest of a Horse
Clarifies the term 'weapons' in a horse bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of silāḥ in a horse bequest and apply it to identify which items are included.

Core Idea
In a horse bequest, 'weapons' means the rider's arms, not the horse's gear.

This lesson clarifies a common ambiguity in bequests: when a testator leaves 'a horse with its weapons,' what exactly does 'weapons' refer to? Abu Yusuf's inquiry and Al-Baqqali's list provide a precise Hanafi definition, ensuring the bequest is correctly fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Recognize that the passage deals with a bequest (wasiyyah) of a horse with a qualifying phrase 'bi-silahi'. The ambiguity lies in the reference of 'silah'.
The bequest is voluntary, not obligatory; the definition determines what property transfers.
2
Understand the ambiguity: rider's vs. horse's gear
Abu Yusuf explicitly asks whether 'silah' means the rider's weapons or the horse's equipment (like armor, saddle). This is a linguistic and customary interpretation issue.
In Arabic, 'silah' can be ambiguous without context.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's ruling
Abu Yusuf rules that 'silah' refers to the man's (rider's) weapons. This becomes the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
This follows the principle that default interpretation follows common usage.
4
Examine Al-Baqqali's minimum list
Al-Baqqali specifies the minimum components: a sword, shield, spear, and 'qirs'. These are the essential fighting weapons.
The term 'qirs' may be a weapon or equipment; it is included as part of the minimum.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a bequest of 'a horse with its weapons', include the rider's sword, shield, spear, etc., but exclude the saddle, bridle, or horse armor.
If the testator intended otherwise, it would need explicit wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوصى لرجل بفرس بسلاحه سأل أبو يوسف أهو على سلاح الرجل أو على سلاح الفرس ؟ قال : على سلاح الرجل. قال البقالي في فتاويه : وأدنى ما يكون من السلاح سيف وترس ورمح وقرص ولو أوصى له بذهب أو فضة وللموصي سيف محلى بذهب أو فضة كانت الحلية له وبعد هذا ينظر : إن لم يكن في نزع الحلية ضرر فاحش ينزع الحلية من السيف وتعطى للموصى له وإن كان في نزعها ضرر فاحش ينظر إلى قيمة الحلية وإلى قيمة السيف فإن كانت قيمة السيف أكثر تخير الورثة إن شاؤوا أعطوا الموصى له قيمة الحلية مصوغا من خلاف جنسها وصار السيف مع الحلية لهم، وإن كانت قيمة الحلية أكثر يخير الموصى له إن شاء أعطى وأخذ السيف وإن شاء أخذ القيمة، وإن كانت قيمتها على السواء كان الخيار للورثة.
And if someone bequeaths to a man a horse with its weapons, Abu Yusuf asked: Is it considered the man's weapons or the horse's weapons? He said: The man's weapons. Al-Baqqali said in his Fatawa: The minimum of weapons is a sword, shield, spear, and qirs. And if someone bequeaths to him gold or silver, and the testator has a sword decorated with gold or silver, the ornamentation belongs to him (the legatee). After this, it is considered: If there is no significant harm in removing the ornamentation, it is removed from the sword and given to the legatee. And if there is significant harm in removing it, then one looks at the value of the ornamentation and the value of the sword. If the value of the sword is greater, the heirs have the choice: if they wish, they give the legatee the worth of the ornamentation as crafted from a different type, and the sword with its ornamentation becomes theirs. If the value of the ornamentation is greater, the legatee has the choice: if he wishes, he pays and takes the sword; if he wishes, he takes the value. And if their values are equal, the choice belongs to the heirs.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First, concerning a bequest of 'a horse with its weapons' (فرس بسلاحه): Abu Yusuf clarifies that the phrase refers to the rider's weapons (like sword, shield, spear), not the horse's gear (like saddle, bridle). Al-Baqqali lists the minimum components of 'سلاح' as sword, shield, spear, and 'قرص' (possibly a sort of weapon). Second, when a bequest of gold or silver is made and the testator owns a sword decorated with gold or silver, the legatee is entitled to the ornamentation, but the method of delivery depends on harm. If removal causes no significant harm, the ornamentation is detached and given. If removal would harm the sword, then a valuation is made: if the sword is worth more, the heirs can choose to pay the legatee the value of the ornamentation in a different form; if the ornamentation is worth more, the legatee can choose to pay for the sword and take it; if equal, the heirs choose. This ruling ensures the bequest is fulfilled without causing disproportionate damage.

Key Terms
سلاح (silāḥ): Weapons; in this context, the rider's arms: sword, shield, spear, qirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a bequest of 'a horse with its weapons', what does 'weapons' refer to according to Abu Yusuf?
A) The horse's armor and gear
B) The rider's weapons
C) Both rider's and horse's weapons
D) Only specialized weapons

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets 'weapons' in a horse bequest as the rider's fighting equipment, following Abu Yusuf's clarification.

Bequest of Gold/Silver from a Decorated Sword
Establishes the method for delivering bequest of metal from a decorated sword

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on fulfilling a bequest of gold or silver from a decorated sword, including the choice based on harm and comparative value.

Core Idea
When a bequest includes gold/silver from a sword, removal depends on harm; if harmful, values determine who chooses.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a testator bequeaths gold or silver but owns a sword decorated with that metal. The Hanafi ruling provides a detailed method to deliver the bequest without causing disproportionate damage to the sword, balancing the rights of the legatee and the heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest and the asset
The testator bequeaths gold or silver (e.g., 'I give you gold/silver of such amount'), but the testator's estate includes a sword decorated with gold or silver.
The bequest is specific: the metal itself, not the sword.
2
Determine ownership of the ornamentation
The ornamentation (ḥilya) on the sword belongs to the legatee by virtue of the bequest.
But the sword itself may be separate property.
3
Assess harm in removal
Examine whether removing the ornamentation would cause 'significant harm' (ḍarar fāḥish) to the sword. If no harm, simply remove and give.
Harm is judged by the damage to the sword's value or structural integrity.
4
If harm exists, compare values
When removal causes significant harm, compare the value of the ornamentation to the value of the sword (without ornamentation).
This determines which party has the right to choose the method.
5
Apply the choices based on which is more valuable
If the sword is worth more, the heirs choose: give the legatee the value of the ornamentation in a different form (crafted from a different metal) and keep the sword. If the ornamentation is worth more, the legatee chooses: pay the value of the sword and take it, or take the value of the ornamentation. If equal, the heirs choose.
This ensures no party suffers a major loss.

وإذا أوصى لرجل بفرس بسلاحه سأل أبو يوسف أهو على سلاح الرجل أو على سلاح الفرس ؟ قال : على سلاح الرجل. قال البقالي في فتاويه : وأدنى ما يكون من السلاح سيف وترس ورمح وقرص ولو أوصى له بذهب أو فضة وللموصي سيف محلى بذهب أو فضة كانت الحلية له وبعد هذا ينظر : إن لم يكن في نزع الحلية ضرر فاحش ينزع الحلية من السيف وتعطى للموصى له وإن كان في نزعها ضرر فاحش ينظر إلى قيمة الحلية وإلى قيمة السيف فإن كانت قيمة السيف أكثر تخير الورثة إن شاؤوا أعطوا الموصى له قيمة الحلية مصوغا من خلاف جنسها وصار السيف مع الحلية لهم، وإن كانت قيمة الحلية أكثر يخير الموصى له إن شاء أعطى وأخذ السيف وإن شاء أخذ القيمة، وإن كانت قيمتها على السواء كان الخيار للورثة.
And if someone bequeaths to a man a horse with its weapons, Abu Yusuf asked: Is it considered the man's weapons or the horse's weapons? He said: The man's weapons. Al-Baqqali said in his Fatawa: The minimum of weapons is a sword, shield, spear, and qirs. And if someone bequeaths to him gold or silver, and the testator has a sword decorated with gold or silver, the ornamentation belongs to him (the legatee). After this, it is considered: If there is no significant harm in removing the ornamentation, it is removed from the sword and given to the legatee. And if there is significant harm in removing it, then one looks at the value of the ornamentation and the value of the sword. If the value of the sword is greater, the heirs have the choice: if they wish, they give the legatee the worth of the ornamentation as crafted from a different type, and the sword with its ornamentation becomes theirs. If the value of the ornamentation is greater, the legatee has the choice: if he wishes, he pays and takes the sword; if he wishes, he takes the value. And if their values are equal, the choice belongs to the heirs.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First, concerning a bequest of 'a horse with its weapons' (فرس بسلاحه): Abu Yusuf clarifies that the phrase refers to the rider's weapons (like sword, shield, spear), not the horse's gear (like saddle, bridle). Al-Baqqali lists the minimum components of 'سلاح' as sword, shield, spear, and 'قرص' (possibly a sort of weapon). Second, when a bequest of gold or silver is made and the testator owns a sword decorated with gold or silver, the legatee is entitled to the ornamentation, but the method of delivery depends on harm. If removal causes no significant harm, the ornamentation is detached and given. If removal would harm the sword, then a valuation is made: if the sword is worth more, the heirs can choose to pay the legatee the value of the ornamentation in a different form; if the ornamentation is worth more, the legatee can choose to pay for the sword and take it; if equal, the heirs choose. This ruling ensures the bequest is fulfilled without causing disproportionate damage.

Key Terms
حلية (ḥilya): Ornamentation; decorative metal (gold/silver) on the sword.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ruling on bequest of gold/silver from a decorated sword, who has the choice when the sword is more valuable than the ornamentation?
A) The legatee
B) The heirs
C) The testator's executor
D) Both parties must agree

Key Takeaway
When a bequest of gold/silver cannot be literally fulfilled without harming a valuable asset, the Hanafi school provides a choice-based solution to prevent loss.
